O'Daniel v. Sapp


NO. 2012-CA-001961-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 105



June 13, 2014, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Sub nomine at Martin v. O'Daniel, 2015 Ky. LEXIS 1607 (Ky., Apr. 2, 2015)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Martin v. O'Daniel, 2016 Ky. LEXIS 423 (Ky., Sept. 22, 2016)
Review denied by Martin v. O'Daniel, 2017 Ky. LEXIS 65 (Ky., Feb. 16, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SHEILA R. ISAAC, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-CI-00820.
Martin v. O'Daniel, 2011 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 429 (Ky. Ct. App., May 20, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred by granting the three police officers summary judgment in the car buyer's malicious prosecution claim because the court had previously determined that the officers were not entitled to immunity and the trial court erred in holding that that previous decision was impacted by the recent decision of Rehberg v. Paulk; [2]-The trial court erred by granting the officers summary judgment after finding that the car buyer failed to prove the institution or continuation of judicial proceedings by the officers even though a prosecutor obtained an indictment from a grand jury because a malicious prosecution action could be maintained sub judice.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded.

Rosen v. Hall


NO. 2014-CA-000448-EL


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 146



June 4, 2014, Entered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Davis v. Wingate, 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 147 (Ky. Ct. App., June 10, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: MOTION TO SET ASIDE PURSUANT TO KRS 118.176(4) [*1] . ACTION NO. 14-CI-00081.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in declaring that a candidate was not a bona fide candidate without considering the constitutionality of House Bill 427 (2013) because the candidate did not anticipate a ruling on his bona fides without an opportunity to amend his response, the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over the matter, and the constitutional issue was sufficiently raised that the trial court could not simply ignore it prior to its ruling on the candidate's bona fides; [2]-The trial court erred in requiring notification to the Attorney General pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.075 because no appellant's brief was filed in the expedited proceeding, the Attorney General did not have a vested institutional interest in the bona fides challenge under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 118.176(2), was not subject to the injunction issued, and was not an indispensable party.


OUTCOME: Motion granted.

 

403 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Regents of Ky. Cmty. & Tech. College Sys. v. Farrell


NO. 2012-CA-001367-MR AND NO. 2012-CA-001480-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


443 S.W.3d 12; 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 111



May 30, 2014, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PHILLIP J. SHEPHERD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 10-CI-01677. APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PHILLIP J. SHEPHERD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 10-CI-01677.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The circuit court erred in granting summary judgment in favor certain teachers in relation to furloughs authorized by House Bill 1 because their due process and equal protection rights under Ky. Const. § 2 were not violated where their property rights did not entitle them to anything beyond the written notice specified in 101 Ky. Admin. Regs. 5:015E § 2(5)(b), the teachers were executive branch employees and local school district teachers were not; [2]-The circuit court properly determined that the furloughs violated Ky. Const. § 183 because there was no legitimate state purpose for furloughing the teachers who were executive branch employees on a holiday while protecting all other elementary and secondary teachers from the furloughs.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

404 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Wood v. Commonwealth


NO. 2013-CA-000369-MR & NO. 2013-CA-000460-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


432 S.W.3d 726; 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 78



May 16, 2014, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE OLU A. STEVENS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 11-CR-003634.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-While the allotment of peremptory strikes at defendant's trial under Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.40 was not constitutionally defective and the trial judge's failure, sua sponte, to include a "no adverse inference" instruction in the penalty phase instructions was not defective where it was not requested in accordance with Ky. R. Crim. P. 9.54(3), the trial court's reckless homicide charge was inflammatory and defendant should have been allowed, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055(2)(b), to explain the attendant circumstances to the jury where the circumstances were in the record and the testifying witness used the plea sheets, which included the details of the crime.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.

OUTCOME: Orders affirmed.

Carroll v. N.E. Reed


NO. 2011-CA-002151-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


425 S.W.3d 921; 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 47



March 14, 2014, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM EDMONSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE RONNIE C. DORTCH, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 11-CI-00023.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A fiscal court was properly granted summary judgment in a county court clerk's action for declaratory and injunctive relief because the ordinance in question did not implicate powers not already afforded to the fiscal court by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 64, was not inconsistent with the requirements set forth in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 64.152 that required the clerk to account for expenses and to relinquish excess income, and merely allowed the fiscal court to exercise a degree of financial control throughout the year.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Rider v. Commonwealth


NO. 2013-CA-000136-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


460 S.W.3d 909; 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 196



January 17, 2014, Rendered


NOTICE: TO BE PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, May 6, 2015. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered to be Published.
Review denied by Rider v. Commonwealth, 2015 Ky. LEXIS 1735 (Ky., May 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM KNOX CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS L. JENSEN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 09-CR-00008.
Rider v. Commonwealth, 2014 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 45 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 17, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a movant was entitled to amend his sentence when the movant contended that the Kentucky Legislature's amendment of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.043(5), after a prior version of that subsection was declared an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers doctrine, constituted a change in circumstances warranting the amendment of his sentence. HOLDINGS: [1]-The amended version of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.043(5), which pertained to conditional discharge, was not an ex post facto law and its application did not warrant amendment of the movant's sentence.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Maclean v. Middleton


NO. 2011-CA-000267-MR & NO. 2011-CA-000268-MR & NO. 2011-CA-001076-MR & NO. 2011-CA-001160-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


419 S.W.3d 755; 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 3



January 3, 2014, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified January 10, 2014
Related proceeding at Middleton v. PNC Bank, NA, 2014 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 846 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 31, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEALS AND CROSS-APPEALS FROM JEFFERSON FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE JERRY J. BOWLES, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CI-502718.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Distributions to the husband under trusts created by his great-grandfather were exempt from characterization as marital property under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.190(2)(a); the husband's expenditure of marital funds for litigation involving the trusts did not change the source of the distributions from the trusts; [2]-The trial court did not err under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.200(1) in awarding the wife $2,500 per month in maintenance for 12 months because she lacked sufficient financial resources to provide for her reasonable needs was presently unable to support herself through appropriate employment; [3]-In calculating the husband's child support obligation, the trial court did not err under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.212(2)(d) in imputing an income of $2,100 per month to the wife; the findings regarding her earning capacity were supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

409 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Fairhurst v. Moon


NO. 2013-CA-000061-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


416 S.W.3d 788; 2013 Ky. App. LEXIS 167



November 27, 2013, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM MCCRACKEN FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE CYNTHIA E. SANDERSON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 12-CI-00533.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The starting point for a trial court's analysis under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021(1) was the constitutional presumption that a fit parent acted in the child's best interest; [2]-A trial court erred by finding that a father was unable to object to the entry of a grandparent visitation order merely because he had not entirely denied visitation; rather, the trial court had to presume that the parents had a right to impose any limitation on a grandparent's visitation with the children; [3]-The grandparent had the burden of proving that the court-ordered visitation would be in the best interest of the children; [4]-The trial court could not make the determinations required by Walker v. Blair until after all parties had a reasonable opportunity to present proof.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

Short v. City of Olive Hill


NO. 2012-CA-000873-MR AND NO. 2012-CA-000939-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


414 S.W.3d 433; 2013 Ky. App. LEXIS 115



July 26, 2013, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM CARTER CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE REBECCA K. PHILLIPS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-CI-00220.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because Olive Hill, Ky., Nuisance Ord. § 1.2(7)(a)-(c) listed several weeds and provided specific factors for identifying a weed, the ordinance was not arbitrary or unconstitutionally vague as applied to property owners fined for failing to cut weeds; [2]-Due process was satisfied because notice and a citation were issued, one of the owners participated in the hearing, and the order was furnished to the owners; [3]-Whether or not an owner was present at the time of the oral pronouncement, the board was required under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 65.8828(5) to send the order via certified mail because the owners were not present when the written order was entered; [4]-Although service by regular mail was improper, the order had to be upheld because the owners did not timely appeal to the district court under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 65.8831(1), (2) after receiving the written order.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

 

413 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. Commonwealth


NO. 2011-CA-001951-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


403 S.W.3d 69; 2013 Ky. App. LEXIS 88



June 14, 2013, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS D. WINGATE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 10-CI-01452.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Kentucky Department of Housing, Buildings and Construction's (DHBC) internal policy was null and void, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13A.130(2), because the DHBC's internal policy was to effectively presume that no one applying for a master plumber's license had any kind of criminal conviction, and the DHBC ignored Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 335B.020(3)'s requirement that the DHBC first make a determination that the convicted felon had been successfully rehabilitated; [2]-The DHBC was required to determine that the applicant had been successfully rehabilitated before a license could have been issued to the applicant because the applicant was convicted of three crimes; [3]-Without making that prior determination, the DHBC lacked authority to issue the applicant a license; [4]-The applicant's master plumber's license was void.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

 

414 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Virgil v. Commonwealth


NO. 2011-CA-001673-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


403 S.W.3d 577; 2013 Ky. App. LEXIS 76



May 17, 2013, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE FRED A. STINE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 87-CR-00199.
Virgil v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 562 (Ky. Ct. App., Nov. 5, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court reconsidered its order granting petitioner inmate's request for post-conviction DNA testing because the statute in effect at the time of the request restricted such testing to death penalty cases. The appellate court held this was error because it was appropriate to apply a recent amendment to the DNA testing statute, found in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 422.285(5) (2013), allowing post-conviction DNA testing to cases which included the inmate's case, retroactively to the inmate's case, since the amendment reflected a strong public policy of the Commonwealth of Kentucky.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Sanitation Dist. No. 1 v. McCord


NO. 2011-CA-000819-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2013 Ky. App. LEXIS 15



January 25, 2013, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM KENTON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PATRICIA M. SUMME, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 10-CI-02847.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Sovereign immunity barred a negligence claim against a sanitation district arising from sewage overflows because the district provided integral state functions as set forth in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 220.110(1), 220.030, 220.310, 220.320 while acting under its parent counties' control pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 220.035, 220.140, 220.170. The property owners could maintain claims of inverse condemnation, as to which sovereign immunity was no bar, and claims of nuisance and trespass seeking to recover for an unconstitutional taking of private property without just compensation.


OUTCOME: Reversed in part and remanded.

Norton v. Perry


NO. 2009-CA-002343-MR AND NO. 2009-CA-002394-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2013 Ky. App. LEXIS 10



January 11, 2013, Rendered 
January 11, 2013, Entered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Opinion of October 12, 2012, Withdrawn.
Review denied and ordered not published by Zeoli v. Norton, 2013 Ky. LEXIS 667 (Ky., Dec. 11, 2013)
Review denied and ordered not published by Perry v. Zeoli, 2013 Ky. LEXIS 660 (Ky., Dec. 11, 2013)
Remanded by, Costs and fees proceeding at, Motion granted by Norton v. Perry, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 66 (E.D. Ky., Jan. 3, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JAMES D. ISHMAEL, JR., JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-CI-06061.
Norton v. Perry, 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 208 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 12, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court erred in dismissing appellant property owners' claims against appellee government officials as their due process claims and common law causes of action were ripe for adjudication. The officials' argument concerning exhaustion of administrative remedies did not warrant a dismissal of the matter. One of the officials' actions was sufficient to establish personal jurisdiction, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 454.210. Under Ky. Const. § 13, owners were entitled to adequate discovery on takings issue. The trial court erred in dismissing the other claims without full and complete discovery.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

Jones v. Commonwealth


NO. 2011-CA-001298-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


413 S.W.3d 306; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 293



December 21, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Jones v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. LEXIS 614 (Ky., Nov. 13, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM GRAVES CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TIMOTHY C. STARK, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 11-CR-00093.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 218A.1415 and 218A.14151(2), the trial court did not err in holding that it had no authority to consider whether the prosecution's reasons for denying deferred prosecution were substantial and compelling. The granting of deferred prosecution was solely within the province of the prosecution and the trial court could not substitute its judgment for that of the prosecution.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

419 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Shafizadeh v. Shafizadeh


NO. 2010-CA-000758-MR AND NO. 2010-CA-002125-MR AND NO. 2011-CA-000825-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


444 S.W.3d 437; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 285



December 14, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Shafizadeh v. Guillory, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 84246 (W.D. La., June 17, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE JERRY J. BOWLES, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-CI-500527.
Shafizadeh v. Shafizadeh, 2009 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 81 (Ky. Ct. App., Apr. 10, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband said the trial court had no authority to enter an order while a Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26A.020 petition to disqualify the trial judge was pending. The appellate court held the trial court's order was premature but this defect did not extinguish the otherwise proper order because (1) the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction to decide "this kind of" case, (2) the trial court only lost particular case jurisdiction until the disqualification petition was decided, and, (3) when the Chief Justice denied the petition, the particular case jurisdictional defect was cured.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

420 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Pezzarossi v. Nutt


NO. 2011-CA-000990-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


392 S.W.3d 417; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 303



December 7, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Ordered Published February 8, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE BRIAN C. EDWARDS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-CI-011007.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff creditor sued defendant attorney seeking compensatory and punitive damages regarding the attorney's alleged fraudulent misrepresentation about his client repaying the creditor's loan. The loan was not repaid. The trial court declined to instruct the jury on the punitive damage claim. A jury awarded compensatory damages to the creditor. The appellate court found that the creditor established his threshold claim of fraudulent misrepresentation by clear and convincing evidence, and, thus, the trial court should have granted the request to instruct the jury on punitive damages.


OUTCOME: That part of the judgment addressing punitive damages and the order denying the motion for a new trial reversed, cause remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the issue of punitive damages.

 

421 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. County of Hardin Planning & Dev. Comm'n


NO. 2011-CA-001553-MR AND NO. 2011-CA-001632-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


390 S.W.3d 840; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 240



November 9, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. County of Hardin, 2013 Ky. LEXIS 693 (Ky., Dec. 11, 2013)
Related proceeding at Uninsured Emplr.' Fund v. Poplar Brook Dev., 2015 Ky. App. LEXIS 145 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 9, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM HARDIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE KELLY MARK EASTON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CI-01778. CROSS-APPEAL FROM HARDIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE KELLY MARK EASTON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CI-01778.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Although the Kentucky Uninsured Employer's Fund took no legislative or regulatory action limiting property use, its filing of an invalid lien under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.770, which resulted in termination of financing for a subdivision project, amounted to a taking. Thus, the developer was entitled to recover damages for inverse condemnation. Although the case did not involve the usual circumstances of a regulatory taking, it presented a real and substantial injury to a property owner resulting from an invalid state lien, for which compensation was properly awarded.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

422 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Norton v. Perry


NO. 2009-CA-002343-MR AND NO. 2009-CA-002394-MR

423 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins Indep. Schs v. Doe


NO. 2011-CA-001965-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


379 S.W.3d 808; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 196



September 28, 2012, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM LETCHER CIRCUIT COURT APPEAL FROM LETCHER CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SAMUEL T. WRIGHT III, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 11-CI-00108.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A finding against the school board in an action involving hazing was improper under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 160.160 because governmental immunity should have been sustained since municipal school boards were entitled to governmental immunity. There had been an intention to create an overall uniformity in all public schools with resulting coalescence between the powers and duties of an independent school system and those of a county school system. The trial court also erred when it found that the school board waived its immunity by purchasing liability insurance.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated in part and remanded.

Commonwealth v. Fowler


NO. 2011-CA-001581-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


409 S.W.3d 355; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 187



September 21, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Fowler v. Commonwealth, 2013 Ky. LEXIS 275 (Ky., May 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CHARLES L. CUNNINGHAM, JR., JUDGE. ACTION NO. 11-CR-000575.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The circuit court erred in granting defendant's motion to suppress evidence of marijuana and cocaine seized during a traffic stop, because a police officer had probable cause for the stop based upon defendant's failure to signal a lane change in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189.380. The circuit court, in finding that the statute did not require a driver to signal before changing lanes, deleted language from the statute, which was improper. This resulted in an absurd construction of the statute, as Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189.380 clearly required a driver to signal before changing lanes.


OUTCOME: Reversed; and remanded.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Long-term health care facility operators asserted that a county revenue commission improperly imposed an occupational license fee on capital gains from the sale of their business assets. Williams v. Chase Bank USA, N.A.

390 S.W.3d 824; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 78



May 25, 2012, Rendered

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JAMES M. SHAKE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 10-CI-000070.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellee bank was not required to obtain a certificate of authority before filing its suit against appellant debtor, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 271B.15-020(1), as a national bank was not required to file as a foreign corporation in order to maintain a lawsuit in state court, 12 U.S.C.S. § 24. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

430 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


A.C. v. Cabinet for Health & Family Servs.


NO. 2011-CA-000504-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


362 S.W.3d 361; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 41



February 24, 2012, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM KENTON FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE CHRISTOPHER J. MEHLING, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 10-AD-00049.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In proceedings for the termination of parental rights, the court held that, in enacting Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 625.080(3), the Kentucky legislature intended to afford indigent parents the benefits of counsel during the entire course of the termination proceedings, including any appeal. However, while an indigent parent defending a termination of parental rights action enjoyed a statutory right to counsel during the appeal, that right to counsel did not include the right of an indigent parent to bring a frivolous appeal and did not include the right to counsel for bringing a frivolous appeal.


OUTCOME: The order terminating the mother's parental rights was affirmed because the appeal was frivolous.

Reynolds Enters. v. Ky. Bd. of Embalmers & Funeral Dirs.


NO. 2010-CA-000729-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


382 S.W.3d 47; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 329



February 10, 2012, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Ordered Published March 30, 2012.
Review denied by Reynolds Enters. v. Ky. Bd. of Embalmers & Funeral Dirs., 2012 Ky. LEXIS 324 (Ky., Nov. 14, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PHILLIP J. SHEPHERD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-CI-00830.
Reynolds Enters. v. Ky. Bd. of Embalmers & Funeral Dirs., 2012 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 122 (Ky. Ct. App., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-There was no violation of the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Kentucky Constitution because the regulations contained in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 316.030(1) were rationally related to a legitimate state interest; [2]-The distinction between funeral directors and crematory operators reflected a legitimate interest in protecting public health and welfare; [3]-The interest in transporting dead human bodies did not rise to the level of a recognized property right; therefore, only the rational basis test had to be met; [4]-The trial court did not abuse its discretion by declining to enjoin the Kentucky Board of Embalmers and Funeral Directors from enforcing Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 316 against a crematory; [5]-The licensing requirements could not have been avoided simply by obtaining permission from a family member to transport a dead human body.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Moffitt v. Commonwealth


NO. 2010-CA-001822-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


360 S.W.3d 247; 2012 Ky. App. LEXIS 25



February 3, 2012, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM LIVINGSTON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CLARENCE A. WOODALL, III, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 01-CR-00024.
Moffitt v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 130 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 30, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Kentucky's Sex Offender Registration Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 17.500-17.580, did not violate the federal procedural or substantive due process rights of a person convicted of kidnapping a minor under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 509.040 by placing him on the sex offender registry pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 17.510(6), 17.520(2)(a), 17.500(3)(a). OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Castillo

2011 Ky. App. LEXIS 241



December 16, 2011, Rendered


NOTICE: TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied and ordered not published by Castillo v. Commonwealth, 2012 Ky. LEXIS 665 (Ky., Aug. 15, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS J. KNOPF, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CR-000446. APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE OLU A. STEVENS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CR-000446.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Where petitioner was charged with first-degree assault but the Commonwealth chose not to pursue the case and it was dismissed without prejudice and where petitioner, more than 10 years later, moved to expunge the case, the circuit court erred in granting the motion because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 431.076(a) authorized expungement only in cases that were dismissed with prejudice. Further, the circuit court was without jurisdiction to consider the matter pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 59.05 because petitioner sought relief more than 10 years after the order of dismissal was entered.


OUTCOME: The order granting petitioner's motion for expungement was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

435 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



W. Ky. Rural Elec. Coop. Corp. v. City of Bardwell


NO. 2010-CA-001140-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


362 S.W.3d 351; 2011 Ky. App. LEXIS 239



December 16, 2011, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CARLISLE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TIMOTHY A. LANGFORD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 09-CI-00064.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In a dispute over the provision of utility services to an annexed area, a first utility had the dominant right to provide service under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 96.538 because a fiscal court was the consumer both before and after the annexation. There was no distinction between consumers who added new services in § 96.538. Even though the trial court focused on who paid the bill to determine which party was the consumer, a county both paid for the services and used the services. Moreover, the trial court properly considered annexation of several properties as a single annexation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

443 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Gallien v. Ky. Bd. of Med. Licensure


NO. 2009-CA-000694-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


336 S.W.3d 924; 2011 Ky. App. LEXIS 54



March 25, 2011, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE FREDERIC COWAN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-CI-008619.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor appeals from an order of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) dismissing her petition for judicial review of an adverse determination of appellee Kentucky Board of Medical Licensure. At issue before the court was whether the circuit court correctly dismissed the doctor's petition because it had not been filed within the 30 days prescribed by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 311.593 and 13B.140(1).


OVERVIEW: The Board issued a complaint and emergency order of suspension against the doctor based on criminal accusations against her. Because the doctor had not practiced in more than two years during the pendency of that matter, the Board issued another order requiring her to complete a clinical skills assessment pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 311.604. The doctor did not schedule the assessment as ordered, and the Board issued an order of suspension, noting that the doctor had thirty days to appeal the order. She failed to file a petition for judicial review until nearly 18 months later. On appeal, the court determined that the delay was fatal to the doctor's appeal. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 311.593 and 13B.140, when read together, imposed a 30-day period of limitations for an aggrieved party to challenge a final order of the Board regarding a disciplinary action. The circuit court correctly concluded that it lacked jurisdiction to consider the doctor's petition for judicial review because the petition had not been timely filed. Although the order of suspension did not directly refer to itself as a "final and appealable order," it was clearly intended to act as such.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court.


 

444 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Aubrey


NO. 2009-CA-000728-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 214



November 19, 2010, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS D. WINGATE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 09-CI-00087.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commonwealth of Kentucky, sought review of a judgment of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) denying its motion to dismiss on the grounds that sovereign immunity barred a Declaratory Judgment Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. ch. 418, action against it. The action was filed by appellee members of the County Employees Retirement Systems (CERS). Appellee Kentucky Retirement Systems also tendered an appellee brief.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether sovereign immunity served as a bar to declaratory judgment actions that were not seeking monetary recompense but were challenging the constitutionality of a statute, as were the members; specifically, Ky. Rev. Stat. § 61.637(17). The Retirement Systems advocated that the Attorney General should defend the action, not it. The court determined that the Retirement Systems was a "person" pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. § 418.085 since corporations qualified as a "person." In addition, the court was unpersuaded by the argument that the Attorney General was in a better position than the Retirement Systems defend challenges to the constitutionality of statutes. The court then noted that it was convoluted reasoning to suggest that the Attorney General was protected by sovereign immunity under the declaratory judgment act, but the Retirement Systems was not. Both the Retirement Systems and the Attorney General were parts of the Commonwealth. The Commonwealth had the prerogative to opt out of defending the action but it could not then also claim sovereign immunity. Therefore, the trial court did not err in denying the Commonwealth's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

NO. 2009-CA-000186-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY

APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS L. CLARK, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 02-CI-02669.
DiGiuro v. Ragland, 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 188 (Ky. Ct. App., June 25, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death action, defendant appealed the judgment of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), arguing that the action was barred by the one-year statute of limitations under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.140 and that the punitive damage award was constitutionally excessive in that it violated his federal due process protections.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was charged with murder for the intentional killing of the decedent, plaintiff, the decedent's father, filed a wrongful death action. After defendant pled guilty to the lesser offense of manslaughter, plaintiff moved for summary judgment in the wrongful death action. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff on the issue of liability, and trial proceeded on the issue of damages. The jury awarded $3.3 million in compensatory damages and $60 million in punitive damages. On review, the court held that, because it had previously decided that plaintiff's claim was not barred by the statute of limitations, the law of the case doctrine applied and precluded the court from reviewing the issue again. However, the purpose of the punitive damage award was not to compensate the estate but to vindicate the state's legitimate interests in punishment and deterrence of conduct of the type in which defendant engaged. Under that analysis, the $ 60 million punitive award was grossly excessive; as such, it was violative of the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: That portion of the trial court's judgment awarding $60,000,000 in punitive damages was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to reduce the award to the constitutionally acceptable amount of $ 30 million, which represented a single-digit ratio of 9 to 1. While on the high end of single-digit ratios, such a punitive damage award was constitutionally permissible given the reprehensibility of defendant's murderous conduct.

 

446 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Phillips v. Commonwealth


NO. 2009-CA-000551-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


324 S.W.3d 741; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 199



October 22, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent civil proceeding at Phillips v. McCollum, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16219 (W.D. Ky., Feb. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM HENDERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE KAREN LYNN WILSON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-XX-00003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Henderson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which upheld his conviction for violating a city ordinance by willfully failing to file an occupational license return under City of Henderson Ordinance § 21-33.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the ordinance as applied deprived him of due process of law. He claimed that the trial court erred in failing to declare the ordinance unconstitutional, if not on its face, then at least as applied to him. Defendant argued that the City's failure to appoint a Board of Occupational License Appeals as described in the ordinance violated due process by depriving citizens of an administrative vehicle by which they could challenge their claim or assessment as to whether or not a return was due or a tax owed. Thus, defendant contended that the ordinance was unconstitutional as applied because it failed to offer him a pre-deprivation hearing, which would have been a meaningful opportunity either to contest the ordinance's requirements or to withhold a contested tax assessment. The court agreed with defendant. On paper, the ordinance provided defendant a fair opportunity to challenge his obligations, but the City never established the Board of Occupational License Appeals. The court further held that the putative administrative remedy could not have been exhausted as a prerequisite for judicial relief.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed.

 

447 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Abdul-Jalil v. Commonwealth


NO. 2009-CA-000487-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


324 S.W.3d 433; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 190



October 15, 2010, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE IRV MAZE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CR-001981.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which denied his motion to suppress evidence discovered during the execution of a warrant to search the car he was driving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the anonymous tip lacked the predictive quality required by the court's jurisprudence and that reliance on a tip which lacked sufficiently predictive information cannot be corroborated and therefore, was lacking as a basis for probable cause to seize his property. The Commonwealth argued that given the totality of the circumstances, the trial court was correct in denying defendant's motion. The Commonwealth justified the seizure of defendant's vehicle by claiming that there was probable cause to believe that a weapon would be found in the car and that if the car had not been impounded on the spot, the evidence would probably have been lost or destroyed. The court agreed with defendant and overruled the decision because an informant's tip lacked information that was adequately predictive. The tip also could have been corroborated to justify impounding the vehicle. Defendant's movement across the center console did not corroborate any aspect of the anonymous tip and certainly did not give rise to suspicion that evidence of a crime would be found anywhere in the car other than the area within his immediate control.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and remanded.

 

448 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Taylor v. King


NO. 2009-CA-001599-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


345 S.W.3d 237; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 179



October 1, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Taylor v. Daniel King Rsui Indem. Co., 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 111352 (W.D. Ky., Aug. 7, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CHRISTIAN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ANDREW SELF, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-CI-00805.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an estate administrator and a decedent's survivors, challenged a decision from the Christian Circuit Court, Kentucky, which determined that the Kentucky Dram Shop Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.241, prohibited the recovery of punitive damages against appellee bar owner.


OVERVIEW: It was alleged that a bartender at the owner's facility served a patron a large amount of drinks within a short period of time. The patron had an accident that killed the decedent. The trial court found that the decedent's estate was unable to recover punitive damages from the bar owner. This appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court determined that the prior interpretations of the Kentucky Dram Shop Act in Jackson v. Tullar were consistent with the clear language of the statute relating to the recovery of punitive damages. However, the Act's implicit prohibition on recovery of punitive damages violated the jural rights doctrine under Ky. Const. §§ 14, 54, 241 and separation-of-powers doctrine under Ky. Const. §§ 27, 28, 109. Therefore, the Act was unconstitutional to the extent that it prohibited recovery of punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings on the merits of the estate's claim for punitive damages.

450 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. Commonwealth


NO. 2008-CA-001729-MR AND NO. 2008-CA-001786-MR AND NO. 2009-CA-000306-MR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


335 S.W.3d 444; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 116



June 25, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Garcia, 2011 Ky. LEXIS 217 (Ky., Apr. 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEALS FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE KIMBERLY N. BUNNELL, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-CR-00152-MR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which denied their motion to suppress evidence obtained during a vehicular stop. Appellants alleged that the police stop of their vehicle was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ky. Const. § 10 because it was based upon an anonymous tip without any corroborating evidence of wrongdoing or any indicia of reliability.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were observed by a motorist swerving on the road. He called the police and told them where the appellants were located, but did not give his name. When the officer arrived, a person in another vehicle pointed to appellants. The officer stopped and searched appellants. They were ultimately arrested. Appellants filed motions to suppress, contending the stop of their vehicle was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ky. Const. § 10. They argued the tip came from an anonymous person. The Commonwealth alleged this was an identifiable informant or a citizen informant case. The court reversed. It ruled the tip was from an anonymous informant and did not carry sufficient indicia of reliability because it consisted of information readily available to a casual bystander. The officer testified he saw a man in a van pointing to appellants' vehicle and he did not have a conversation with him; thus, the tip was not from an identifiable citizen informant. The officer did not personally observe any illegal activity by appellants to corroborate the tipster's story. Given the totality of the circumstances, there was insufficient reliability to justify stopping appellants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying appellants' motion to suppress. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

451 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Ky. Exec. Branch Ethics Comm'n v. Atkinson


NO. 2009-CA-001145-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


339 S.W.3d 472; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 105



June 18, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Atkinson v. Ky. Exec. Branch Ethics Comm'n, 2011 Ky. LEXIS 615 (Ky., June 9, 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by Ky. Exec. Branch Ethics Comm'n v. Wooten, 2014 Ky. App. LEXIS 158 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 3, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PHILLIP J. SHEPHERD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-CI-01798.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Kentucky Executive Branch Ethics Commission, sought review of an opinion and order of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by appellees, current and former property valuation administrators (PVAs) in their declaratory judgment action and which enjoined the Commission to dismiss administrative charges against the PVAs for alleged violations of the Executive Branch Code of Ethics.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11A.080(1)(a), the Commission investigated the alleged violation of the Executive Branch Code of Ethics by the PVAs and found probable cause to believe a violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11A.020(1)(c) had occurred in the PVAs' hiring of family members. The trial court concluded that the Code of Ethics did not apply to the PVAs. It held that since the PVAs did not fall within the definition of "officer" or "public servant" under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11A.010(7) and (9), they were local officials and the Commission lacked jurisdiction to bring administrative charges against them. On appeal, the court disagreed. It determined that there was evidence that the PVAs were major management personnel in the executive branch of state government and thus were "officers" subject to the Executive Branch Code of Ethics. When the trial court resolved the case on statutory grounds, the Commission's claim that the PVAs' declaratory judgment action was premature for failure to exhaust administrative remedies became moot. However, the court's decision that the statutes were misapplied meant that the PVAs did have to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded with directions for the trial court to dismiss the case and lift its order holding the administrative proceedings in abeyance so that the PVAs could exhaust their administrative remedies.


 

452 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. Peabody Coal Co.


NO. 2009-CA-000927-WC


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 102



June 4, 2010, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified July 16, 2010
Affirmed by Vision Mining, Inc. v. Gardner, 2011 Ky. LEXIS 177 (Ky., Dec. 22, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
PETITION FOR REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD. ACTION NO. WC-02-01692.
Martinez v. Peabody Coal Co., 2005 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 801 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 23, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from a prior appeal, the Workers' Compensation Board (Kentucky) affirmed a judgment for appellee employer, denying appellant coal miner's claim for benefits for black lung disease. It found that the miner failed to overcome the presumption in the consensus classification statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. 342.316(13). The miner appealed, arguing that the burden placed upon him under § 342.316 was a violation of his right to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The miner's expert reported that the miner suffered from pneumoconiosis. The employer's expert submitted his own report that the miner did not. Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.316(13), the miner's x-rays were submitted to a panel of experts for a consensus decision. Two of the three believed he did not suffer for pneumoconiosis. Because the miner did not submit clear and convincing evidence to the contrary, as required under § 342.316(13), the administrative law judge determined that he did not qualify for workers' compensation benefits. The Board agreed. However, the reviewing court reversed, finding that § 342.316(13) impermissibly violated the miner's right to equal protection. Coal miner cases were treated differently with no substantial or justifiable reason for the disparate treatment of similarly situated compensable illnesses. There simply was no substantial nor justifiable reason to treat workers who contracted pneumoconiosis from coal mining differently from those who contracted pneumoconiosis due to the inhaling of other particulates. The burden that it established for those who made a claim was, therefore, a violation of equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

 

453 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Curtis Green & Clay Green, Inc. v. Clark


NO. 2006-CA-000086-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


318 S.W.3d 98; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 89



May 21, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Cherry v. Wingate, 2012 Ky. Unpub. LEXIS 12 (Ky., Feb. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CI-01067.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court, Kentucky, granted summary judgment declaring that appellant employers, members of the workers' compensation self-insurance group, were jointly and severally liable for all claims against the fund. The employers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employers argued that the enactment of S.B. 86 impaired vested rights and defenses and it constituted special legislation prohibited by the Kentucky Constitution because the employers were the only entity affected by the governor's ratified Executive Order and by the statute's retroactive application. The appellate court found that the language of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 304.50-005 clearly defined the class as required and provided that it was applicable to all members of the class. There were distinctive and natural reasons supporting the classification, which was met by the nature of self-insured groups, the similarity of such groups and the legitimate legislative interest in regulating the risks and liabilities of injured employees and their members. There was no indicating that S.B. 86 would apply only to the group if there were other workers' compensation self-insured groups. Application of S.B. 86 was not unconstitutional, special, or retroactive legislation. The circuit court had jurisdiction over the rehabilitation and sufficient notice was given. There was no breach of the indemnity agreement which would allow the employers to rescind the joint and several provisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Sahni v. Hock


NO. 2007-CA-001785-MR, NO. 2007-CA-002421-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


369 S.W.3d 39; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 79



April 23, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Sahni v. Hock, 2011 Ky. LEXIS 231 (Ky., Apr. 13, 2011)
Review denied by, Review improvidently allowed by Sahni v. Hock, 2011 Ky. LEXIS 336 (Ky., Nov. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DENISE CLAYTON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 01-CI-06364. CROSS-APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DENISE CLAYTON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 01-CI-06364.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court, Kentucky, granted judgment in favor of appellee shareholder, individually and on behalf of appellee corporation, on her derivative claims for breach of fiduciary duty. Appellant director appealed; the shareholder cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The director argued that the shareholder failed to satisfy the demand requirement of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 271B.7-400(2), because she alleged claims in her verified complaint that were not included in her demand letter. The appellate court concluded that the shareholder failed to make a sufficient demand for action as contemplated by the statute. The demand letter dated May 16, 2001, simply requested production of certain information and demanded an investigation into her particular allegations. She at no time demanded the commencement of legal action. The trial court did not err by concluding that the shareholder fairly and adequately represented the interests of the shareholders as she was the only shareholder available to pursue claims on behalf of the other shareholders. The shareholder failed to demonstrate a specific injury to herself outside the diminution in value of company stock and she did not sufficiently allege a cause of action under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 271B.8-300. The shareholder's proceeding was not wholly without merit, and the trial court erred in awarding the director attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in favor of the shareholder individually and remanded with instructions to dismiss her direct action claim; the judgment was reversed as to the award of attorney fees to the director and remanded for further proceedings. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

 

457 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. Vision Mining, Inc.


NO. 2009-CA-000874-WC


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 69



April 9, 2010, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Vision Mining, Inc. v. Gardner, 2011 Ky. LEXIS 177 (Ky., Dec. 22, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
PETITION FOR REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD. ACTION NO. WC-07-01156.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee, a coal miner, sought review of an opinion and order of the Kentucky Workers' Compensation Board (Board), affirming the dismissal of his claim against appellee employer by an Administrative Law Judge (ALJ). The employee contended that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.316, which defined the procedure for coal workers' pneumoconiosis claims (CWP), was unconstitutional in violation of his right to equal protection under the law.


OVERVIEW: Attached to the employee's CWP claim application, as required by § 342.316(3)(a)(1), was an x-ray interpretation, indicating that the employee was positive for CWP. The employer countered with its own x-ray interpretation. According to the statute, because the interpretations differed, an x-ray was sent to a three-person panel for a consensus, with the panel's classification of the CWP presumed to be the correct classification of the employee's condition unless overcome by clear and convincing evidence. On appeal, the court agreed with the employee that the statute unconstitutionally violated his equal protection rights as a coal miner who suffered from pneumoconiosis by imposing more stringent procedural and substantive law requirements on coal worker claimants than on other pneumoconiosis claimants. There was no rational basis for disparate treatment of industrial workers with the same occupational disease based on nothing more than the industry in which the disease was contracted. Accordingly, § 342.316 was unconstitutional insofar as it required the three-member consensus panel and imposed a higher burden of proof upon CWP claimants than on other pneumoconiosis claimants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the cause for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PAMELA R. GOODWINE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-CR-01241.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress evidence was denied, defendant entered a conditional guilty plea in the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) to first-degree trafficking in a controlled substance, possession of drug paraphernalia, and operating on a suspended or revoked license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress because the search of his vehicle was illegal under U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court of appeals agreed. The officer conducted a traffic stop of defendant's vehicle for failing to use his blinker when he turned left in a left-turn-only lane. Upon checking defendant's license, it was discovered that defendant was driving on a suspended license. The officer placed defendant under arrest for that offense. The officer testified at the suppression hearing that his only reason for stopping defendant was the commission of a minor traffic offense. He further stated that during the arrest there was nothing in plain view that generated a suspicion that defendant might have drugs or paraphernalia in the vehicle.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case was remanded to allow defendant to withdraw his guilty plea.

Hill v. Commonwealth


NO. 2008-CA-001752-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


308 S.W.3d 227; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 111



February 12, 2010, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM HARDIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE KELLY MARK EASTON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-CR-00254.
Hill v. Commonwealth, 2010 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 111 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 12, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pro se defendant appealed from an order of the Hardin Circuit Court (Kentucky), directing that $ 2,175 forfeited to the Commonwealth not be returned to him. Defendant argued that the currency was not connected to any criminal activity for which he was convicted and should have been returned to him.


OVERVIEW: There was sufficient evidence to warrant forfeiture of the money under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.410(1)(j). The money was found in close proximity to the drugs. Defendant's recorded confession included a denial that he smoked crack cocaine but made money from it. Defendant was found with one large bag of cocaine in one pants pocket and several small "packaged" baggies in the other pocket. Given the evidence of traceability, the burden of proof then shifted to defendant, forcing him to rebut the presumption, by clear and convincing evidence, that the money was not involved in drug related activity. The only evidence he presented was his self-serving testimony that he won it gambling. He claimed he had a casino receipt on him at the time of his arrest, but he did not produce it at trial or the forfeiture hearing. The forfeiture was not excessive when compared to other cases involving the forfeiture of property. Also notable was the fact that defendant could have been fined between $ 1,000 and $ 10,000 due to his being convicted of a felony under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 534.030(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Campbell v. Campbell


NO. 2006-CA-001803-MR AND NO. 2006-CA-001827-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 27



February 5, 2010, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Campbell v. Campbell, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 581 (Ky., June 9, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT FAMILY COURT DIVISION. HONORABLE JERRY J. BOWLES, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-FC-006862.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband filed a petition for dissolution of his marriage to appellee former wife. The Jefferson Circuit Court Family Court Division (Kentucky) dissolved the marriage but reserved other issues for future adjudication. The parties then agreed to binding arbitration. The family court signed the arbitration award without independent review. Both parties appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The arbitration order required the family court to enter the arbitrator's award as a judgment of the family court without independent judicial review or without an opportunity for either party to submit objections to the family court. In a case of first impression in Kentucky, the court concluded on appeal that the family court improperly delegated its constitutional duties, including its decision-making authority, to an arbitrator in contravention of Ky. Const. § 109 and in circumvention of the legislative intent regarding the duties of family court judges. Because of the Commonwealth's compelling interests in the area of domestic relations and the family court's unique protective role in this area of the law, especially in the establishment of family courts through constitutional amendment, a domestic relations proceeding was not an arbitratable controversy within the meaning of the Uniform Arbitration Act, codified as Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 417. Under Ky. R. Civ. P. 52.01 and Jefferson Fam. Ct. R. Prac. 702, the family court was required to hold a hearing upon all pending matters and to make independent findings of fact and conclusions of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the cause with directions that the family court conduct an evidentiary hearing or trial and render independent findings of fact and conclusions of law as required by law.

 

461 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Commonwealth v. Spurlock


NO. 2008-CA-001184-MR & NO. 2008-CA-001275-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


308 S.W.3d 221; 2010 Ky. App. LEXIS 15



January 22, 2010, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified: March 26, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEALS FROM CLAY CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE OSCAR G. HOUSE, JUDGE. ACTION NOS. 05-CI-00279 AND 05-CI-00280.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commonwealth of Kentucky, Energy and Environment Cabinet (Cabinet), sought review of two orders of the Clay Circuit Court (Kentucky) declaring void the Cabinet's final orders entered against appellees, an individual property owner and a coal company. The Cabinet had imposed civil penalties on the owner for violating the provisions of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 350 et seq., and its related regulations pertaining to surface coal mining.


OVERVIEW: The Cabinet sent the owner notices of assessments on a preprinted form that did not advise the owner of his right to seek a waiver of the requirement that he prepay the proposed penalties if he wanted to request a formal hearing. The owner never responded and then sought judicial relief. The circuit court declared the orders void. On appeal, the court overturned the Cabinet's orders on different grounds. In Franklin, the Supreme Court of Kentucky held that the Cabinet's prepayment provisions imposed prior to the granting of a formal hearing were unauthorized by statute and unconstitutional. Despite this ruling and subsequent legislative and administrative changes in response to Franklin, the form notice here advised the owner that he was not entitled to an administrative hearing absent prepayment of the proposed penalty. An agency was without authority to issue an order in direct contradiction of Kentucky's statutes and judicial decisions. This was particularly true where the agency misinformed a citizen regarding a constitutional right to which he was entitled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's opinion and orders and remanded the case to the Cabinet with directions that the owner be granted the opportunity to request a formal hearing accompanied by a proper request for a waiver from the prepayment provisions.


 

462 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Cabinet for Health & Family Servs. v. J.T.G.


NO. 2009-CA-000211-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


301 S.W.3d 35; 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 245



December 4, 2009, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM SCOTT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TAMRA GORMLEY, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-J-00205.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Cabinet for Health and Family Services (Cabinet), sought review of an order of the Scott Circuit Court, Family Division (Kentucky) (Scott Family Court) finding it in contempt for failing to pay child care assistance costs to appellees, an uncle who agreed to take permanent custody of a child who was his niece. The uncle resided in Scott County and the child's mother resided in Jefferson County.


OVERVIEW: The Jefferson Family Court granted permanent custody of the child to the uncle and his partner. Although it was not in the order, the uncle claimed that the Cabinet agreed to pay for child care assistance costs. At the uncle's request, the Jefferson Family Court transferred the action to Scott County. Despite having transferred the action, the Jefferson Family Court ordered the Cabinet to provide assistance. The uncle returned to the Scott Family Court to enforce the Jefferson Family Court's order. The court held that the Scott Family Court abused its discretion in holding the Cabinet in contempt for failing to comply with the Jefferson Family Court's order because the Jefferson Family Court lost jurisdiction over the matter once it was transferred to the Scott Family Court pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 452.010(1). Thus, the Jefferson Family Court's order was void ab initio. Further, the Scott Family Court abused its discretion in denying the Cabinet's Ky. R. Civ. P. 59.05 motion to alter, amend, or vacate its previous orders mandating payment of child care costs because the law of the case doctrine did not apply and it did not consider Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 610.010(12).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the Scott Family Court and remanded the case with instructions for the Scott Family Court to disregard the invalid order entered by the Jefferson Family Court and to reconsider the Cabinet's Ky. R. Civ. P. 59.05 59.05 motion in light of the appellate opinion, including but not limited to a consideration of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 610.010(12) and its applicability to the facts of the case.

McDonald's Corp. v. Ogborn


NO. 2008-CA-000024-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


309 S.W.3d 274; 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 236; 30 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 56; 107 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1516



November 20, 2009, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM BULLITT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TOM MCDONALD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CI-00769.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a negligence and false imprisonment action resulting from a hoax perpetrated against managers and employees of a fast-food restaurant, defendant restaurant corporation appealed a judgment of the Bullitt Circuit Court (Kentucky) that awarded compensatory and punitive damages under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.184 to plaintiff, a former employee who was sexually assaulted as a result of the hoax.


OVERVIEW: As a result of a hoax telephone call by someone representing himself to be a police officer, the employee was falsely accused of theft, threatened, subjected to strip and body cavity searches, and held against her will in a room with several men, one of whom sexually assaulted her. On review, the court that the evidence supported the employee's false imprisonment claim because she was deprived of her clothing, repeatedly objected to the search of her body, was threatened with further police involvement, was held in a locked room, and had a constant guard between herself and the door. The evidence further supported the employee's negligence claim because the evidence showed that the restaurant corporation was aware of the hoax, that the hoax had been perpetrated at another of its restaurants, and that its management team made a conscious decision not to tell restaurant managers of the hoax or to provide training or instruction to prevent the hoax from successfully occurring again. The award of punitive damages was not unreasonable because the jury found that the restaurant corporation owed a duty to train, supervise, or warn about the hoax calls and that it failed in that duty.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the restaurant's former employee was affirmed.

Affirmed by TECO Mech. Contr., Inc. v. Commonwealth, 366 S.W.3d 386, 2012 Ky. LEXIS 23 (Ky., 2012)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PHILLIP J. SHEPHERD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CI-00464.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mechanical contractor appealed the summary judgment entered in the Franklin Circuit Court, Kentucky, upholding the constitutionality of portions of Ky. Rev. Stat. ch. 337 and assessing back wages and civil penalties against the contractor.


OVERVIEW: The contractor provided services on public works projects that were awarded based on payment of the prevailing wage pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 337 (the Act). The Court of Appeals of Kentucky upheld the trial court's finding that the Act was constitutional. The Cabinet was not exercising judicial authority when it issued its citation and sought to collect back wages. The trial court used the incorrect standard of review in finding for the Cabinet on its counterclaims. The audit forms submitted by the Cabinet were inadmissible hearsay.


OUTCOME: The trial court's finding that the Act was constitutional was affirmed; however, the appellate court vacated and remanded the trial court's finding for the Cabinet on its cross-claims. On remand, the trial court was directed to evaluate the evidence presented de novo without deferring to the Cabinet as to its findings or its method of classification.

Revenue Cabinet v. Asworth Corp.


NO. 2007-CA-002549-MR AND NO. 2008-CA-000023-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 229



November 20, 2009, Rendered


NOTICE: TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified February 5, 2010.
Review denied by Asworth Corp. v. Revenue Cabinet, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 424 (Ky., Aug. 18, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Asworth, LLC v. Ky. Dep't of Revenue, Fin. & Admin. Cabinet, 131 S. Ct. 1046, 178 L. Ed. 2d 865, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1056 (U.S., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS D. WINGATE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CI-00288.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court, Kentucky, reversed the order of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals (Board), holding that appellee corporations were not subject to Kentucky corporation income tax but were subject to tax on their distributive share income from partnerships, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 141.206. Appellant Finance and Administration Cabinet, Department of Revenue (Cabinet) appealed; the corporations cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporations argued that the circuit court erred by finding that they were subject to taxation pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 141.206(5). The appellate court found that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 141.206(5) subjected the corporations to taxation. The statute was not void for vagueness, i.e., unintelligibility. While the corporations did no business in Kentucky, at various times they owned up to a 99% limited and/or general partnership interest in, and have received distributive shares of partnership income from the profits of, a partnership which did business in Kentucky. As such, this provided the requisite link for taxation under the Commerce Clause and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 141.206(5), the legislature intended for the amount of tax owed to be calculated using the formula found therein. This would not result in extraterritorial values being taxed. The corporations were not entitled to immediate payment of any refund, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 131.365, 134.580. The challenged portions of the house and senate bills were not impermissible special legislation in violation of Ky. Const. § 59 with respect to regulating the rate of interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed to the extent that the corporations had a tax nexus with Kentucky; the judgment was reversed insofar as the apportionment method applied and the order of an immediate refund in favor of the corporations.

Fuel Transp., Inc. v. Gibson

2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 183

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Gibson v. Fuel Transp., Inc., 2010 Ky. LEXIS 652 (Ky., Oct. 13, 2010)
Review granted by Fuel Transp., Inc. v. Gibson, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 368 (Ky., Dec. 9, 2010)
Affirmed by, Remanded by, Vacated by, in part Gibson v. Fuel Transp., Inc., 2013 Ky. LEXIS 29 (Ky., Mar. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM KNOTT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE KIM C. CHILDERS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CI-00103.
Gibson v. Am. Mining Ins. Co., 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 90858 (E.D. Ky., Nov. 7, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death action, defendant fuel transport company appealed a judgment of the Knott Circuit Court (Kentucky) in favor of plaintiff, the estate of a decedent who died in an accident caused by the transport company's alleged negligence, arguing that the trial court erred in denying its motion for a new trial on the basis of juror misconduct and that the imposition of punitive damages was improper without a showing of gross negligence.


OVERVIEW: The driver of a coal truck entered the wrong lane and overcorrected, causing his rig to overturn. Moments later, the vehicle in which the decedent was a passenger crashed into the coal debris, and the decedent sustained fatal injuries. On review, the court held that the trial court did not err in declining to grant a new trial because a juror did not conceal that her father had been killed in an automobile accident. Although defense counsel asked jurors if they had ever been involved in a traffic accident, the jurors were not asked if any family members had been involved in such an accident; as such, defense counsel failed to ask questions that would have elicited the information they claimed the juror withheld. However, the trial court erred in denying a directed verdict on the punitive damages claim. Punitive damages under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.184 were only proper in cases of gross negligence. Although the fuel transport company's driver failed to exercise reasonable care, his actions did not rise to the level of wanton or reckless disregard for others. An award of punitive damages under the circumstances would eliminate the distinction between ordinary and gross negligence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case was remanded with instructions to vacate that portion of the judgment awarding punitive damages.

2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 176

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant illegitimate son appealed an order of the Perry Circuit Court, Kentucky, dismissing his claim for an interest in property.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died intestate on September 20, 1975, and was survived by all four of his children. Appellant was his illegitimate son. At the time of his father's death, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 391.090(2) prohibited an illegitimate child from inheriting from his father. Accordingly, all property owned by decedent descended to only his three youngest children. In 1977, the Kentucky Supreme Court held Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 391.090(2) unconstitutional. Over thirty years later, appellant filed a complaint for his interest in his father's property. The circuit court dismissed the complaint, because judicial precedents holding Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 391.090 unconstitutional did not have a retroactive effect. The Court of Appeals of Kentucky upheld the decision. Because decedent died before Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 391.090 was declared unconstitutional, appellant did not inherit an interest in his father's property.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Delahanty v. Commonwealth ex rel. Maze


NO. 2008-CA-000580-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


295 S.W.3d 136; 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 124



July 31, 2009, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SUSAN SCHULTZ GIBSON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 08-CI-001666.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a district court judge, sought review of a decision of the Jefferson Circuit Court, (Kentucky), which granted a writ of prohibition against the judge. The controversy involved a verbal and written prohibition, promulgated by the judge, that prohibited a county attorney and his assistants from making objections during a preliminary probable cause hearing.


OVERVIEW: The judge issued an order precluding county attorneys from posing objections to questions at future preliminary hearings on several listed grounds. The circuit court issued a writ of prohibition against the judge. The court held that a requirement that a writ of prohibition against a district court be filed in a circuit court was not without reason and was in conformance with the provisions set forth in Ky. R. Civ. P. 81, Ky. Sup. Ct. R. 1.040(6), and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23A.080(2). The court rejected the judge's argument that the Kentucky Supreme Court was the only court that could impose a prohibition. Further, the county attorney had standing to commence the action. The court agreed with the lower court that the extraordinary relief afforded by a writ was warranted because the judge's directive prevented county attorneys from advocating on behalf of the Commonwealth, resulting in an irreparable injury without an adequate remedy for appeal. Although the judge had potential grounds for sanctioning the individual attorney, he could not issue a verbal and written directive stifling the ability of all county attorneys to ask questions of defense witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.
