Newport Indep. Sch. District/Newport Bd. of Educ. v. Commonwealth


NO. 2008-CA-001615-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


300 S.W.3d 216; 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 118



July 24, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Newport Indep. Sch. District/Newport Bd. of Educ. v. Commonwealth, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 515 (Ky., Jan. 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JULIE REINHARDT WARD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-CI-01770.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a school district, board of education, and superintendent, filed a petition for a declaration of rights contesting the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 160.350(2). They challenged a judgment of the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted appellee Commonwealth's motion to dismiss and upheld the statute as constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The school district entered into a contract with the superintendent, who was an Ohio resident. The Kentucky Office of Education Accountability issued an investigative report stating that the superintendent violated § 160.350(2) because he was not a Kentucky resident. The court of appeals held that requiring the superintendent to reside in Kentucky after he was appointed was not an improper restraint upon his right to travel and migrate under Ky. Const. § 24 and the United States Constitution. Section 160.350(2) imposed a permissible residency requirement. There was no requirement that a candidate for superintendent had to have been a Kentucky resident for a certain number of years. Instead, Kentucky residency was imposed as a condition of employment that could occur after hiring. The statute did not deny the superintendent equal protection of the law. The Commonwealth's argument that a Kentucky resident would have a better comprehension of Kentucky's educational needs was a rational basis for Kentucky's requirement that superintendents live in Kentucky.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's order.

Kessler v. Switzer


NO. 2008-CA-002083-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


289 S.W.3d 228; 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 76



June 5, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Kessler v. Switzer, 2010 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 975 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PAULA SHERLOCK, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-D-503629.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband appealed an extension of a domestic violence order (DVO) entered by the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) for one year.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.750(2) did not require proof of additional acts of violence. A hearing was not required before an extension of a DVO was ordered. If a hearing was required, the process articulated in § 403.750(2) for extending a DVO would be rendered useless, as the process would be the same as the process for originally granting a DVO. The husband failed to notify the Kentucky Attorney General during the pendency of the case before the trial court and therefore his constitutional claims were not preserved for review under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.075. The trial court was familiar with the details of the case, as she had followed it through district and circuit court. Further, the trial court considered the dismissed criminal charges, appellee wife's affidavit, and the fact that the wife was only asking for a one-year extension of the DVO. The trial court properly considered the circumstances surrounding the original issuance of the DVO and the effectiveness of the DVO in preventing any violence between the parties, which fully satisfied the purpose of Kentucky's domestic violence and abuse policy under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.715(1).


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

472 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Looper


NO. 2008-CA-000850-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


294 S.W.3d 39; 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 61



May 8, 2009, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Looper, 2009 Ky. LEXIS 611 (Ky., Oct. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CRAIG Z. CLYMER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-CR-00674.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth challenged an order of the McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed the charges against defendant for violating Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 150.740 and ruled that the statute was unconstitutional as being void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Section § 150.740 banned the importation of the members of the animal family Cervidae in the Commonwealth. Defendant had purchased elk, deer, antelope, and exotic sheep in Missouri and was enroute travelling through Kentucky to a lodge in Tennessee that had purchased the animals. The court of appeals held that the trial court properly determined that § 150.740 was unconstitutional as applied in the case as being void for vagueness. It was reasonable to believe that defendant drove through Kentucky in good faith. He had no notice that merely driving through Kentucky with the deer and elk was a felony. The statute did not define the word "importation." The definitions of "import" connoted a business interest underlying the activity of bringing in particular goods. Merely transporting an item through an area was not the same as importing it. It would be reasonable for defendant to have believed that as long as he did not unload cervids in Kentucky, he would not be importing them. The statute did not provide any limitation on the common meaning of importation. There was no administrative regulation construing the statute.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the order of the trial court.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS L. CLARK, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CR-01733.

Ann. § 510.155, which prohibited the unlawful use of electronic means to induce a minor to engage in sexual or other prohibited activities. In exchange for his plea, the Fayette Circuit Court, Kentucky, sentenced him to a total of five years' imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from four conversations he had on the internet and telephone with an undercover police detective posing as a fourteen-year-old girl. Defendant entered a conditional guilty plea to four counts of violating Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.155, which prohibited the use of electronic means to induce a minor to engage in sexual activities. The Court of Appeals of Kentucky held that the protection against double jeopardy was not violated. Each count of the indictment referred to conduct which would constitute a separate violation of Ky. Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't v. Metro Louisville Hospitality Coalition


NO. 2008-CA-000377-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


297 S.W.3d 42; 2009 Ky. App. LEXIS 24



February 13, 2009, Rendered 
February 13, 2009, Entered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE STEPHEN P. RYAN, JUDGE. ACTION NOS. 06-CI-010176 & 06-CI-010668.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) ruled that the severability clause in an ordinance banning smoking in certain places was invalid, and therefore struck the ordinance in its entirety due to an unconstitutional provision exempting a racetrack. Appellant county metro council sought review; appellees, a corporation and a limited liability company, moved to dismiss the appeal for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court entered judgment, the council amended and re-enacted the ordinance, deleting the exemption for the racetrack. Appellees argued that as a justiciable controversy no longer existed, the appellate court lacked jurisdiction. The appellate court disagreed. A justiciable controversy existed because appellees sought relief beyond the racetrack's exemption and because there were pending actionable citations under the former ordinance. The trial court invalidated the entire ordinance, despite a severability clause that complied with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 446.090, based upon its finding that the council would not have passed the ordinance without the exemption for the racetrack. In doing so, it erred by reviewing the legislative history without first finding that any portion of the ordinance was ambiguous. With the deletion of the racetrack exemption, the ordinance could still fully serve its purpose of promoting the public's health. The ordinance was not inseparably connected and dependent upon the racetrack exemption such that was is apparent that the council would not have enacted it in the absence of the exemption.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied appellees' motion to dismiss and reversed the decision of the trial court.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE KIMBERLY N. BUNNELL, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 07-XX-00003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an opinion by the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) that affirmed the trial court's denial of his motion to present the result of a preliminary breath test as exculpatory evidence; defendant claimed that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.104(2) was unconstitutional because it violated his right to due process and offended the doctrine of separation of powers.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was pulled over for driving without his headlights illuminated, the police officer noticed that he had a strong odor of alcohol about his person. The officer administered several field sobriety tests to defendant, which defendant failed, as well as a preliminary breath test (PBT). The appellate court found that defendant did not refuse to submit to one of the tests found in § 189A.104(1) nor was he subject to any enhancement of penalties. Consequently, the statute and its prohibition regarding the admissibility of PBT results did not apply. Furthermore, because the statute was inapplicable to defendant's case, the question of its constitutionality was a moot issue.


OUTCOME: The appellate opinion, the judgment of conviction, and the order denying defendant's motion to present exculpatory evidence were vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Grant v. Heltsley


NO. 2007-CA-002193-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


268 S.W.3d 382; 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 318



October 17, 2008, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CHRISTIAN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JASON S. FLEMING, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 02-CI-01216.
Lynn v. Grant, 2005 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 731 (Ky. Ct. App., June 24, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Christian Circuit Court (Kentucky) entered three judgments that found appellee maternal grandmother sufficiently proved that grandparent visitation with appellee father's teenage son and daughter was in the best interests of those children. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father's wife was the daughter of the maternal grandmother. The father and his wife had two children and soon divorced. The wife eventually received joint custody of the two children. Thereafter, the maternal grandmother's husband died. The wife died a few days later. The father obtained sole custody of them following a heated custody action involving the maternal grandmother. The maternal grandmother sought visitation with the two children. Later, the trial court entered judgments finding that the maternal grandmother sufficiently proved grandparent visitation, as contemplated by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021, was in the best interests of the two children. The appellate court found that (1) even though the father's woefully deficient appellate brief could have been stricken for noncompliance with Ky. R. Civ. P. 76.12, the appellate court would still decide the matter, (2) the father had not shown that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021 was unconstitutional, (3) the maternal grandmother had shown pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021, and by clear and convincing evidence, that visitation of the two children with her was in the best interests of the children.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

478 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


S.J.L.S. v. T.L.S.


NO. 2006-CA-001730-ME, NO. 2006-CA-001731-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


265 S.W.3d 804; 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 282



September 12, 2008, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE ELEANORE GARBER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-AD-500471. APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE ELEANORE GARBER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 01-FC-005806.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In companion cases, appellant biological parent appealed a decision by the Jefferson Family Court, Kentucky, refusing to set aside, under Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02, an adoption decree and a joint custody order relating to her biological child. Appellee, the biological parent's same-sex life partner, argued that the adoption was permitted as a "stepparent-like" adoption under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 199.470(4)(a).


OVERVIEW: When granting the life partner's adoption petition, the family court accepted the parties' agreement that the adoption would not terminate the biological parent's rights. On appeal, the court held that the life partner was not the child's stepparent because same-sex marriages were void as against public policy, and "stepparent-like" adoptions were not recognized in Kentucky. The family court's creation of the legal fiction that the life partner was a stepparent was an invalid attempt to avoid Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 199.520(2), 402.020(1)(d), 402.040(2), and Ky. Const. § 233a. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 199.520(2), requiring termination of ties between biological parents and children upon adoption, was not subject to waiver by agreement. The adoption was also invalid because the Kentucky Cabinet of Families and Children refused to consent as required by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 199.510(1). Despite its procedural irregularities, the adoption decree was not attackable because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 199.540(2)'s one-year annulment period had passed, but the custody order was attackable under Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02 because the family court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to grant the adoption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the family court's order overruling the biological parent's motion to set aside the adoption decree rendered in favor of the life partner. The court reversed the family court's order overruling the biological parent's motion to set aside the joint child custody order and remanded for further proceedings.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the decision entered by the Perry Circuit Court (Kentucky) that entered judgment in favor of appellees in a dispute over the use of a coal haul road.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were the owners of surface land located and appellees were the owners or assignees of the mineral rights on the same property, acquired by a severance deed from 1910. The court concluded that the trial court erred in denying appellants the right to a trial by jury. Moreover, as there was no dispute that appellants neither withdrew their demand, nor consented to the bench trial by written or oral stipulation, the appellate court found that they did not waive their constitutional right to a jury trial on all issues pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 38.04 and 39.01.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

480 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Cook v. Taylor


NO. 2007-CA-000122-MR & NO. 2007-CA-000221-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 264



August 22, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, August 19, 2009. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered not to be Published.
Review denied and ordered not published by Taylor v. Cook, 2009 Ky. LEXIS 212 (Ky., Aug. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM ANDERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CHARLES R. HICKMAN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CI-00020.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant spouse, individually and as administratrix of a decedent's estate (administratrix), appealed an order of the Anderson Circuit Court (Kentucky) dismissing her claims against appellees, a paramedic and an emergency medical technician (EMT). The paramedics cross-appealed the decision not to additionally dismiss the administratrix's claims pursuant to the doctrine of release.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the paramedics were not subject to the Good Samaritan immunity under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 411.148 and 311A.150. Section 411.148 did not apply to the regular professional work responsibilities of paramedics for which they were paid. The paramedics provided care to the decedent in the normal course of their work. They had a duty to assist the decedent. Care or treatment for remuneration or due to a pre-existing duty was specifically exempted from the immunity granted by § 411.148. The purpose of § 411.148 was to encourage the rendering of medical assistance to those in need by trained medical personnel by removing the fear of liability that accompanied rendering aid under the common law. The adoption of § 411.148 was within the legislature's police powers, and did not violate the jural rights doctrine under Ky. Const. §§ 14, 54, and 241. The refusal to dismiss the suit under the release doctrine was proper as there were fact issues as to what was stated by paramedics about the decedent's condition. Whether the spouse would have signed the release depended on the version of the facts that was correct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

481 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Dutschke v. Jim Russell Realtors, Inc.


NO. 2007-CA-001146-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


281 S.W.3d 817; 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 248



August 1, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Dutschke v. Jim Russell Realtors, Inc., 2009 Ky. LEXIS 848 (Ky., May 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE MARTIN MCDONALD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-CI-07011.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants home buyers sued appellees, the seller, a real estate agent, the agent's agency, and the agency's owner, in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) for fraudulent inducement. The trial court granted appellees' motion to require arbitration, and an arbitrator awarded the buyers less damages than they sought. The trial court denied the buyers' motion to vacate the arbitration award and confirmed the award. The buyers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The buyers said Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 417, on arbitration, was unconstitutional under the Kentucky Constitution. The appellate court held it had no authority to accept their claim that a Kentucky Supreme Court decision was wrongly decided. Chapter 417 did not violate their Ky. Const. § 7 right to a jury trial because that section contemplated exceptions to the right, and Ky. Const. § 250, allowing the creation of an arbitration system, was such an exception. Chapter 417 did not violate the separation of powers doctrine in Ky. Const. §§ 27 and 28 because Ky. Const. § 250 gave the legislature the power to establish an arbitration system. The standard for finding if a party was bound by an arbitration agreement was not that applied to a waiver of constitutional rights in a criminal case but, once a proper arbitration agreement was shown, required one opposing arbitration to rebut a statutory presumption of its validity. Chapter 417 did not violate Ky. Const. § 2 by failing to provide meaningful judicial review of arbitration because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 417.160 and 417.170 provided such review. The level of judicial review was consistent with the purposes of arbitration.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Veltrop v. Commonwealth


NO. 2007-CA-000385-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


269 S.W.3d 15; 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 244



August 1, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Veltrop v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 729 (Ky., Nov. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM BARREN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PHIL PATTON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-XX-00001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the district court, defendant entered a conditional plea of guilty to DUI in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.010. She reserved the question of whether § 189A.010(2) was unconstitutional. The Barren Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed the district court's decision. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 189A.010(2), which applied to test results taken over two hours after cessation of operation or physical control of a motor vehicle, violated the Kentucky Constitution's principle of separation of powers. The court held that defendant lacked standing to challenge the provision. Her test result was obtained well within the two-hour limit that was set forth as an element of the offense in § 189A.010(1)(a). Because the test result was within that time period, § 189A.010(2) had no relevance or application to her case. She therefore could not have suffered any injury or harm from it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Monumental Life Ins. Co. v. Dep't of Revenue


NO. 2005-CA-002148-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


294 S.W.3d 10; 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 207



June 27, 2008, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Monumental Life Ins. Co. v. Dep't of Revenue, 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 340 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 8, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Monumental Life Ins. Co. v. Ky Dep't of Revenue, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 2866 (U.S., Mar. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER L. CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-CI-01652.
Monumental Life Ins. Co. v. Dep't of Rev., 201 S.W.3d 500, 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 263 (Ky. Ct. App., 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals denied appellant taxpayer's tax refund claims against appellees, the Commonwealth of Kentucky, the city, the county, and various government agencies, for certain tax years. The Board also denied the taxpayer's request for relief from additional tax assessments. The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed the Board's order. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board found that the taxpayer, a domestic life insurance company, was at fault for failing to report the underlying details of its separate accounts account and for failing to include applicable items in its Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.320 filings. The primary issues were (1) whether the value of the taxpayer's investment corporate stock was erroneously treated in the computation of the taxpayer's tax liability under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.320 for certain years, and (2) whether assets booked as separate accounts were properly subjected to taxation during certain years. On appeal, the court found that the computation method used followed the procedures in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.020. Moreover, the taxpayer reported the grand total of the separate accounts account in its filings, but failed to file the supporting subaccounts which would have disclosed that items booked to the account were taxable. Taxable items were not listed for Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.320 taxation purposes. Thus, the separate accounts account for the periods in question qualified as omitted under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 132.290, and the retroactivity provisions of the statute were properly applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE W. DOUGLAS KEMPER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-XX-000021.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING IN PART, VACATING IN PART, AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bingo facilities filed complaints against appellee health department in the district court for review of a citation and penalty imposed for violation of a Smoke Free Law, Louisville, Ky., Metro Ordinance No. 123-2005. The complaints were consolidated. The district court ruled that the facilities were exempt from the Smoke Free Law. The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) reversed and remanded the judgment. The facilities appealed.


OVERVIEW: The facilities, which were rented by charitable organizations, challenged the constitutionality of an ordinance which allowed for appeals to the district court. The facilities argued that the district court had no appellate jurisdiction. The facilities also argued that the circuit court improperly held that the district court's review was limited to a determination as to whether a decision by a code enforcement board was based upon substantial evidence of record, rather than a de novo review. On appeal, the court found that the circuit court erred when it held that the district court could only review the board's action for arbitrariness under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 65.8831. Because the district court did not have appellate jurisdiction, the district court was to conduct a de novo review of the record created before the code enforcement board and was not confined to a determination as to whether the board's decision was arbitrary. Finally, the circuit court was to address whether the district court's finding that the private organization exemption applied to the facilities was correct based upon a review of the code enforcement board's record.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was reversed in part as to the applicable standard of review of the district court's decision, was vacated in part as to the circuit court's reversal of the district court's decision regarding the general applicability of the Smoke Free Law to the charitable organizations that rented the facilities. The matter was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Commonwealth v. Chauvin


NO. 2008-CA-000027-OA


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 190



June 13, 2008, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS. TO BE PUBLISHED. [UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Chauvin, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 146 (Ky., June 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
ORIGINAL ACTION REGARDING JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 06-CI-009152.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Commonwealth of Kentucky, Cabinet for Health and Family Services (Cabinet), petitioned for writs of prohibition and mandamus to direct respondent Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) to vacate its order requiring counsel for defendant below to produce information concerning plaintiff below's prescription drug history contained in the Kentucky All-Schedule Prescription Electronic Reporting (KASPER) records.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.202(6), as amended in 2007, which prohibited the release of KASPER documents for any discovery or evidentiary purposes in civil actions, conflicted with Ky. R. Civ. P. 26.02(1). The Kentucky legislature did not create a privilege when it made KASPER records confidential. The conflict implicated the separation of powers doctrine. The portion of § 218A.202(6) that precluded the release of KASPER records for discovery purposes was unconstitutional as it articulated a rule of practice that purported to control a responsibility assigned by the Kentucky Constitution to the Kentucky Judicial Branch. As KASPER records were confidential, it was error to order that they be produced solely based on a determination that the arguments of defendant's counsel provided good cause for the relief requested. After a preliminary showing of good cause, the KASPER records were to be produced under seal to the trial court for an in camera review so it could decide what portion of the records, if any, satisfied the relevancy requirement of Rule 26.02(1). Any ordered release of KASPER records was to be conditioned upon a confidentiality provision.


OUTCOME: The relief sought was denied to the extent that it asked that the order for the release of plaintiff's KASPER records be vacated. The trial court was directed to issue an amended order requiring that the records be produced to the trial court under seal and for an in camera review to determine what portion of those records, if any, was relevant to the matter at issue and could be released. To that extent, the original action was granted.

St. Luke Hosps., Inc. v. Commonwealth


NO. 2007-CA-001092-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


254 S.W.3d 830; 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 146

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 26, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS D. WINGATE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CI-00367.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted summary judgment dismissing a declaratory judgment action filed by appellant hospital, in which it claimed that the two-hospital limitation and the thirty-minute requirement imposed by appellee, the Cabinet for Health and Family Services (Cabinet) issued under the 2004-2006 State Health Plan pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 194A.010, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the instant court found that the hospital raised a constitutional issue and had standing to challenge the selection criteria under the 2004-2006 State Health Plan, it first held that the selection criteria promulgated by the Cabinet did not constitute special or local legislation, as the classification was reasonable, natural, and consistent with the legitimate purpose of the government. Second, the Cabinet's regulation did not arbitrarily discriminate against urban hospitals in violation of Ky. Const. §§ 2 and 3, as the Cabinet held a lengthy review process and considered numerous factors when drafting the regulation, and it was clear the Cabinet limited participation in the project to minimize exposure to the inherent risks. Likewise, in the interest of public health, it was reasonable for the Cabinet to study the feasibility of expanding emergency cardiac services to rural areas. As a result, the regulation survived a rational basis scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted appellees, a county metro revenue commission, a metro government, a city transit authority, and a county board of education, summary judgment in the taxpayer's declaratory judgment action seeking a refund for the overpayment of occupational taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed tax returns based upon incorrect calculations. The commission issued the taxpayer a refund. The taxpayer sought an additional refund, which the commission did not approve based upon City of Louisville, Kentucky, General Codified Ordinances § 112.20 and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 160.487. The appellate court held that there was nothing inherent in either the occupational tax ordinance or the statute that violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. The commission did not collect or fail to apportion what was appropriately due. The taxpayer misconstrued its obligations under the ordinance and statute. The occupational tax was authorized by both statute and ordinance. Because there was no possible penalty related to a failure to make the excess payment of the occupational tax, the taxpayer voluntarily paid the amount in dispute. There was nothing in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 96A that would make it a special or local act violative of the Ky. Const. § 59.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's ruling that the taxpayer was not entitled to any additional refund of the taxes it voluntarily overpaid.

Horn v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-002386-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


240 S.W.3d 665; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 430



November 9, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 8, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM GRAYSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SAM H. MONARCH, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CR-00171.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Grayson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted him of manufacturing methamphetamine, in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1432(1)(b), and possession of anhydrous ammonia in an unapproved container with the intent to manufacture methamphetamine. The trial court had denied defendant's suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: Individuals who were questioned by officers on a narcotics task force about their purchase of items commonly used to manufacture methamphetamine indicated that they were delivering the items to defendant. The two men cooperated in an undercover operation targeted at defendant, whereupon the items were delivered to him. Defendant failed to open the door when police approached, and the police forcibly entered the building because they believed that the evidence was being destroyed. Defendant refused to consent to a search, which was eventually conducted after a search warrant was obtained. The trial court denied suppression of evidence seized and defendant entered a conditional guilty plea. On appeal, the court found no error in the denial of suppression. Although the trial court had determined that the forcible entry was illegal, the warrant constituted an independent source that was sufficiently distinguishable, such that the forced entry was purged of its illegality. Accordingly, the exclusionary rule was not applicable in the circumstances. The search warrant was valid and it was based on a sufficient and truthful affidavit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

J.M.R. v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-002608-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


239 S.W.3d 116; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 407



October 26, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DOLLY W. BERRY, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-AD-500222.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed two judgments entered by the Jefferson Family Court (Kentucky), which terminated her parental rights to her two infant children.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the children's therapists testified to the children's statements that they feared their stepfather would harm them in the future and that they did not want to reunify with their mother because of her inability or unwillingness to leave their stepfather. The statements fell within the Ky. R. Evid. 803(4) hearsay exception as they were made to the therapists in order to receive medical treatment. The mother's due process rights were not violated even though the children did not testify. The ramifications of the children's testimony was considered, and it was not in their best interests to testify. Moreover, the mother had had the opportunity to question the children during an in camera interview. There was substantial evidence that the mother had failed to provide the necessary food, clothing, shelter, medical care, or education for her children. The mother had not paid any child support in five months, and still resided in the stepfather's house. The stepfather paid the bills. Finally, termination of the mother's parental rights was proper under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 625.090(2)(c) as the mother abused her children or allowed them to be abused.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Boyle v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-000761-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


245 S.W.3d 219; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 411



October 26, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 10, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Boyle v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 61 (Ky. Ct. App., Jan. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM LINCOLN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DAVID TAPP, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-XX-00001.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Lincoln Circuit Court (Kentucky), pursuant to a conditional guilty plea, of driving under the influence of alcohol, following the denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove his unmarked pick-up truck after midnight with a single orange, road-construction barrel in its bed. The appellate court held that as a matter of ordinary human experience the increasingly ubiquitous orange, road-construction barrels were ordinarily transported during daylight hours, in bunches, by marked construction or government vehicles. Thus, at the time of an investigatory stop leading to defendant's arrest and guilty plea, there was a reasonable and articulable suspicion that defendant was in possession of a stolen barrel. Even though the barrel was later shown to have been borrowed, the investigatory stop was not unconstitutional or improper. But for defendant's palpable intoxication, the stop would have been momentary and therefore not a significant violation of defendant's privacy interests when compared to the Commonwealth's significant interest in investigating possible criminal activity. The denial of the suppression motion was proper.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

Cam I, Inc. v. Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't


NO. 2005-CA-000085-MR; NO. 2005-CA-000090-MR; NO. 2005-CA-000091-MR; NO. 2005-CA-000092-MR; NO. 2005-CA-000100-MR; NO. 2005-CA-000113-MR; AND NO. 2005-CA-000176-MR

[UNLESS OTHERWISE ORDERED BY THE KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, OPINIONS DESIGNATED "TO BE PUBLISHED" BY THE COURT OF APPEALS ARE NOT TO BE PUBLISHED IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS PENDING, IF DISCRETIONARY REVIEW IS GRANTED, OR IF ORDERED NOT TO BE PUBLISHED BY THE COURT WHEN DENYING THE MOTION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW OR GRANTING WITHDRAWAL OF THE MOTION.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified October 19, 2007.
Review granted by Cam I, Inc. v. Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 86 (Ky., Apr. 16, 2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by, Sub nomine at Blue Movies, Inc. v. Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't, 2010 Ky. LEXIS 101 (Ky., Apr. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEALS AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE STEPHEN P. RYAN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CI-001967.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, several entities engaged in various adult entertainment or sexually oriented businesses, appealed the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which upheld the constitutionality of an ordinance of appellee municipality restricting the operation of appellants' businesses. Appellee cross-appealed the order and judgment granting appellants' motion for a temporary injunction, in part.


OVERVIEW: Appellants had brought suit challenging the ordinance on numerous state constitutional grounds and moved the trial court for a temporary restraining order and a temporary injunction enjoining appellee from enforcing or implementing the ordinance. On the day the complaint was filed, the trial court entered an order granting temporary injunctive relief enjoining appellee from enforcing the ordinance pending further orders of the court. The court rejected appellants' assertion to the contrary and held that Ky. Const. §§ 1 and 8 granted no greater protection to free speech and free expression than the United States Constitution. Because the purpose of the ordinance was to regulate the secondary effects associated with the businesses, and not the message allegedly conveyed therein, the court applied an intermediate standard of scrutiny. As such, the court determined the ordinance was content neutral and did not relate to the suppression of free speech. The court upheld the restrictions set forth in the ordinance prohibiting nudity, restricting the hours of operation, prohibiting alcohol sales, imposing staging requirements, etc., as within appellee's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court upholding the constitutionality of the ordinance. As to the appeal, the court affirmed the judgment as to appellants and reversed the judgment of the trial court with regard to appellee's cross-appeal.

 

492 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Perkins v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-000934-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


237 S.W.3d 215; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 374



October 5, 2007, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM KNOTT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOSEPH F. BAMBERGER, SPECIAL JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CR-00118.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Knott Circuit Court (Kentucky) of possession of a controlled substance (a lesser-included offense of a trafficking count), possession of a controlled substance, possession of drug paraphernalia, and possession of marijuana, following the denial of his motion to suppress. Defendant was sentenced to five years of imprisonment. Defendant's post-trial motions were denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that all evidence from a knock and talk should have been suppressed. The appellate court held that defendant's 15- or 16-year-old son consented to the entry into the house. The consent was voluntary and it was reasonable for the officers to believe that the son had the apparent authority to consent to their entry. Defendant voluntarily admitted to the officers that he possessed illegal substances, and voluntarily consented to a search of his person and of his bedroom. The son was old enough to consent to the entry. The officers made no effort to coerce or to deceive the son into granting them entry. The entry of the officers into defendant's bedroom did not exceed the son's consent. Probable cause was not so clearly established as to preclude the reasonableness of a knock and search visit. Defendant did not preserve his claim of error as to the chain of custody. Finally, a jury reasonably might have found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance instead of trafficking in a controlled substance. While the trial court was not obligated to tender a possession instruction in the face of an objection by defendant, its decision to do so was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

494 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Sims v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-001369-MR, NO. 2006-CA-001528-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


233 S.W.3d 731; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 327



September 7, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CRAIG Z. CLYMER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 94-CR-00100



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a plea agreement, appellant pled guilty to murder and was sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of parole for 25 years. Later, appellant filed a motion against appellee Commonwealth, seeking a new sentencing hearing pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02(e), (f), and Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42. The McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied the motion. Appellate sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged as an adult for a murder committed when he was 16 years old. Initially, the Commonwealth sought the death penalty, but as a result of negotiations, appellant pled guilty to murder and was sentenced to life without parole for 25 years. Later, the United States Supreme Court decided that someone under 18 when he committed murder was not subject to the death penalty. On the basis of this, appellant sought a new sentencing hearing. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the motion was untimely under Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42(10). The constitutional right established in the United States Supreme Court's decision was not that an accused might escape a life sentence, and indeed, the opinion contained dictum to the effect that life imprisonment without parole remained a permissible sentence. Although that decision was to have been given retroactive application in all those cases in which a sentence of death was imposed on an accused who was under the age of 18 when he committed the crime, this was not such a case. Appellant did not claim that his plea was not knowing, voluntary, and intelligent when it was made.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

495 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Galloway v. Fletcher


NO. 2006-CA-002428-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


241 S.W.3d 819; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 324



August 31, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 23, 2008.
Review denied by Galloway v. Fletcher, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 696 (Ky., Jan. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS D WINGATE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 06-CI-01074.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, unsuccessful nominees for a vacancy on a state university board of regents, sought review of a decision entered by the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by appellees, the governor, the nominating committee members, and the state university, in the unsuccessful nominees' action requesting a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Two lists of nominees for the vacancy had been submitted to the governor by the committee; both lists were rejected. The governor chose a nominee from the third list submitted. The unsuccessful nominees had been named on the first rejected list. The court concluded in its threshold inquiry that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12.070(3) applied to the governor's appointment of members of the state university's board of regents because the phrase "administrative boards and commissions," while not defined in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12.010, could be construed pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 446.080 to include governing bodies of state universities. While Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 164.005(5)(a), which specifically applied to the appointment of board of regents members, could be interpreted to required the governor to make such an appointment from the first list of nominees, such a construction would require the first sentence of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12.070(3) to be given no effect, and, thus, the governor properly made an appointment from the third list submitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.


 

496 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Morton v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-001756-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


232 S.W.3d 566; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 302



August 24, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 4, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM MASON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOHN W. MCNEILL III, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CR-00099.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Mason Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied defendant's motion to suppress drug evidence, he entered a conditional guilty plea to possession of a controlled substance in the first degree. He then appealed the denial of his suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant's car for weaving. He approached defendant's car with his drug-sniffing dog. After the dog alerted to the trunk and the driver's side door, the officer asked for permission to search the car; defendant refused. The officer patted him down and found cocaine inside a folded 10-dollar bill in defendant's pocket. Defendant alleged the drug was the fruit of an unlawful search in violation of the Fourth Amendment. He argued that the search of car, but not his person, was authorized under the automobile exception. The appellate court disagreed. As defendant was the driver and lone occupant of a car, the dog's alert to the presence of drugs inside the car gave officer the authority to search defendant drugs. Defendant argued that as the officer claimed he searched him for weapons, and did not believe that the folded money was contraband, the search could not be validated under the "plain feel" exception. The appellate court held that the test was not whether the officer's subjective belief was constitutionally adequate to support his action but whether the facts known to him could validate his actions under any permissible constitutional standard.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Simmons v. Commonwealth


NO. 2004-CA-002527-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


232 S.W.3d 531; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 292



August 17, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 1, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CI-0774.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order from the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed his petition for a declaration of rights and permanent injunctive relief and granted summary judgment to appellee Kentucky Parole Board in the inmate's action, alleging that the Board's order to serve out his time violated the administrative regulation in effect at the time that the murders, for which he was convicted, were committed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a guilty plea to two counts of murder, in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 507.020, arising from the death of his wife and her boyfriend, and two concurrent life sentences were imposed with parole eligibility. The inmate was denied parole on two occasions, with the Board directing the inmate to serve out his life sentences on the latter denial. The inmate filed his petition, alleging that the Board's issuance of the serve-out order violated 501 Ky. Admin. Regs. 1:011 (1983). The trial court agreed with the Board that no violation had occurred, and it granted summary judgment to the Board and dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court initially noted that dismissal was not warranted for the inmate's technical violation of Ky. R. Civ. P. 76.12(4)(c)(v). The court found that although the Board issued its serve-out order based on 501 Ky. Admin. Regs. 1:030(3)(f) (2003), there was no ex post facto violation because there was no enhancement of punishment or elongation of the inmate's sentence. The Board did not exceed its authority under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13A.130 with respect to the separation of powers doctrine under Ky. Const. §§ 27 and 28.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Atkins v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-000285-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 285



August 17, 2007, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied and ordered not published by Atkins v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 257 (Ky., Nov. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM SCOTT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROBERT G. JOHNSON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-CR-00010.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prior to entering a guilty plea, defendant filed a motion challenging the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.500 and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.510. The Scott Circuit Court (Kentucky), in a summary order, found that the challenged statutes were constitutional. Defendant appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 218A.500 and 218A.510 were vague and overbroad. The overbreadth argument was that the statutes criminalized the possession of items, such as rolling papers, that may have had both legal and illegal uses. The appellate court held that defendant was correct that the items he had in his possession, including rolling papers, a rolling machine, scissors, and a water bong, could all have legal uses. However, when viewed in the context of his arrest, including the fact that defendant's van had an odor of marijuana smoke, defendant admitted that he had recently been smoking marijuana, and defendant's prior conviction for possession of both marijuana and paraphernalia, clearly provided a context within Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.510 to support the citation for possession of paraphernalia. Therefore, as applied to defendant, the statutes were not overbroad. As to the claim of vagueness, the appellate court held that the statutes clearly gave a person of common intelligence notice of what was unlawful under the statutes. Thus, the appellate court held that the trial court properly found that the statutes were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gussler v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-000754-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


236 S.W.3d 22; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 225



July 20, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 13, 2007.
Review denied by Gussler v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 397 (Ky., Oct. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM LAWRENCE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DANIEL SPARKS, JUDGE. ACTION NOS. 86-CR-00062 AND 86-CR-00063.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pled guilty to murder, kidnapping, second degree burglary, first degree arson, second degree arson, theft by unlawful taking over $ 100, and first degree robbery. Later, appellant filed Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42 and Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02 motions against appellee State, requesting a new sentencing hearing. The Lawrence Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied the motions. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought relief based on a recent United States Supreme Court decision which found death sentences for juveniles between the ages of 15 and 18 were unconstitutional. However, the appellate court found that this holding did not affect the imposition of a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility for parole for a minimum of 25 years, which was the sentence imposed in this case. Appellant argued that the Commonwealth's offer to recommend a sentence less than death had become meaningless as such sentences were now forbidden. The appellate court disagreed. Appellant knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently entered into the plea agreement in order to receive what was then, and was still, a constitutionally valid sentence for his multiple crimes. The mere fact the law had changed such as to lower the ceiling of possible sentences did not deprive him of the benefit he received from his bargain.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Allen v. Woodford County Bd. of Adjustments


NO. 2006-CA-000603-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


228 S.W.3d 573; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 190



June 29, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified July 13, 2007. Released for Publication August 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM WOODFORD CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROBERT G. JOHNSON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CI-00177.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision of appellee board, which granted an owner's application for a conditional use permit. The Woodford Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed the decision. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The owner filed an application with the board seeking a conditional use permit to allow a "tourist home" on the property. Appellants first argued the board acted arbitrarily when it relied upon the definition of a tourist home supplied by the board's zoning compliance officer. Appellants admittedly became aware of the zoning compliance officer's recommended interpretation of the term "tourist home" at an earlier hearing. Appellants did not appeal the officer's actions to the board. The appellate court held that appellants' attempt to have the trial court and the appellate court review the officer's interpretation was untimely. That interpretation stood. Appellants also argued that the board's decision to grant the conditional use permit was an unconstitutional exercise of arbitrary power. However, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 100.237 gave the board the power to grant conditional use permits. Woodford County, Kentucky, Zoning Regulations, art. VII, § 701.4 specifically named "Tourist Home along State or Federal Highway" as a conditional use in the A-1 zone. Appellants failed to meet their burden of persuading the appellate court that the board acted outside its regulatory authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Wood


NO. 2006-CA-000854-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


230 S.W.3d 331; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 185



June 22, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication September 4, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM GARRARD CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE C. HUNTER DAUGHERTY, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 02-CR-00009.
Wood v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 127 (Ky. Ct. App., June 4, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth of Kentucky appealed an order of the Garrard Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted appellee inmate relief pursuant to Ky. R. Crim. P. 11.42. The inmate was serving a sentence on a first-degree rape charge.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sought relief under Rule 11.42, alleging juror misconduct and ineffective assistance of counsel. The trial court granted relief after hearing testimony from a juror in the case that established that the jury had consulted a dictionary during deliberations for the definition of the word rape. On appeal, the Commonwealth argued that the trial court improperly heard testimony from the juror under Ky. R. Crim. P. 10.04. The appellate court affirmed, holding that 1) contrary to the restrictions in Rule 10.04, overt acts of misconduct by jurors could be considered by a trial court dealing with allegations of juror misconduct; 2) using a dictionary to look up the meaning of "rape" was an overt act; 3) the inmate was clearly prejudiced by the juror misconduct as the dictionary definition did not require penetration while penetration was a required element in Kentucky's rape statutes; and 4) as the trial court did not err in granting the inmate relief, there was no need to address his ineffective assistance of counsel claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

502 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Holloway


NO. 2005-CA-000829-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


225 S.W.3d 404; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 161



May 25, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, (July 9, 2007). Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered to be Published.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JAMES D. ISHMAEL, JR, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 96-CR-00729.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth of Kentucky appealed after the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted appellee former arrestee's Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 431.076 petition for the expungement of all records concerning a 1996 case.


OVERVIEW: A grand jury returned a "No True Bill" when presented with various felony and misdemeanor theft charges against appellee. The charges were dismissed without prejudice to refiling. Recognizing that § 431.076 did not facially apply when charges were dismissed without prejudice, the trial court granted the petition, stating that it was exercising the sound discretion and inherent power of the trial court to fairly administer justice. The appellate court reversed, finding that there was no justification for expungement under the law. The words of § 431.076 were clear and unambiguous. They plainly stated that records could be expunged when there was a verdict of not guilty or when a case was dismissed with prejudice. The state legislature intentionally put the words "with prejudice" in the statute. Reading the statute to also include instances where a case was dismissed without prejudice would disregard the plain language of the statute. The appellate court noted that case law indicated that courts had inherent power to expunge records in instances in which there was no statutory authority, however, those instances were extremely limited and did not apply in appellee's case.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed.

 

503 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Cundiff


NO. 2005-CA-002536-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


245 S.W.3d 786; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 143



May 11, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 18, 2008.
Review denied by Miller v. Cundiff, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 391 (Ky., Mar. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM PULASKI CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JEFFREY T. BURDETTE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CI-00443.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenant sued appellee landlords, seeking damages for personal injuries suffered at her apartment under the Uniform Residential Landlord Tenant Act (URLTA), Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 383.500 et seq. The Pulaski Circuit Court (Kentucky) entered summary judgment dismissing the claim. The tenant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tenant tripped and fell over a three-inch gap in the carpet at the apartment. The gap was present when the tenant moved into the apartment. The tenant admitted that she noticed the condition when she first walked through the apartment, and she stated that she asked the landlords to repair the carpet. The tenant stated that she made several additional requests for repairs over the next 10 weeks. The landlords denied receiving any such requests from the tenant. The trial court concluded that the URLTA did not alter the common-law rule that a lessor had no duty to repair leased premises in the absence of an agreement to do so. The landlords were not liable for injuries caused by breach of any covenant to make repairs to the leased premises. Rather, the remedy for breach of an agreement to repair was the cost of repair. Even if the alleged oral representations could have imposed such a duty on the landlords, the tenant was still not entitled to recover damages for her injuries.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

504 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Layton v. Commonwealth


NO. 2004-CA-002309-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 134



May 4, 2007, Rendered


NOTICE:

PLEASE REFER TO THE KENTUCKY RULES REGARDING FINALITY OF OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied and ordered not published by Layton v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 45 (Ky., Jan. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM BALLARD CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. SHADOAN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CR-00005.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND VACATING AND REMANDING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress was denied, defendant was convicted of facilitation of the manufacture of methamphetamine (Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 506.080), complicity, and engaging in organized crime (Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 506.120). The Ballard Circuit Court (Kentucky) followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced him to 10 years' imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and four others manufactured methamphetamine at two houses. He claimed manufacturing methamphetamine was not a predicate offense for the organized crime charge. The appellate court disagreed; illegal trafficking was part of the definition of "criminal syndicate" under § 506.120(3)(e), and under § 506.120(1)(b), one engaged in organized crime by providing material aid to maintain the syndicate. His conviction of facilitation of the manufacture of methamphetamine and of being an accomplice in a criminal syndicate did not violate the double jeopardy ban, since each offense required proof of a fact that the other did not. The amendment of the indictment was proper under Ky. R. Crim. P. 6.16, as no new offense was charged and defendant was not prejudiced. The evidence was sufficient to prove defendant facilitated the manufacture of methamphetamine. The searches of both houses were constitutional. Defendant's request under Ky. R. Evid. 615 to separate witnesses was untimely. Before considering probation, the trial court stated it would follow the jury's sentencing recommendation; it thus failed to give proper consideration to probation under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 533.010(2).


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated and remanded the judgment of the trial court for consideration of probation and resentencing in compliance with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 533.010(2). It affirmed as to all remaining issues.

 

505 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Boone v. Ballinger


NO. 2006-CA-001257-ME AND NO. 2006-CA-001287-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


228 S.W.3d 1; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 133



May 4, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication August 8, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Boone v. Ballinger, 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 209 (Ky. Ct. App., July 6, 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSING AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kenton Circuit Court (Kentucky) determined that appellee ex-husband had been a devoted father to two girls, performing the majority of the everyday tasks related to their upbringing and essentially serving as their primary parent. Thus, it concluded that he was the de facto custodian and that appellant biological father and the mother were estopped from denying that he was the legal father. The biological father and mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: Several months into dissolution proceedings, the ex-husband learned for the first time that the two youngest children born during his 15-year marriage to the mother were not his biological daughters. The mother had been having an extra-marital affair with the biological father. The mother and biological father realized that he was possibly the children's father, but they had no tests done until the dissolution proceedings. The appellate court held that while the ex-husband did not qualify for de facto custodian status under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.270, the biological father's conduct might preclude him from displacing the ex-husband altogether in the girls' lives as Kentucky recognized the applicability of the doctrine of waiver in a child custody dispute. The doctrine of paternity by estoppel did not apply so as to estop the biological father and mother from seeking a paternity determination. Finally, as to the mother's 401(k) retirement account, the trial court erred in deeming it marital property without considering Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.190(4).


OUTCOME: The portion of the trial court's judgment dismissing the biological father's petition for custody or visitation was reversed and remanded for the trial court to address whether he had waived the typically superior custody rights of a biological father. The trial court's original property supplemental decree was reversed to the extent that the mother's 401(k) retirement account was not exempted from property division.

 

506 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Turner v. Perry County Coal Corp.


NO. 2006-CA-001019-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


242 S.W.3d 658; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 96



April 6, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 20, 2008.
Review denied by Turner v. Perry County Coal Corp., 2008 Ky. LEXIS 439 (Ky., Feb. 13, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Turner v. Perry County Coal Corp., 555 U.S. 818, 129 S. Ct. 80, 172 L. Ed. 2d 29, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6840 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM PERRY CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM ENGLE III, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CI-00448.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant daughter sought review of an order of the Perry Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted summary judgment on the issue of whether the daughter had an ownership interest in real property. Appellees were the buyer of several undivided interests in property from a decedent's estate and the possessor of the property. The buyer had instituted the action, seeking a partition of the property.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was the illegitimate child of the decedent. She claimed sole ownership of the property in question as the decedent's only heir-at-law. The appellate court affirmed. The daughter had no claim to the property. At the time of his death in 1962, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 391.090(2) governed the intestate succession of the decedent's property. Under that statute, illegitimate children could recover only from their mother's estates. Although the statute was struck down in 1977 as unconstitutional, the Kentucky Supreme Court specifically stated that its opinion finding the statute invalid would not be applied retroactively. Thus, upon his death on December 29, 1962, the decedent's property passed to his heirs-at-law under the then-existing laws of intestate succession. Those heirs were identified in a May 1967 affidavit of descent filed by one of the decedent's second cousins.


OUTCOME: The trial court was affirmed.


 

507 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Hallum v. Commonwealth


NO. 2006-CA-000387-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


219 S.W.3d 216; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 89



March 23, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication May 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM HOPKINS CIRCUIT COURT HONORABLE CHARLES W. BOTELER, JR., JUDGE ACTION NOS. 03-CR-00053, 04-CR-00091, & 05-CR-00154.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Hopkins Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied his motion to suppress evidence, appellant was convicted by a jury of first-degree possession of a controlled substance (methamphetamine), possession of marijuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, and unlawful possession of precursors to manufacture methamphetamine. Appellant challenged the judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: The evidence was discovered by deputies who had accompanied a child protective services investigator during a mandatory investigation pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 620.040(1). Appellant did not dispute that he gave the deputies and investigator consent to enter his house. When the investigator entered the closed bedroom to investigate the referral she had received regarding the possible neglect of children, it was not unreasonable for the deputies to also enter the room because the visit was not criminal in nature. Thus, the deputies did not need to receive appellant's consent to enter the bedroom. Even if it was unreasonable to enter the bedroom, exigent circumstances existed where the deputies entered the bedroom with the investigator after she informed appellant she was required to look in that room. Moreover, the deputies had obtained a search warrant after observing drug manufacturing evidence in plain view in the bedroom. The evidence discovered in the kitchen was also properly seized where a deputy was lawfully in the kitchen to get a drink for a child and the evidence was in plain view.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

VanWinkle v. Petry


NO. 2006-CA-000066-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


217 S.W.3d 252; 2007 Ky. App. LEXIS 18



January 19, 2007, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 10, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MADISON FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE JEAN CHENAULT LOGUE, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 02-CI-01175.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND VACATING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee maternal grandparents filed an ex parte motion seeking custody of their grandchildren. The Madison Family Court (Kentucky) ordered that the grandparents had to agree with appellant mother's visitation with her children and sua sponte modified the grandparents' visitation by giving them an extra weekend of visitation each month. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents entered into an agreed order under which they had joint custody and the grandparents had visitation of one weekend per month. In their multiple court filings, the grandparents never alleged that the mother and father were unfit; that the children were dependent, neglected or abused; or that the grandparents were acting as de facto custodians. The appellate court held that awarding the grandparents additional visitation was error, as they had not sought such relief under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021, the trial court did not find that additional visitation would be in the children's best interest, nor did it consider the Vibbert factors. The only right the grandparents had regarding the children involved visitation. By filing ex parte motions seeking custody when they disagreed with the parents' decisions, they unduly interfered with the parents' constitutionally protected rights to make decisions for their children. However, since the grandparents had been granted visitation pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021, they remained parties to the action to that extent; therefore, the appellate court denied the mother's request to dismiss them from the dissolution action.


OUTCOME: The orders awarding additional visitation to the grandparents and requiring their approval of any changes regarding the mother's time with the children were vacated. The remainder of the order was affirmed.

 

509 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Bess v. Bracken County Fiscal Court


NO. 2005-CA-000541-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


210 S.W.3d 177; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 347



December 1, 2006, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM BRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOHN W. MCNEILL, III, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CI-00112.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants filed suit challenging Bracken County, Ky., Ordinance §§ 53.91 and 53.92, enacted by appellee, the Bracken County, Kentucky, Fiscal Court. These ordinances banned pit bull terriers and provided penalties for persons who owned them; appellants alleged they were inconsistent with Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 258.095's definition of "vicious dog." The Bracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) dismissed the complaint; appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that under its police powers, the fiscal court could ban pit bull terriers and take them without compensation. The appellate court agreed. The ordinance was supplemental to, not inconsistent with, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 258, which banned vicious dogs generally, as it did not limit ch. 258's application but provided more comprehensive protection. The fiscal court's determination that pit bull terriers had "inherently vicious and dangerous propensities" was reasonable, given the evidence to support that finding. As the forfeiture and destruction of such dogs was pursuant to a valid exercise of the police power, no compensation was due to their owners. The ordinance gave an owner the opportunity to appear in court and present evidence and defenses to the action; therefore, procedural due process was afforded. The right to travel guaranteed by the Equal Protection and Privileges and Immunities Clauses of the U.S. Constitution did not require that when traveling to another jurisdiction, a person had to be given benefits that were superior to those enjoyed by the jurisdiction's own residents simply because the traveler enjoyed those benefits in another place.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

K.R.L. v. P.A.C.


NO. 2006-CA-000364-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


210 S.W.3d 183; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 349



December 1, 2006, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM BELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JAMES L. BOWLING, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 05-AD-00009.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 625.090, appellant mother filed a petition for involuntary termination of appellee father's parental rights with respect to appellee child. The Bell Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied the petition; the mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother alleged the father had severely beaten her and had held her and the child hostage; that he failed to pay child support; and had abandoned his child for nearly two years. The father admitted fighting with the mother, but denied the severity of the assault. He admitted failing to pay child support, but alleged he was prevented from seeing his son due to a protective order the mother had obtained. The appellate court initially held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 625.110, which allowed appeals only from an order granting a termination petition, was unconstitutional because it violated the mother's right to appeal guaranteed by Ky. Const. § 115. Therefore, she had standing to appeal the order denying her termination petition. However, she had presented no evidence to support a finding that termination of the father's parental rights was in the child's best interest. Because the evidence did not compel a finding that the father's parental rights should have been terminated under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 625.090(1), the trial court's decision was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

King v. Campbell County


NO. 2005-CA-001841-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


217 S.W.3d 862; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 331



November 3, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication April 18, 2007.
Review denied by King v. Campbell County, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 522 (Ky., Apr. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JULIE REINHARDT WARD, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 05-CI-00332.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed the taxpayer's complaint against appellee county, challenging a county occupational license fee ordinance adopted pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 68.197, as amended. The trial court found that the amendment to § 68.197 and the fee ordinance were both constitutionally valid.


OVERVIEW: The fee ordinance was first authorized in a public question approved by the voters pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 120.250 to fund traffic improvement and mass transportation projects. On review, the court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayer's challenge. The ballot question met the requirements of § 120.250 and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 83A.120, and the court found that the taxpayer's challenge was untimely under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 120.250. The court also found that the constitutional challenges had no merit. Although Ky. Const. § 59 prohibited local or special acts, there were distinctive and natural reasons setting those counties whose license fees were authorized by public question apart from other counties such that a legitimate legislative purpose to relieve threatened fiscal hardship was served by requiring latter counties to credit license fees but relieving the former from that requirement. The application of the amendment to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 68.197 retroactively did not violate due process because the amendment did not withdraw a provision upon which taxpayers had relied but merely sought to clarify the license fee credit provision in the wake of a court opinion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the taxpayer's complaint.
