Kimbrough v. Child Support Div. ex rel. Belmar


NO. 2005-CA-001532-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


215 S.W.3d 69; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 226



July 21, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication March 20, 2007.
Review denied by Kimbrough v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 71 (Ky., Mar. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE JOAN L. BYER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 95-FC-002095.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order of the Jefferson Family Court (Kentucky), which denied the father's motion to set aside a prior order that granted the motion of appellee mother for an increase in child support. The father contended that the calculations made pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.212(2)(g)(4) violated the father's equal protection and due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a motion to increase the child support obligation for the father's two children and the trial court granted the motion. In a motion to set aside or modify the order, the father challenged the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.212(2)(g)(4). Pursuant to § 403.212(2)(g)(4) the mother's gross income was reduced by a deduction of imputed child support because of the mother's prior-born child. the father was not permitted to make a similar deduction on his income calculation for an after-born child. The court held that § 403.212(2)(g)(4) did not violate the father's equal protection rights because the state had an interest in seeing that the prior-born child was provided for and § 403.212(2)(g)(4) was rationally related to that state interest. The trial court had discretion, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.211(2) and (3) to take into account extraordinary circumstances, including the impact of the child support obligation on after-born children. The father did not provide sufficient evidence to support his assertion that his due process rights were violated because the father of the prior-born child was not paying his child support obligation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Cherry v. Augustus


NO. 2004-CA-001496-MR AND NO. 2004-CA-001730-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


245 S.W.3d 766; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 205



July 7, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 18, 2008.
Review denied by Cherry v. Augustus, 2008 Ky. LEXIS 407 (Ky., Mar. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
2004-CA-001496-MR. APPEAL FROM McCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TOMMY W. CHANDLER, SPECIAL JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 01-CI-00370.

2004-CA-001730-MR. CROSS-APPEAL FROM McCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TOMMY W. CHANDLER, SPECIAL JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 01-CI-00370.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant/cross-appellee employee sued appellee/cross-appellant sheriff in the McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) to enforce an order of the McCracken County Deputy Sheriff Merit Board calling for the employee to be reinstated as a deputy sheriff with full back pay retroactive to his termination date. The trial court ordered reinstatement and certain back pay, but denied other relief. The employee appealed and the sheriff cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff did not obey the Board's order to reinstate the employee with back pay. The appellate court held the limitations period was tolled by a court order setting aside the Board's order as, until the court order was vacated, there was nothing to enforce. By excluding this time, the enforcement action was not time-barred. Laches did not bar restitution and back pay claims. Vacating the sheriff's request for judicial review for lack of jurisdiction did not deny it as he could have refiled under the saving statute, but did not, so claim preclusion barred his claims. Comparing what the employee would have earned as a deputy sheriff each year of his termination to his actual earnings, rather than comparing his total earnings over the period to what his total earnings as a deputy sheriff would have been, did not abuse discretion. The sheriff's recalcitrance after termination did not bear on the award in a suit to enforce an administrative board's order. Attorney's fees were not recoverable under the merit board statutes, a contract, or quantum meruit. The Board could not award damages for lost opportunity to pursue a law enforcement career or punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Scott v. AEP Ky. Coals, LLC


NO. 2005-CA-002486-WC


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


196 S.W.3d 24; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 189



June 30, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, August 9, 2006. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered to be Published.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] PETITION FOR REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD. ACTION NO. WC-02-02188.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant appealed an opinion of the Workers' Compensation Board (Kentucky), which had found that he could not receive additional benefits upon reopening his claim for worsening of pneumoconiosis because he had no additional exposure to coal dust since filing an earlier petition to reopen. Claimant challenged the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.125(5)(a), and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.316(12), and alleged a mistake.


OVERVIEW: Claimant had previously filed a petition to reopen his claim, and he filed the instant petition thereafter. The Board denied his petition, finding that he had not shown additional exposure to coal dust since filing his earlier petition. Claimant contended that the requirement for an additional exposure was a violation of his due process and equal protection rights, because no such showing was required for other types of claims. The court held that the legislature had a rational basis for requiring additional exposure under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.125(5)(a), and that the doctrine of res judicata also applied. In addition, the court observed that there was a need for finality of decisions and that because § 342.125(5)(a) was more specific than § 342.125(1)(d), its requirement of additional exposure controlled. The court also held that claimant's constitutional challenges were not precluded for failure to exhaust his remedies, because the Board could not pass on the constitutionality of legislation. However, because the Board had not addressed claimant's contention of a mistake in his filing, additional proceedings on that issue were required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the opinion in part, remanding to the Board to determine whether claimant had met the requirements for reopening his claim on the grounds of mistake.

Union Planters Bank, N.A. v. Hutson


NO. 2004-CA-002160-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


210 S.W.3d 163; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 170



June 9, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, (December 4, 2006). Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered to be Published.
Rehearing denied by Union Planters Bank, N.A. v. Hutson, 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 372 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM WHITLEY CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PAUL E. BRADEN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CI-00287.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART AND REVERSING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank (mortgagee) appealed a $ 98,000 judgment entered by the Whitley Circuit Court (Kentucky) for appellee mortgagors under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 382.365 after the mortgagee failed to timely release a mortgage.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagors argued that the mortgagee did not release a mortgage until 234 days after it had notice that the mortgage had been satisfied. The appellate court held that the mortgagors suffered no damages, actual or threatened, due to the delay in releasing the mortgage. A mortgagor's daughter was aware of the penalty and would "normally" follow-up on notice letters if the mortgage was not promptly released, but she did not do so with her mother's mortgage. Receipt of the notice was an element of the cause of action. It was a little unclear whether the trial court found that the mortgagee received the notice, but even if the trial court did not find that the mortgagee received the notice, the findings were sufficient as there was no motion for additional findings. The statute was not unconstitutional under the Due Process Clause and Ky. Const. § 2 as the mortgagors had a duty to act reasonably and in good faith. Further, the mortgagors' rights flowed from a contract, in which there was an implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing. Finally, the exclusion of line of credit and revolving credit plan mortgages from Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 382.365 did not violate Ky. Const. § 59.


OUTCOME: The judgment was set aside. The case was remanded for a new trial as to damages only, with the mortgagors receiving such amounts as accrued under the statute while they were acting in a reasonable manner and in good faith.

Target Oil & Gas Corp. v. Commonwealth


NO. 2004-CA-001947-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 156



May 26, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Rehearing denied by Target Oil & Gas Corp. v. Commonwealth Dep't of Fin. Insts., Div. of Secs., 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 224 (Ky. Ct. App., June 7, 2006)
Review denied by Gas Group, Inc. v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 787 (Ky., Aug. 17, 2006)
Review denied and ordered not published by Target Oil & Gas Corp. v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 47 (Ky., Feb. 14, 2007)
Related proceeding at Target Oil & Gas Corp. v. Commonwealth, 2008 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 812 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-CI-00588.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) ordered appellants, a corporation and its president, to comply with a subpoena duces tecum issued by the director of appellee, the Kentucky Office of Financial Institutions' Division of Securities. In the subpoena, the Division sought financial records, records of the corporation's drilling practices, and a list of all investors and the amount of the interest each held. Appellants challenged the order.


OVERVIEW: The Division was investigating investor complaints against the corporation. The court stated that it had been held by the United States Supreme Court that an administrative subpoena should be enforced if the inquiry was within the authority of the agency, the demand was not too indefinite, and the information sought was reasonably relevant. Here, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 292.460 authorized the director to inquire concerning potential violations of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 292.320, regarding securities fraud. The corporation did not claim that the subpoena was too broad, and the records sought were clearly relevant. The director's authority had not been preempted by the National Security Markets Improvement Act of 1996, 15 U.S.C.S. § 77r. It permitted the states to retain jurisdiction over fraudulent conduct. Under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 292.320, the director's authority was not limited to fraud practiced against Kentucky residents. Finally, an administrative subpoena satisfying the Supreme Court's test did not violate the Fourth Amendment or Ky. Const. § 2, and because the corporation's activities were solely commercial, a demand for a list of investors did not offend the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Dunlap v. Commonwealth


NO. 2004-CA-002058-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 107



April 7, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Rehearing denied by Dunlap v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 371 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 8, 2006)
Review denied by Dunlap v. Commonwealth, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 183 (Ky., Sept. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM CARROLL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE STEPHEN L. BATES, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-XX-00009.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted discretionary review of an order from the Carroll Circuit Court (Kentucky), which affirmed defendant's conditional guilty plea to driving under the influence (DUI) in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.010.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with DUI after a vehicle stop at a seat belt safety roadblock. He filed motions to suppress, arguing the roadblock was unconstitutional and was a violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189.125(7), which precluded officers from stopping cars or citing drivers solely for not wearing a seat belt. He argued that since the initial stop was improper, his arrest was improper. The motions were denied. Defendant pled guilty while reserving his right to appeal that denial. On appeal, the court found that the roadblock was neither constitutionally nor statutorily improper, so the stop of defendant's vehicle and his resulting arrest were proper. While § 189.125(7) prohibited routine traffic stops for a seat belt violation, roadblocks to check for general motor vehicle safety violations were not prohibited. The roadblock: (1) was solely used to promote the state's strong interest in preventing traffic accidents and in promoting highway safety; (2) met nearly every factor in the Kentucky State Police Traffic Safety Checkpoint Policy, which was known as the OM-E-4 guideline; and (3) was minimally intrusive and did not involve an unconstitutional exercise of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for DUI.

 

519 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Fin. & Admin. Cabinet v. Beyer


NO. 2004-CA-002598-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


193 S.W.3d 755; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 152



March 10, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, July 6, 2006. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered to be Published.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JEFFREY HINES, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 04-XX-00016.



DISPOSITION: REVERSING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayers sued appellant Kentucky Finance and Administration Cabinet, Department of Revenue, seeking damages and a declaration that Ky. Rev. Stat. § 138.450(12)(a) and (f) violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and Ky. Const. § 2. The trial court granted the taxpayers summary judgment; the Mccracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed. The Cabinet sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the classifications of "new car purchaser" and "used car purchaser" as established by Ky. Rev. Stat. § 138.450(12)(a) and (f) unreasonably and arbitrarily discriminated between purchasers of new cars and purchasers of used cars without any legitimate governmental purpose in doing so, thereby violating the Equal Protection Clause. The high court disagreed. By this legislation, the general assembly intended to stimulate the used car market in Kentucky, which was a legitimate governmental interest, and the classification was rationally related to that goal. And as § 138.450(12)(a) and (f) furthered a legitimate governmental interest, the distinction between a new car and a used car for the purpose of taxation was not an exercise of arbitrary power over property by the legislature. Accordingly, § 138.450(12)(a) and (f) did not violate Ky. Const. § 2.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Cabinet for Health & Family Servs. ex rel. A.W. v. Huddleston


NO. 2005-CA-000165-ME


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


185 S.W.3d 222; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 47



February 17, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 7, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM WARREN FAMILY COURT. HONORABLE MARGARET RYAN HUDDLESTON, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-J-00778 & 03-J-00929.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART, VACATING IN PART, AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Cabinet for Health and Family Services appealed an order by the Warren Circuit Court, Family Division, (Kentucky) that restricted placement of two children to a specific county; the Cabinet claimed that the family court's restriction on where it could place the children was unduly burdensome on its efforts to reunite the family.


OVERVIEW: When the children were committed to the custody of the Cabinet, appellee mother, who was incarcerated for alcohol-related charges, stipulated to having neglected the children. The children were placed with foster parents in a certain county. After the mother's release from jail, she moved to a different county that was approximately 100 miles away from the children. The family court determined that the children should remain under the Cabinet's care and commitment and that the Cabinet's permanency goal of reunification was in the children's best interests. Nevertheless, it ordered the Cabinet to keep the children's residence in the first county. The appellate court held that pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 610.010(11), the Legislature conferred sole and exclusive authority upon the Cabinet to determine the appropriate placement of the children committed to its care. In addition, Ky. Const. §§ 27, 28 precluded the trial court's exercise of executive powers, such as ordering the placement of children. Therefore, the family court erred in restricting the Cabinet's ability to place the children in a home nearer to their mother.


OUTCOME: The order was vacated as to the limitation of the children's placement, the case was remanded for entry of a corrected order; the order was affirmed in all other respects.

Smith v. Commonwealth


NO. 2004-CA-001757-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


205 S.W.3d 217; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 39



February 10, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication November 28, 2006.
Review denied by Smith v. Commonwealth, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 810 (Ky., Nov. 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM BOONE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ANTHONY W. FROHLICH, JUDGE. INDICTMENT NO. 02-CR-00329.
Smith v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 462 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 11, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Boone Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted a motion by the Commonwealth to forfeit defendant's vehicle which was seized by police after it was found to contain drugs. Defendant argued that the forfeiture of his vehicle violated the principle of double jeopardy and was unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over for speeding. A search of the vehicle revealed cocaine. Defendant pled guilty and was sentenced to 12 years' imprisonment. While his direct appeal was pending, defendant tried to get the vehicle back, ostensibly to allow his fiancee to use it. The Commonwealth argued that under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.410, the vehicle was subject to forfeiture because it had been used to transport cocaine. Defendant testified that he had bought the vehicle with proceeds from a personal injury settlement. The appellate court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.405 et seq., while perhaps having certain punitive aspects, served important nonpunitive goals. In most cases, there would be a close association between a criminal conviction and a forfeiture pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.405 et seq. However, that did not mean that the forfeiture constituted an additional criminal punishment. There was not a substantial possibility that the result in defendant's case would have been any different if the excessive fines question had been presented to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Davis v. Dep't of Revenue of the Fin. & Admin. Cabinet


NO. 2004-CA-001940-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


197 S.W.3d 557; 2006 Ky. App. LEXIS 1



January 6, 2006, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 25, 2006.
Review denied by Dep't of Revenue v. Davis, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 735 (Ky., Aug. 17, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Dep't of Revenue v. Davis, 550 U.S. 956, 127 S. Ct. 2451, 167 L. Ed. 2d 1129, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 5914 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Dep't of Revenue v. Davis, 553 U.S. 328, 128 S. Ct. 1801, 170 L. Ed. 2d 685, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 4312 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE BARRY WILLETT, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 03-CI-003282.



DISPOSITION: VACATING AND REMANDING.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the order of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, the Department of Revenue of the Finance and Administration Cabinet for the Commonwealth of Kentucky. The taxpayers had filed a class action declaratory judgment complaint alleging that Kentucky's decision to tax the income earned on out-of-state bonds was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The cumulative impact of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 141.020, 141.030, 141.040 was that Kentucky exempted from taxation interest income derived from bonds issued by the Commonwealth or its subdivisions but required taxes to be paid on interest income derived from bonds issued by a sister state or its subdivisions. The taxpayers asserted that the tax on the income earned on the out-of-state bonds violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution and the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The trial court found that the tax system at issue was constitutional and that the taxpayers lacked standing to challenge the tax provisions. The court found that Kentucky's bond taxation system was facially unconstitutional as it afforded more favorable treatment to in-state bonds than it did to extraterritorially issued bond. Further, the court found that the trial court erred by finding that the taxpayers lacked standing to represent the class as that issue was not before the trial court pursuant to the Department's motion for summary judgment and the taxpayers had basic personal standing.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order granting summary judgment to the Department and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Fletcher v. Graham


NO. 2005-CA-002357-OA


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 264



December 16, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Fletcher v. Graham, 192 S.W.3d 350, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 123 (Ky., May 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL ACTION REGARDING FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 05-CI-00711.



DISPOSITION: DENYING CR 76.36 RELIEF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner governor sought an order in the nature of mandamus directing the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) to give his pardon-specific instructions to a grand jury to ensure that the grand jury understood its constitutional role and to prevent it from issuing indictments that impinged upon the governor's pardoning power under Ky. Const. § 77.


OVERVIEW: A special grand jury was empaneled to investigate whistle-blower allegations that officials in the governor's administration had violated the classified service statutes, commonly referred to as the merit system. After the grand jury issued numerous indictments, the governor issued an executive order pardoning the indictees and others who might be indicted for the same offenses. When the grand jury continued to issue indictments for pardoned offenses, the governor requested the circuit court to supplement its instructions to the grand jury by specifying what he maintained was the legal effect of the pardon. The appellate court held that although the governor's power under § 77 extended to the sort of pre-indictment general amnesty that the executive order purported to grant, his arguments overstated the effect of a pardon and the authorities upon which he relied did not compel the result he sought. The governor's pardoning power did not preclude indictment for pardoned offenses and did not oblige the circuit court to instruct the grand jury concerning the effect of such pardons.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

Steel Techs., Inc. v. Estate of Congleton


NO. 2003-CA-002090-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 143



June 24, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Review granted by Steel Techs., Inc. v. Congleton, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 57 (Ky., Mar. 15, 2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Steel Techs., Inc. v. Congleton, 2007 Ky. LEXIS 125 (Ky., June 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM GALLATIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE STANLEY BILLINGSLEY, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 02-CI-00162, CIVIL ACTION NO. 02-CI-00172, CIVIL ACTION NO. 02-CI-00180.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a decedent's two minor children and her estate, sued defendant employer after the decedent was killed when a steel coil fell off one of the employer's tractor-trailer rigs. The Gallatin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted plaintiffs summary judgment on the issue of liability. A jury awarded plaintiffs compensatory damages of $ 667,267 and punitive damages of $ 1 million, from which the employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the employer's driver braked, a 15-ton steel coil broke loose from the trailer and struck the decedent's vehicle; she died shortly thereafter. There was evidence that the employer knew of three prior, similar accidents in which steel coils fell from trucks, but no safety awareness meetings were held before the accident at issue. The appellate court rejected the employer's claim that this evidence inflamed the jury; it was relevant to show that the employer was on notice that steel coils could break free from trailers, and there was no indication that the punitive damage award was intended to punish the employer for the three prior incidents. The employer was properly found vicariously liable for punitive damages based on evidence of its own negligence in ensuring that steel coils were safely secured. Jury instructions that closely tracked Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 411.186 provided constitutionally-sufficient standards for assessing punitive damages. A ratio of 1 to 1.5 between punitive and compensatory damages was within constitutional limits. The decedent's pre-impact fear was compensable. No expert testimony was needed to establish damages for loss of parental consortium.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

525 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Webb v. Carter County Fiscal Court


NO. 2004-CA-000486-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


165 S.W.3d 490; 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 126



May 27, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 18, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CARTER CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SAMUEL C. LONG, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CI-00067.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff magistrate sued defendants, an executive and a fiscal court, alleging that he was wrongfully terminated from employment, and seeking reinstatement as a county employee, backpay, and attorney's fees. The Carter Circuit Court (Kentucky) ruled in favor of the executive and the fiscal court. The magistrate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The magistrate argued that the trial court erred by concluding that his duties as assistant road foreman were incompatible with his duties as a magistrate. The appellate court found that, as a member of the fiscal court, the magistrate was authorized and called upon to consider matters involving salary, tenure, and promotion of county employees. This close interrelationship between the positions rendered the magistrate's concurrent employment with the county road department incompatible with his elected office. In addition, the fiscal court was directly responsible for the implementation of the county road program, had authority over the county road supervisor, and was responsible for approving his proposed policies. Since the magistrate was employed as assistant county road foreman, he was subordinate to the county road supervisor while having the capacity to exert control over his supervisor in his role as a member of the fiscal court. This concurrent public employment and occupancy of this public office were thus functionally incompatible. The incompatibility doctrine did not unduly burden free speech or free association in this case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

526 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't


NO. 2004-CA-001258-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 106



May 6, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
As Modified May 20, 2005.
Review granted by Woods v. Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 269 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 14, 2005)
Review granted by Louisville/Jefferson County Metro Gov't v. Woods, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 373 (Ky., Dec. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE F. KENNETH CONLIFFE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-CI-003636.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a minor and his guardian, sued appellee government over injuries the minor sustained at a public park. The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted the government summary judgment, finding that appellants failed to create a material fact issue as to whether the government's conduct was willful or malicious as required by the Kentucky Recreational Use Statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. § 411.190. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The government built an "extreme park" made of concrete where bikers, skateboarders, and roller bladers could negotiate undulating terrain, deep bowls, and full pipes. The minor, 11 years old, accidentally rode his bike from the beginners' area over a precipitous drop into an 11-foot bowl and was seriously injured. The park had signs warning users to know their abilities, to have parental supervision, and to wear helmets and pads. Under § 411.190(6), landowners were not immune from suit for willful or malicious failure to guard or warn against a dangerous condition. The appellate court found that there was a material fact issue as to whether the government acted willfully toward the minor in failing to erect a physical barrier between the beginners' course and the 11-foot bowl (failure to guard), or in the manner in which it warned users of the park of the potential dangers lurking therein (failure to warn). To constitute willful conduct it was not necessary to show ill will, but an entire absence of care for the life, person, or property of others which exhibited indifference to consequences. The question of willfulness was for the jury to decide.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

527 of 1068 DOCUMENTS



Rogers Group, Inc. v. Masterson


NO. 2004-CA-000341-MR, TO BE HEARD WITH NO. 2004-CA-000483-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


175 S.W.3d 630; 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 102



April 29, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Review denied by Rogers Group v. Masterson, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 355 (Ky., Nov. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM HARDIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOHN WOODS POTTER, JUDGE, ACTION NO. 02-CI-01627. HON. JANET P. COLEMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Hardin Circuit Court is affirmed and the case is remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee citizen's group brought an action against, among others, appellants, a city and property owner, seeking to have an agreed upon judgment entered in a separate case set aside. The Hardin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted the relief and ordered the agreed upon judgment set aside. The city and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The agreed upon judgment at issue allowed the owner to run a quarry on the land, and provided for the city to receive certain acreage. The trial court found that this was illegal judicial rezoning. The appellate court agreed. Rezoning was not a judicial function, and a court did not have the authority to order a particular classification be applied to land. The agreed judgment, in essence, zoned the property. The city had no classification that would have allowed a quarry. Thus, the agreed judgment improperly created the zone, and it applied it only to the owner. Under Ky. R. Civ. P. 60.02, a motion attacking a judgment as void was not required to be filed within a specific time. The trial court properly found that the motion to set aside was made in a reasonable time, since the citizen's group had been challenging the agreed judgment in one way or another since it was entered, and the city and the owner were not misled by any delay. The agreed judgment's provisions giving the city the acreage and settling the zoning issues were tied together, and thus it would have been inequitable to set aside only part of the agreed judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Rehm v. Navistar Int'l


NO. 2002-CA-001399-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 48

Review granted by Rehm v. Navistar Int'l Corp., 2005 Ky. LEXIS 343 (Ky., Nov. 16, 2005)

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS B. WINE. ACTION NO. 01-CI-001344.
Rehm v. Clayton, 132 S.W.3d 864, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 86 (Ky., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an executrix and several heirs, challenged a decision from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee contractors in a case alleging premises liability, negligence, gross negligence, willful misconduct, and intentional and outrageous conduct.


OVERVIEW: The employee was exposed to insulation products on the contractors' property, and he was diagnosed with an incurable form of cancer associated with exposure to asbestos. Thereafter, an action was filed against the contractors. The contractors' motion for summary judgment was granted, and the executrix and the heirs sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the claims were barred under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 342.610, 342.690. First, the issue of "regular or recurrent" was an issue of law to be decided by the court if the underlying facts concerning business operations were not in dispute. Next, entitlement to protection under §§ 342.610, 342.690 was strictly construed. The work performed by the employee was a regular or recurrent part of the business of the 16 contractors. The employee's consent to the Kentucky Workers' Compensation Act negated any argument that the application of §§ 342.610, 342.690 was unconstitutional under the jural rights doctrine. The trial court properly allowed the amendment of certain pleadings, the contractors had secured workers' compensation insurance, and the failure to allow more discovery was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Schwartz v. Hasty


NO. 2003-CA-000796-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


175 S.W.3d 621; 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 43



February 11, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Review denied by Ky. Farm Bureau Mut. Ins. Co. v. Schwartz, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 993 (Ky., Nov. 16, 2005)
Review denied by Schwartz v. Hasty, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 354 (Ky., Nov. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM GARRARD CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE C. HUNTER DAUGHERTY, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CI-00220.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed an order of satisfaction from the Garrard Circuit Court (Kentucky), which held that underinsured motorist (UIM) benefits he received from his own insurers were not subject to the collateral source rule and could be credited against the amount he could recover from defendants, the other driver and the other driver's liability insurer, after he was awarded tort damages in a personal injury action against the other driver.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was severely injured when a car operated by the driver struck him. The driver had vehicle liability insurance through a policy with the insurer. Plaintiff had UIM policies with other insurers, which paid him benefits. Plaintiff filed a personal injury complaint against the driver and he received an award of damages. The insurer moved for an order of satisfaction, arguing Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 304.39-320 limited plaintiff's recovery by the amount he already recovered in UIM benefits, which resulted in satisfaction of the tort award. The trial court agreed. Plaintiff appealed, arguing that the collateral source rule applied and denied the other driver a setoff for the UIM payments. The insurer argued that applying the collateral source rule allowed plaintiff a double recovery, and that § 304.39-320 entitled the driver to a setoff for the UIM payments. The court found, first, that the collateral source rule applied to UIM insurance payments just as it applied to other insurance payments. Also, an interpretation of § 304.39-320 as authorizing a setoff violated Ky. Const. § 54, even if a double recovery occurred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of satisfaction and remanded for a recalculation of the damages plaintiff could recover from the other driver and the insurer.

Ky. Ret. Sys. v. Heavrin


NO. 2004-CA-000238-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


172 S.W.3d 808; 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 24



February 4, 2005, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 24, 2005.
Review denied by Ky. Ret. Sys. v. Heavrin, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 321 (Ky., Oct. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 03-CI-00350.
State Ret. Sys. v. Heavrin, 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 648 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 17, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted appellee employee's appeal from an administrative proceeding and overruled a final order rendered by appellant the Kentucky Retirement System (System). The effect of said order allowed the employee to purchase five years of non-qualified service credit at a price reflective of her actual salary and required the System to refund any excess payment made by her, plus interest. The System appealed.


OVERVIEW: The System challenged the judgment entered. But, the appeals court held that it erroneously calculated the employee's current rate of pay, that said calculation was illogical and unfair to the employee because it did not contemplate her actual earnings, and that the System misapplied the statutory formula for calculating the cost of her non-qualified service credit. The employee's cost to purchase the service credit was to be based upon her final rate of pay. The System contended that because the employee worked 8-hour days, its calculation of her final rate of pay did not reflect her actual hours or days worked. The System knew that the employee worked an 8-hour day, but only 24.5 hours per week. It also knew that she was a permanent part-time employee working only 100 hours per month, earning approximately $ 32,000 per year. It was clear from the evidence presented that both the System and the hearing officer ignored that information in reaching its decision as to the employee's actual hours worked.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, IN PART, AND REVERSED AND REMANDED, IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Pulaski Circuit Court (Kentucky), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee annexed taxpayers and concluded that the city's assessment and levy of taxes on the taxpayers violated statutory requirements. The taxpayers cross-appealed from the circuit court's ruling that while the taxpayers were entitled to refunds, they could not recover the refunds in their class-action lawsuit.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed suit, arguing that the city had improperly collected taxes from them after their properties were annexed into the city because the city failed to file accurate maps as required by statute. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment on the issue of the improper levy and collection of the taxes. The court affirmed the circuit court's ruling on all of the other issues.

Gov't Emples. Ins. Co. v. Winsett


NO. 2003-CA-002769-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


153 S.W.3d 862; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 364



December 17, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 25, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM WARREN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS R. LEWIS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 02-CI-01543.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subrogee insurer sought review of a decision of the Warren Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed the insurer's intervening complaint, finding it was barred by the applicable statute of limitations. Appellees had been involved in a car accident with the subrogee's insured and were named as defendants in the original action by the insured.


OVERVIEW: The insured was involved in an automobile accident with appellees and filed a lawsuit against them. The lawsuit was initiated by the insured against appellees and was filed within the applicable statute of limitations period. The insurer intervened in the action and the trial court dismissed the insurer's claim, finding that the claim was barred under the two-year limitation period set forth in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.125. The court held that it was error to dismiss the insurer's claim. As a subrogee, the insurer's claim was derivative of the insured's claim, and the statute of limitations that was applicable to the insured was also applicable to the insurer. The court did not decide which statute of limitations was applicable to the insurer's claim, finding instead that the insurer's complaint should have been allowed because it related to the insured's lawsuit, was filed as part of the insured's lawsuit, and intervention was thus allowed pursuant to Ky. R. Civ. P. 24. Intervention by the insured prior to trial or other disposition of the case was presumptively timely.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Roman Catholic Bishop of Louisville v. Burden


NO. 2004-CA-000086-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


168 S.W.3d 414; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 351



December 10, 2004, Rendered  
December 10, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 26, 2005.
Reconsideration denied by Roman Catholic Bishop of Louisville v. Burden, 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 390 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 10, 2004)
Review denied by Roman Catholic Bishop v. Burden, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 265 (Ky., Aug. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 02-CI-004515. HONORABLE THOMAS B. WINE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alleged victim of sexual abuse sued defendant church, seeking damages for its actions, or lack of action, concerning alleged sexual abuse by a priest who worked for the church. The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied the church's motion for summary judgment and its motion to alter, amend, or vacate. The church appealed.


OVERVIEW: The church argued that the statute of limitations barred the alleged victim's claim under either Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.249 or Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.140. The appellate court ruled that the general rule under Ky. R. Civ. P. 56.03 was that a denial of a motion for summary judgment was, first, not appealable because of its interlocutory nature and, second, was not reviewable on appeal from a final judgment where the question was whether there existed a genuine issue of material fact. Because there had not yet been a final judgment entered in the case from which an appeal was taken, that exception to the rule had no application. The trial court's inclusion of Ky. R. Civ. P. 54.02 finality language in its initial denial of the summary judgment motion was meaningless because that rule was limited to actions involving multiple parties or multiple claims, which was not the case. Even if Ky. R. Civ. P. 54.02 applied and could have operated to make the interlocutory judgment final and appealable, there had been no conclusive determination of the rights of any party.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

535 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Wilfong v. Commonwealth


NO. 2002-CA-000535-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


175 S.W.3d 84; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 353



December 10, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Review denied by Wilfong v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 1006 (Ky., Nov. 16, 2005)
Review denied by Wilfong v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 352 (Ky., Nov. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MEADE CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 01-CR-00057. HONORABLE SAM H. MONARCH, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Meade Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicted defendant of third-degree rape under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 510.060, and sentenced him to one year in prison and a subsequent three-year period of conditional discharge as required by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§532.043. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§532.043 violated the separation of powers doctrine by infringing upon the judiciary's duty to administer justice and by removing all discretion from the trial court by imposing a three-year mandatory conditional discharge. The appeals court disagreed. The Kentucky Legislature, rather than the judiciary, designated the elements of criminal conduct and the penalty for crimes. Similarly, the legislature did not unconstitutionally usurp judicial functions by eliminating the exercise of discretion by the trial court in fixing a sentence, as it had the plenary power to set criminal penalties. Second, since defendant pled guilty and was not sentenced by a jury, his request that the appeals court declare § 532.043 to be in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.055 and the constitutional guarantee of due process lacked merit. Finally, defendant failed to show that the conditions of his conditional discharge on any protected-constitutional activity was sufficiently real and substantial in relation to the legitimate scope of government regulation of persons on supervisory release to justify a facial challenge with the relaxed standing approach.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

536 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Weinberg


NO. 2003-CA-001464-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


150 S.W.3d 75; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 319



October 29, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 16, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM KNOTT CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOHN ROBERT MORGAN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 94-CI-00095.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commonwealth of Kentucky, Transportation Cabinet, sought review of a decision of the Knott Circuit Court, (Kentucky), which entered judgment in favor of appellee driver and determined that 601 Ky. Admin. Regs. 13:025 (1990), amounted to an arbitrary exercise of power when it was used to suspend the driver's privilege to drive after accumulating too many speeding tickets.


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted two times in a two year period for speeding 16 to 25 miles per hour and a total of 12 points were assessed against his license. Under 601 Ky. Admin. Regs. 13:025 (1990), the driver's privilege to drive was suspended by the Cabinet after a hearing. The Cabinet did not offer any evidence at the hearing other than the two traffic convictions. The driver challenged the regulation and the hearing by filing a complaint with the lower court, and the lower court granted judgment in favor of the driver, concluding that 601 Ky. Admin. Regs. 13:025 (1990) amounted to an arbitrary exercise of power because the point-system failed to rely upon accident-cause statistics as mandated by the regulation. The court held that 601 Ky. Admin. Regs. 13:025 (1990), as adopted August 9, 1990, and as applied through 1997 was invalid. The evidence overwhelmingly established that the Cabinet failed to follow 601 Ky. Admin. Regs. 13:025 (1990) when it did not use the accident-cause statistics when it created the point system. The court reversed the lower court's decision to the extent that it attempted to require the current version of the regulation to be "revamped."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court to the extent that it found that the 1990 version of the regulation was arbitrary and capricious. The court reversed that port of the decision that directed the Cabinet to revamp the regulation.

 

537 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Am. Life & Accident Ins. Co. of Ky. v. Commonwealth


NO. 2003-CA-001802-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


173 S.W.3d 910; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 299



October 15, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Review denied by Am. Life & Accident Ins. Co. v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 320 (Ky., Oct. 12, 2005)Released for Publication October 24, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE STEPHEN P. RYAN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CI-002316.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company brought an action against appellee revenue cabinet, and others, seeking a refund of taxes paid. The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted the revenue cabinet's motion to dismiss. The insurance company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insurance company had been taxed on certain on its property. Later, the statutes which provided the authority for those taxes were declared unconstitutional. The insurance company sought refunds of the taxes at issue. Although the revenue cabinet refunded a portion of the taxes paid, refund of the majority was denied because the revenue cabinet believed that the two-year statute of limitations of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590 barred those claims. The appellate court held that the two-year statute of limitations applied to the suit for a refund and that the doctrines of equitable recoupment and set-off were not available to the insurance company. The tax imposed by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 136.320 in its operation, effect, and incidents was an ad valorem property tax. Therefore, the two-year statute of limitations contained in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590 was applicable. The case law did not support the application of equitable recoupment in the circumstances urged by the insurance company. Set-off was in the nature of a defense but was one available to the taxing authority and thus unavailable to the insurance company.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

538 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


McKenzie v. Commonwealth


NO. 2002-CA-001098-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 276



September 17, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by McKenzie v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 53 (Ky. Ct. App., Mar. 4, 2005)
Substituted opinion at McKenzie v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 54 (Ky. Ct. App., Mar. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM J. WEHR, JUDGE. INDICTMENT NO. 01-CR-00191.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicted defendant of third-degree burglary as an accomplice, enhanced by a finding that he was a persistent felony offender in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the presentation of evidence at trial, the Commonwealth moved to amend the indictment to add as an alternate theory that defendant was complicit to another's commission of the robbery. Defendant was convicted only under the complicity instruction. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in giving the complicity instruction sought by the Commonwealth. Defendant did not waive his right to be proceeded against only by indictment, so the only allowable departure from the indictment was that contemplated by Ky. R. Crim. P. 6.16. The distinction between third degree burglary and complicity to third degree burglary was the sort of amendment that was prohibited because it involved a modification at trial in the elements of the crime charged. This was prejudicial per se. By convicting defendant of complicity to burglary, the jury necessarily acquitted him of the primary offense. Accordingly, he could not have been retried on the charge of third degree burglary.


OUTCOME: The conviction of complicity to third degree burglary was reversed. The appellate court ordered that defendant could not have been retried on the charge of third degree burglary, and that the Commonwealth was required to seek an indictment on the complicity charge from a grand jury or a proper waiver of indictment by defendant before retrial on that charge.

 

539 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Vibbert v. Vibbert


NO. 2002-CA-002348-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


144 S.W.3d 292; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 246



August 27, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 7, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM METCALFE CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 02-CI-00030. HONORABLE PHILIP R. PATTON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021(1), the Metcalfe Circuit Court (Kentucky) awarded visitation to appellee grandfather with appellant parents' minor child against the parents' express wishes. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents claimed that the circuit court ignored Scott v. Scott, 80 S.W.3d 447 (Ky. App. 2002), which required a grandparent seeking visitation under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021 to prove by clear and convincing evidence that harm would result to the child from the parents' limitation of grandparent visitation. The appellate court overruled Scott because it set an unnecessarily strict and unworkable standard. Under the new standard, the grandparent had to prove, by clear and convincing evidence, that the requested visitation was in the best interest of the child. Some factors the circuit court had to consider were the nature and stability of the relationship between the child and the grandparent; the potential detriments and benefits to the child from visitation; the effect visitation would have on the child's relationship with the parents; the physical and emotional health of all the adults involved; and the child's wishes and preferences. Use of the clear and convincing standard was constitutionally required because such cases involved the fundamental right of parents to raise their children as they saw fit without undue interference from the State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the matter was remanded for further consideration in light of the new standard the appellate court announced.

 

540 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Jameson v. Commonwealth


NO. 2003-CA-000967-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 229



August 6, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Review granted by Jameson v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 196 (Ky., Aug. 17, 2005)
Reversed by, in part Commonwealth v. Jameson, 215 S.W.3d 9, 2006 Ky. LEXIS 290 (Ky., Nov. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT HONORABLE R. JEFFREY HINES, JUDGE ACTION NOS. 00-M-01796, 00-M-01797 AND 02-XX-00004.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for review from an order of the McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) which affirmed an order of the McCracken District Court denying defendant's motion to declare McCracken County, Ky., Ordinance No. 2000-4 unconstitutional and to dismiss the criminal complaint against him.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance provided for regulation of sexually-oriented businesses and their employees, aimed at controlling the alleged negative, secondary effects associated with such businesses. Defendant was criminally charged for various ordinance violations. He first claimed the district court erred by not analyzing McCracken County, Ky., Ordinance No. 2000-4, § VII(b) pursuant to a strict scrutiny standard. However, since § VII(b)'s ban on nudity was content-based, it did not fit squarely under the U.S. Supreme Court's Barnes and Pap's A.M. analysis, and § VII(b) was properly analyzed pursuant to an intermediate level standard of review. The appellate court did agree with defendant's claim that if intermediate scrutiny was the appropriate standard of review, the case nonetheless had to be remanded to the district court in light of the Supreme Court's decision in Alameda Books. Defendant's unrebutted evidence was sufficient to cast doubt on the fiscal court's pre-enactment rationale for § VII(b), but because Alameda Books had not yet been rendered at the time of the evidentiary hearing, remand to the district court was necessary.


OUTCOME: The order of the district court was affirmed in part, vacated in part, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

541 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Kerr


NO. 2003-CA-001330-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


136 S.W.3d 783; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 155



May 28, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 9, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM TRIGG CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 02-CR-00021. HONORABLE BILL CUNNINGHAM, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for a violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.489(1). The Trigg Circuit Court (Kentucky) declared Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.489(1) unconstitutionally vague and dismissed the indictment. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the bill which enacted Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.489(1), the legislature enacted Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.482 to define "approved container." However, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.482 stated that it was only applicable to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 250.42-250.488. The trial court ruled that because of this error, an "approved container" was not defined, and thus Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.489(1) was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court held that courts consistently rejected reliance on a compiler's error to strike down or otherwise aid in interpreting a statute. Such an error did not vitiate a statute where its fair intent could have been gathered from the whole text. When the legislature amended Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.482 to include the definition of approved container, and at the same time, declare it illegal to possess anhydrous ammonia in an unapproved container, it intended the definition to apply to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.489. The error committed by the compiler of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.489 by giving it a number outside the scope of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 250.482 did not render unconstitutional an otherwise constitutional statute.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

542 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Bartrum v. Hunter Excavating


NO. 2003-CA-002305-WC


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 156



May 28, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Hunter Excavating v. Bartrum, 168 S.W.3d 381, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 151 (Ky., May 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION FOR REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION BOARD. ACTION NO. WC-02-01163.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant workers' compensation claimant appealed from an order entered by the Kentucky Workers' Compensation Board, which affirmed the denial by an administrative law judge of the claimant's pneumoconiosis-based claim for benefits.


OVERVIEW: The claimant argued that the consensus procedure for processing coal-workers' pneumoconiosis claims denied him a meaningful opportunity to be heard, and that the exclusion of additional supporting x-ray evidence violated his due-process rights. The appellate court held that the due-process rights included the right to present relevant, probative evidence in support of one's claim and in rebuttal of adverse evidence. The exclusion of additional x-ray evidence unduly burdened the claimant's right to challenge the outcome of the consensus procedure. As x-ray reading was nearly as much art as science, and as reasonable differences of opinion among experts were common, cross-examination did not afford a reliable means of exposing a reading's weaknesses. Additional expert opinion was the only meaningful evidence available to a party who wished to challenge consensus readings. To the extent that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 342.316 and the regulations promulgated thereunder precluded the use of additional x-ray evidence in rebuttal in a coal-worker's pneumoconiosis claim, they violated the parties' due-process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ky. Const. § 2.


OUTCOME: The Board's decision was reversed. The case was remanded for additional proceedings.

Hardy v. Commonwealth


NO. 2003-CA-000584-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


149 S.W.3d 433; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 145



May 21, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 9, 2004.
Review denied by Hardy v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 313 (Ky., Dec. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SHEILA R. ISAAC, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 02-CR-01137.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a final judgment and sentence of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which was entered on defendant's conditional plea of guilty to trafficking in a controlled substance in the first degree. The conditional plea was entered under an agreement that defendant would be allowed to appeal the denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car stopped for an equipment violation. Both defendant and the driver were asked for identification. Due to the time of day of the stop and heavy dispatching traffic, it took approximately 20-30 minutes to run the background check on defendant's driver's license. When completed, the background check showed defendant was wanted on an outstanding warrant. Defendant was arrested and during a search incident to the arrest, individual packages of crack cocaine were found. On appeal, defendant asserted that "but for" his illegal detention while waiting for the background check results, the cocaine would never have been found. The court disagreed, holding that (1) the "but for" test did not apply where an intervening circumstance sufficient to dissipate any taint caused by prior unlawful conduct occurred; (2) the lawful arrest based on an arrest warrant was a sufficient intervening circumstance to remove any taint of an illegal detention of defendant; and (3) defendant failed to present evidence to support his claim that he was a victim of racial profiling, and even if he was such a victim, it would not require suppression of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Travis v. Commonwealth


NO. 2003-CA-000127-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 149



May 21, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Discretionary appeal not allowed by Travis v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 290 (Ky., Nov. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MARSHALL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DENNIS R. FOUST, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 02-CR-00078.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant conditionally pled guilty in the Marshall Circuit Court (Kentucky) to manufacturing methamphetamine, first degree trafficking in a controlled substance, first degree possession of a controlled substance, and possession of drug paraphernalia, after the trial court denied his motion to suppress. He appealed the denial of his suppression motion.


OVERVIEW: An officer approached the truck defendant was in when it was parked on the roadside at 3:30 a.m. The appellate court held the officer's community caretaking function let him approach the vehicle with no suspicion of criminal activity. The driver's nervous, evasive behavior, the time of night, and the officer's detection of the odor of ether coming from an article in the truck's bed gave the officer reasonable, articulable suspicion allowing a request for the driver's license, and this brief detainment's scope was reasonably related to its justification. When the officer was told by dispatch of possible drug activity related to the driver, saw the driver acting suspiciously around the article in the truck's bed, and, when the officer asked for consent to search the truck, the driver became excited and began walking toward the officer while "flapping his arms," combined with the fact that the officer was confronting two individuals by himself in the middle of the night, the officer could handcuff the driver and put him in a police car. The truck's owner had full authority to let the police search it, and that authority extended to the suspicious article in the truck's bed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Allen v. Ky. Horse Racing Auth.


NO. 2003-CA-000869-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


136 S.W.3d 54; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 138



May 14, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 01-CI-01432.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Kentucky Horse Racing Authority (KHRA) disqualified appellant owner's horse as the winner of two races and required the owner to return the prize money. The owner appealed; the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed the KHRA's decision. The owner sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The horse finished first in two races, and was given routine urine tests after each race. Its urine tested positive for flunixin, an anti-inflammatory drug, which violated 811 Ky. Admin. Regs. 1:090, § 4(1). The owner had the second sample from each race re-tested; all results were positive for flunixin. The appellate court held that the KHRA's decision was not arbitrary, as it was supported by substantial evidence; though the owner's expert pointed out the absence of flunixin metabolites in the horse's urine, another expert opined that the absence of metabolites indicated that the flunixin may have been given immediately before the race. The appellate court rejected the owner's claim that the chain of custody was broken, as it was unnecessary to establish a perfect chain of custody and the evidence showed there was no tampering. The "trainer responsibility rule" (811 Ky. Admin. Regs. 1:090) was constitutional. There was no double jeopardy violation, as that doctrine did not apply to civil actions. 811 Ky. Admin. Regs. 1:090, § 4(1), which outlawed flunixin for harness horses but not thoroughbreds, did not violate equal protection principles.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

546 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Erickson


NO. 2002-CA-002084-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


132 S.W.3d 884; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 38


February 20, 2004, Rendered  
March 12, 2004, Modified


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 18, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 02-CR-00171. HONORABLE R. JEFFREY HINES, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted on charges of first-degree trafficking in a controlled substance, possession of drug paraphernalia, operating a motor vehicle without an illuminated rear license plate, and being a second-degree persistent felony offender, and he filed a motion to suppress evidence. The McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted the motion, and the Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant's vehicle after he noticed that the vehicle did not have a light illuminating its rear license plate. The officer ran a computer check on defendant while another officer checked identification provided by two passengers in defendant's vehicle, and the officers returned documents they obtained from defendant and his passengers when they received no information indicating cause for concern. The officer engaged defendant in a conversation after he returned defendant's driver's license and proof of insurance, and eventually asked defendant if he would consent to a search of his vehicle. Defendant gave his consent and when officers searched the car, they found 10 bags containing methamphetamine. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the drugs, and the trial court granted his motion. The appellate court held that because the evidence did not show defendant was improperly detained by the officers or that the officers coerced him into giving them consent to search his car, there was no legal basis for suppressing the drugs, and the trial court erred by doing so.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

547 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Kinney v. Butcher


NO. 2002-CA-002150-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


131 S.W.3d 357; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 65



March 12, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 2004


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM PIKE CIRCUIT COURT. CIVIL ACTION NO. 01-CI-00612. HONORABLE EDDY COLEMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party appealed a judgment by the Pike Circuit Court (Kentucky); the injured party claimed that the trial court erred in not instructing the jury on punitive damages and not granting a new trial following alleged misconduct by appellee driver's counsel during closing argument.


OVERVIEW: While the driver was attempting to pass a slow moving van, the van accelerated. The driver applied his brakes in an attempt to avoid a collision with the injured party's vehicle but went into a slide. The injured party claimed that the driver's violation of traffic statutes automatically triggered the imposition of punitive damages. The appellate court held that traveling at a possible speed of 10 miles per hour over the posted speed limit and failing to complete a pass before entering a no-passing zone constituted nothing more than ordinary negligence. Therefore, punitive damages were not available. The trial court's admonition cured any prejudice resulting from the driver's counsel's statements in closing argument. At no time did the injured party move for a mistrial; therefore, she could not complain that the trial court's remedy was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Owens v. Jefferson County Fiscal Court


NO. 2002-CA-001209-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


128 S.W.3d 834; 2004 Ky. App. LEXIS 37



February 20, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 01-CI-005027. HONORABLE THOMAS B. WINE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a commissioner and a voter, appealed an opinion and order by the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) that granted summary judgment to appellees, a fiscal court and a member thereof; the commissioner and voter claimed that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 67C.135(3) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 67C.101(1), the voters approved a merger of a city and a county into a single government. A representative of a university's geography department drew the initial boundaries. The commissioner and the voter argued that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 67C.135(3), which required the members of the fiscal court to approve the plan as drawn, violated the prohibition against arbitrary power and the doctrine of separation in Ky. Const. §§ 2, 27, 28, 29. The appellate court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 67C.135(3) was not prey to invalidation by the courts because it included sufficient criteria for drawing the districts. Because the fiscal court had no power or discretion as to the creation of the initial districts, it was not arbitrary to require its approval of the plan without permitting it to make further refinements after-the-fact.


OUTCOME: The opinion and order were affirmed.

Garriga v. Sanitation Dist. No. 1


NO. 2001-CA-002593-MR, NO. 2002-CA-001192-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 305



December 5, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Alliance for Kentucky's Future, Inc. v. Envtl. & Pub. Prot. Cabinet, 2008 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 5 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 10, 2008)
Related proceeding at Alliance for Kentucky's Future v. Envtl. & Pub. Prot. Cabinet, 2008 Ky. App. LEXIS 401 (Ky. Ct. App., Oct. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM KENTON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE GREGORY M. BARTLETT, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CI-002364. APPEAL FROM BOONE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOSEPH F. BAMBERGER, JUDGE. ACTION NOS. 99-CI-00860 AND 01-CI-00510.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged an order of the Kenton Circuit Court (Kentucky), which dismissed her claims against appellee sanitation district for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, alleging, inter alia, that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 220.035 was unconstitutional. Appellant property owners challenged an interlocutory order and judgment of the Boone Circuit Court (Kentucky), which authorized the sanitation district to condemn their property.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, both the taxpayer and the property owners contended that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 220.035 violated Ky. Const. §§ 2, 3, 27, 28, 29, 59 and 60. The taxpayer was attempting to invoke the circuit court's jurisdiction under the Declaratory Judgment Act, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 418.045. Affirming, the court first held that both the taxpayer and the property owners lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 220.035 because the taxpayer failed to demonstrate that she had been adversely affected by § 220.035 and because the property owners, while they suffered an injury, failed to establish any causal relationship between their injury and § 220.035(4). Addressing appellants' remaining claims, the court held that: (1) the sanitation district's committee did not act arbitrarily in approving the acquisition of the property owners' land; (2) the taxpayer failed to state a violate claim of fraud because she did not show reliance; and (3) the sanitation district was not required to submit a draft plan to a regional planning commission or comply with the Clean Water Act prior to initiating condemnation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the first circuit court dismissing the taxpayer's complaint, and it affirmed the interlocutory order and judgment of the second circuit court, which authorized the sanitation district to condemn the property owners' property.
