Revenue Cabinet v. Comcast Cablevision


NO. 2002-CA-001524-MR, NO. 2002-CA-001579-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


147 S.W.3d 743; 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 330



November 14, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Ordered Published December 31, 2003. Released for Publication November 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER L. CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 01-CI-00653.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING IN PART, VACATING AND REMANDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed the decision of defendant state tax appeal board in favor of defendant cable television company on the issue of the cable television company's public service corporation property tax assessment for two tax years. The state revenue cabinet appealed and the cable television company cross-appealed the trial court's determination that the issues presented were purely questions of law.


OVERVIEW: The state revenue cabinet issued property tax assessments on the cable television company's property. The cable television company protested, but the state revenue cabinet upheld them. The cable television company appealed to the state tax appeals board. An expert witness testified for the cable television company that the state revenue cabinet's assessments included improper valuations. The state tax appeal board ultimately set aside the assessments. The state revenue cabinet lowered its original valuation and argued to the trial court that the fair cash value of the cable television company's operating property was the total business enterprise value shown in the appraisal of the expert witness. The trial court reviewed the issue de novo and upheld the state tax appeals board's decision. On appeal, the appellate court found that the state revenue cabinet's valuation was proper since it assessed the relevant property, the operating tangible property and the franchise, by its fair cash value as a unit. On the cable television company's cross-appeal, it found that the trial court properly used a de novo standard of review and that the assessments were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's determination that the issues presented were purely questions of law was affirmed. However, the trial court's judgment affirming the state tax appeals board was vacated and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

551 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Deweese


NO. 2002-CA-002425-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


141 S.W.3d 372; 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 267



October 24, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Release for Publication September 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 02-CI-007187. HONORABLE LISABETH HUGHES ABRAMSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee juvenile was charged with felony offenses, and because the charges involved the use of a firearm, the juvenile was subject to transfer to circuit court for trial as an adult. Subsequently, the Jefferson Circuit Court, Kentucky, denied a writ of prohibition, wherein appellant Commonwealth requested that the circuit court prohibit the juvenile court from ordering discovery, prior to a transfer hearing. The Commonwealth sought review.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court held the Kentucky Rules of Criminal Procedure did not dictate the timing and scope of discovery in a juvenile transfer hearing. The circuit court ruled that discovery was available pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 610.342. Even though it believed § 610.342 violated the separation of powers doctrine, because it affected matters of practice and procedure, the circuit court concluded § 610.342 was not an unreasonable encroachment on the judiciary. The appellate court rejected the circuit court's ruling. The appellate court held that only the Kentucky Rules of Criminal Procedure, applicable to preliminary hearings, applied in a juvenile transfer hearing pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 635.020(4). As such, Ky. R. Crim. P. 3.07 controlled, and the juvenile was not entitled to complete discovery until probable cause was established. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 610.342 was not a rule of discovery, indeed if it had been, the appellate court would have been constrained to declare it an unconstitutional encroachment on the powers of the judiciary pursuant to Ky. Const. § 116, which reserved the power to prescribe rules of practice and procedure to the Kentucky Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

552 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Commonwealth


NO. 2001-CA-002262-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


120 S.W.3d 185; 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 248



October 10, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified October 31, 2003. Ordered Published October 10, 2003. Released for Publication December 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM McLEAN CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 00-CR-00017. HONORABLE DAVID H. JERNIGAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the McLean Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied defendant's motion to suppress, he entered a conditional plea of guilty to trafficking in a controlled substance within 1,000 yards of a school, possession of a controlled substance in the first degree (methamphetamine), possession of marijuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, and cultivation of marijuana, five or fewer plants, while in the possession of a firearm. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Officers learned that a man subject to an outstanding arrest warrant was living with defendant, went to defendant's home, knocked on the door, and were told to come in. Marijuana cigarettes and firearms were in plain view in the living room. Defendant claimed only he and his companion were in the home, but officers discovered a third man; they arrested all three. Police found marijuana growing in a bedroom closet, drug paraphernalia and firearms in the bedrooms, and methamphetamine in a container in the kitchen. Defendant claimed the trial court erred by ruling that the evidence seized from the bedrooms was admissible under the "safety check" exception to the warrant requirement and that seizure of drugs from the container in the kitchen was a proper "search incident to arrest." The appellate court disagreed. The presence of firearms, drugs, and persons suspected of criminal activity constituted a "'serious and demonstrable potentiality for danger" justifying a "safety check" search. And as the kitchen counter was within the immediate area where defendant might have gained possession of destructible evidence, the search of the container was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

553 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Rockwell Int'l Corp. v. Wilhite


NO. 1997-CA-000188-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


143 S.W.3d 604; 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 193



August 8, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REMAND FROM THE SUPREME COURT OF KENTUCKY. NO. 2000-SC-0142-DG. APPEAL FROM LOGAN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TYLER L. GILL, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 93-CI-000158.
Wilhite v. Rockwell Int'l Corp., 83 S.W.3d 516, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 91 (Ky., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landowners sued appellant corporation in the circuit court for trespass and nuisance. The jury awarded compensatory and punitive damages to the landowners. The appellate court reversed the judgment. The Supreme Court of Kentucky affirmed the appellate court's judgment and ordered a new trial. The case was remanded to the appellate court for further determinations.


OVERVIEW: The landowners alleged injury to their properties as the result of the corporation depositing thereon minute quantities of polychlorinated biphenyls (PCBs). The appellate court found that the five-year statute of limitations period of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 413.120 applied, and that the statute did not bar the landowners' claims. Further, the federal discovery rule applied to the property damage actions with the necessary implication that the landowners, if they had a viable cause of action, were entitled to recover damages for injuries incurred outside of the five-year limitation period preceding the filing of their complaint. However, the landowners could not recover damages under a negligent trespass theory, as they failed to establish that their properties suffered any injury as a consequence of the trespass. Additionally, the permanent nuisance claim failed, as there was no rational basis to find that the discharge of minute quantities of PCBs onto the landowners' properties resulted in any interference with their use and enjoyment of the properties. Finally, the punitive damages award was the result of passion and prejudice resulting from counsel's improper argument.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the landowners was reversed.

Kentec Coal Co. v. Commonwealth


NO. 2002-CA-001239-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 179



July 25, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Review granted by Commonwealth v. Kentec Coal Co., 2004 Ky. LEXIS 166 (Ky., Aug. 18, 2004)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Commonwealth Natural Res. & Envtl. Prot. Cabinet v. Kentec Coal Co., 177 S.W.3d 718, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 303 (Ky., 2005)
Rehearing denied by Commonwealth v. Kentec Coal Co., 2005 Ky. LEXIS 1042 (Ky., Dec. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NOS. 98-CI-00580 AND 98-CI-02002. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed a penalty assessed against appellant mining company (miners) by appellee, the Commonwealth, as a result of a post-mining land use violation. The miners' motion to alter, amend, or vacate the judgment was also denied. The miners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The miners challenged the judgment entered, first arguing that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 350.0301 and 405 Ky. Admin. Regs. 7:092 were invalid and unconstitutional because they denied them due process and equal protection by requiring prepayment of a penalty assessment as a condition precedent to obtaining a formal hearing regarding that very assessment. The appeals court agreed that this impermissibly erected a monetary bar to the fundamental due process right to a hearing. Once a violation was determined, the opportunity to address the fine or penalty flowing from that violation came only at the price of prepayment of the subject matter of the challenge. This bifurcated hearing process did not satisfy fundamental due process. Further, prior to being able to complete restoration of the land in question to use for hay land/pasture or forestry land according to the terms of its original permit plan, a third party built a house on the permit site. There was literally nothing that the miners could do to prevent the construction. The Commonwealth nevertheless issued its noncompliance and cessation order. Such action without a hearing was unreasonable and arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case was remanded.

Pangallo v. Ky. Law Enforcement Council


NO. 2001-CA-002765-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


106 S.W.3d 474; 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 102



May 16, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 2, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CAMPBELL CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 00-CI-01351. HONORABLE LEONARD KOPOWSKI, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review in the Campbell Circuit Court (Kentucky) of the revocation of his police officer certification by appellee law enforcement council. The trial court denied the officer's summary judgment motion and found the council properly revoked the certification. The officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the officer was hired, he said he was a member of the Marine Corps Reserves and was meeting his attendant obligations. He was discharged from the Reserves for other than honorable reasons for not meeting those obligations. The appellate court held the officer waived his due process rights applicable to a police officer's termination, when he resigned for "personal reasons," after being confronted with his inaccurate representation, but he did not waive his right to challenge his employer's conclusion that he willfully falsified information to maintain certified status. The council could not revoke his law enforcement certification for falsification of information to maintain certified status unless he was separated from his job for that reason, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15.386(4)(b). The record only showed his voluntary resignation for personal reasons, which normally resulted in a certification being placed in inactive status, under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15.386(3). The officer was not given notice or an opportunity to be heard regarding his alleged misconduct, nor did he waive those minimal due process rights.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded for the trial court to order the law enforcement council to reinstate the officer's law enforcement certification to inactive status.

O'Neil v. Commonwealth


NO. 2001-CA-001377-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


114 S.W.3d 860; 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 62



March 21, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 8, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE BARRY WILLETT, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CR-002481.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court, Kentucky, convicted defendant of burglary in the second degree, possession of a handgun by a convicted felon, and being a persistent felony offender (PFO) in the second degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by entering the PFO conviction, as he neither pled guilty to nor was found guilty of such charge. The appellate court held that, upon defendant's motion to plead guilty to burglary and handgun possession, the trial court held a hearing where it engaged in a thorough Boykin colloquy with defendant concerning the two charges. However, the record further revealed that, at no time did the trial court ever engage in a similar discussion concerning the PFO. Instead, the trial court entered a guilty plea to the PFO charge in spite of defendant's refusal to do so himself. By entering a judgment summarily convicting and sentencing appellant as a PFO, the trial court denied defendant the right to exercise the full panoply of the relevant protections, which due process guaranteed in state criminal proceedings. The court's action was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was vacated, and the case was remanded.

Commonwealth Transp. Cabinet v. Mohney


NO. 2002-CA-000250-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


107 S.W.3d 907; 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 140



February 21, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Ordered Published: June 6, 2003. Released for Publication July 16, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM GRAVES CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 01-XX-00003. HONORABLE JOHN T. DAUGHADAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the context of a charge against appellee motorist for driving on a suspended license, a district court ordered appellant transportation cabinet to reinstate the motorist's driver's license. The Graves Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed that order. The transportation cabinet appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist's license had been suspended in Florida due to driving under the influence (DUI) convictions. The trial court found that the Commonwealth was unable to adequately prove the sufficiency of the Florida DUI convictions, and that the Florida law requiring permanent revocation of the motorist's license was unconstitutional because it was enacted after his conviction for DUI 4th and after he had been issued a Kentucky license. The appellate court ruled a district court was a court of limited jurisdiction and was allowed to exercise original jurisdiction only as provided by the general assembly. A district court did not have jurisdiction to review the transportation cabinet's denial of a driver's license, or to order the transportation cabinet to issue or reinstate an administratively revoked license. Rather, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 186.580(2) vested such jurisdiction in the circuit court. Furthermore, the transportation cabinet was not even a party to the action at the time the district court entered its order. The district court thus erred when it ordered the transportation cabinet to reinstate the motorist's license.


OUTCOME: The judgment which affirmed the order by the district court was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the circuit court with directions to enter an order vacating the district court's order to the extent that it required the cabinet to reinstate the motorist's driver's license.

Dixon v. Commonwealth


NO. 2002-CA-000014-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 2322



November 15, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication.
Review granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Dixon, 2003 Ky. LEXIS 271 (Ky., Dec. 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE CRAIG Z. CLYMER, JUDGE. INDICTMENT NO. 01-CR-00144.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The McCracken Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied defendant's motion for pretrial diversion after defendant entered a guilty plea to two charges of first-degree possession of a controlled substance and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to three drug charges. The trial court sentenced defendant to time in prison, most of which was probated. Thereafter, defendant moved the trial court for pretrial diversion. Although defendant was eligible for pretrial diversion under the applicable statutory law, his trial counsel informed the trial court that the Commonwealth's attorney refused to recommend that defendants participate in pretrial diversion programs. The Commonwealth refused to make a recommendation on pretrial diversion, even though it was statutorily required to do so, because it was following a pretrial diversion protocol that permitted the prosecutor to categorically deny all defendants access to the pretrial diversion program simply by failing to provide a recommendation to the trial court. The trial court denied defendant's motion for pretrial diversion. After that ruling was entered, the appellate court found the denial of defendant's pretrial diversion request had to be vacated and the case had to be remanded so that the Commonwealth could provide a recommendation. It also found that the protocol was unconstitutional since it conflicted with the pretrial diversion statutes.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying defendant's motion for pretrial diversion was vacated and the case was remanded for the Commonwealth to investigate defendant's application for pretrial diversion and provide the trial court with a recommendation concerning defendant's request for it.

Light v. City of Louisville


NOS. 2001-CA-001310-MR AND 2001-CA-001402-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


93 S.W.3d 696; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 2343



September 20, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Published: December 27, 2002.
Ordered published by Light v. City of Louisville, 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 2349 (Ky. Ct. App., Dec. 27, 2002)
Appeal after remand at Light v. City of Louisville, 2005 Ky. App. LEXIS 147 (Ky. Ct. App., July 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 00-CI-001660. HONORABLE LISABETH HUGHES ABRAMSON, JUDGE.
Light v. City of Louisville, 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 2056 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 20, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) dismissed appellant real property owners' action challenging a tax rate fixed by appellee city in levying ad valorem real property taxes after the real property owners filed a class action suit and sought a declaration of rights as well as refunds regarding the claim that the city did not follow certain statutory requirements in setting the tax rate. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city annually levied ad valorem taxes based upon real property assessments of the county property valuation administrator. As a result, the city was required under Kentucky statutory law to satisfy certain prerequisites before increasing the real property tax rate for any given year. The real property owners argued the city failed to timely satisfy such prerequisites for two different tax years. They sought reimbursement for their alleged overpayment. The city denied their claim. The real property owners then filed a class action lawsuit in the trial court. The city moved to dismiss, claimed that the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals was vested with exclusive jurisdiction over the dispute, and claimed the real property owners had failed to first exhaust their administrative remedies. After the trial court dismissed the lawsuit, the appellate court found that the city was not an agency of the state for the purpose of the statutes establishing and implementing the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeal, that the Board did not have exclusive jurisdiction over the action, and that the real property owners exhausted their administrative remedies when they sought a refund from the city.


OUTCOME: The dismissal order was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

R.C. v. Commonwealth


NO. 2001-CA-001080-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


101 S.W.3d 897; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1401



July 12, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 22, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 00-XX-00045. HONORABLE SHEILA R. ISAAC, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Discretionary Review Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed the order of the trial court concluding that appellant father's daughter was an abused child. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The child told her mother the father had sexually abused her. The appellate court held a licensed clinical social worker was not qualified to state an opinion on the child's psychological symptoms or diagnoses, including whether they indicated sexual abuse. An amendment to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 600.020(47) including a licensed clinical social worker in the definition of "qualified mental health professional" did not indicate the general assembly's intention that such a person be qualified as an expert for all purposes. Interpreting the statute to allow a licensed clinical social worker to state an opinion on a psychological diagnosis or symptoms would unconstitutionally usurp the power of the judiciary to decide in a given case whether a proposed expert witness was qualified and would assist the trier of fact. The child's statements to her mother admitted as excited utterances were not admissible given the lack of evidence of the child's state of mind when she made the statements and the remoteness of the original startling event.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

City of Bromley v. Smith


NO. 2001-CA-001440-MR & 2001-CA-001441-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1397



July 5, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Modified January 24, 2003. Released for Publication July 5, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL AND CROSS-APPEAL FROM KENTON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE PATRICIA M. SUMME, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CI-01527.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city councilwoman, the only member to have voted against two tax provisions, brought suit against appellants, the city, its mayor, and its clerk, to have the provisions declared unconstitutional. The Kenton Circuit Court (Kentucky) declared the taxes unconstitutional, but denied class certification and ruled that the councilwoman's entitlement to a refund was governed by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.590. Both sides appealed.

The affected taxpayers were too numerous to permit joinder, their interest in declaratory relief was common, their entitlement to it involved common questions of law and fact, and the councilwoman could adequately represent their interest.

Hinkle v. Commonwealth


NO. 2001-CA-001308-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


104 S.W.3d 778; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1848



June 28, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported in Table Case Format at: 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1386.Ordered Published August 30, 2002. Released for Publication June 13, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM BULLITT CIRCUIT COURT HONORABLE THOMAS WALLER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 98-CR-00024.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Commonwealth of Kentucky filed an action, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.410, seeking forfeiture of proceeds which were derived when appellant homeowner's house was sold in a foreclosure sale. The Bullitt Circuit Court (Kentucky) entered judgment in favor of the Commonwealth and the homeowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1999, a homeowner pled guilty to violating Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 506.080 by facilitating her husband's crime of cultivating marijuana. A few months later, the homeowner and her husband divorced and the homeowner was awarded the marital residence. The homeowner made payments on two mortgages until early 2001 when she defaulted on the second mortgage and the house was sold at public auction. Immediately thereafter, the Commonwealth moved for forfeiture of almost $ 55,000 of the sale proceeds, the amount remaining after satisfaction of the first mortgage. The appellate court held that (1) because the homeowner's husband pled guilty to felony cultivating and the evidence established that the homeowner facilitated that crime, the trial court ruled correctly that the property was subject to forfeiture; (2) the Commonwealth's action was not barred by the statute of limitations; (3) as the proponent of the forfeiture, the Commonwealth had the burden of proving the forfeiture's propriety; and (4) the trial court erred by ordering the forfeiture without considering whether it was proportionate, given the homeowner's crime and her post-offense payments on her mortgages.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for additional proceedings so that the trial court could assess the proportionality of the forfeiture.

Scott v. Scott


NO. 2001-CA-000447-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


80 S.W.3d 447; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1275



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM HENDERSON CIRCUIT COURT. CIVIL ACTION NO. 01-CI-00069. HONORABLE STEPHEN A. HAYDEN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATING AND REMANDING. DENYING MOTION FOR SANCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents appealed an order by the Henderson Circuit Court (Kentucky) that awarded appellee grandparents visitation with their daughter, claiming that award, pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021, was an unconstitutional interference with their right to raise their child as they saw fit.


OVERVIEW: The trial court presumed that the child would ordinarily benefit from contact with his or her grandparents and that grandparents and grandchildren normally had a special bond that could not be denied. The appellate court held that when the trial court engaged in a presumption contrary to the wishes of the parents and granted their decision no deference, it infringed on the parents' fundamental right as parents to raise their daughter as they saw fit. The result was an unconstitutional application of Kentucky's grandparent visitation statute, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 405.021. Grandparent visitation could only be granted over the objections of otherwise fit custodial parents if it was shown by clear and convincing evidence that harm to the child would result from a deprivation of visitation with the grandparents.


OUTCOME: The order was vacated and remanded for further proceedings.

Thacker v. Commonwealth


NO. 2001-CA-001321-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


80 S.W.3d 451; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1276



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NOS. 01-CR-00029 & 01-CR-00152. HONORABLE JOHN ADAMS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to suppress evidence against him that was obtained through the use of the Kentucky all schedules prescription electronic reporting system (KASPER) authorized by Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.202. After the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) denied defendant's motion, defendant pleaded guilty to several counts of obtaining, and several counts of attempting to obtain, a controlled substance by means of fraud. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While arresting defendant for driving under the influence, a police officer found prescription drug containers for controlled medications and learned that defendant had been charged regarding prescription forgery. A detective then requested a KASPER report which described defendant's prescription activity in Kentucky and showed that defendant had been issued overlapping prescriptions. The detective then questioned defendant's doctors about the prescriptions. The appellate court held that, contrary to defendant's contention on appeal, the detective's use of the KASPER-derived information was not an unreasonable search and seizure under U.S. Const. amend. IV or Ky. Const. § 10. Instead, the administrative search exception to the warrant and probable cause requirements applied because the State had a substantial interest in tracing drug distributions, the KASPER system reasonably advanced that interest, and Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.202(6) clearly allowed only limited police inspection and properly restrained officers' discretion. The detective did not violate the confidentiality provisions of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.202(6) since he did not disclose the KASPER report to anyone.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Jones v. Lathram


NO. 1999-CA-002231-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 1278



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication June 21, 2002.
Review granted by Jones v. Lathram, 2003 Ky. LEXIS 101 (Ky., May 15, 2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Jones v. Lathram, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 218 (Ky., Sept. 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REMAND FROM KENTUCKY SUPREME COURT, NO. 2001-SC-000031-DG. APPEAL FROM GRAVES CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 94-CI-00207. HONORABLE JOHN T. DAUGHADAY, JUDGE.
Jones v. Lathram, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 43 (Ky., Mar. 15, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Kentucky Supreme Court, plaintiff executrix appealed a grant of summary judgment by the Graves Circuit Court in favor of defendant police trooper, claiming that the trooper was not entitled to qualified immunity in the operation of his cruiser.


OVERVIEW: The trooper received what he perceived to be an emergency call for assistance from a fellow trooper and activated his cruiser's blue lights and siren. As the trooper entered a "blind" intersection, his cruiser collided with a truck driven by the decedent. The appellate court held on remand that the trial court properly entered summary judgment in favor of the trooper. When the trooper responded in good faith to what he perceived to be an emergency call for his assistance, he was required to evaluate the situation, to make a serious judgment, and to exercise a degree of discretion wholly distinct in character from that of other lay operators of motor vehicles. Because he was responding to an emergency call for assistance presenting the potential for a life-or-death crisis, he was entitled to qualified official immunity.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

 

567 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


James v. Wilson


1999-CA-000787-MR, 1999-CA-001209-MR, 1999-CA-002172-MR, 2000-CA-001379-MR, 2000-CA-001382-MR, 2000-CA-001491-MR, 2000-CA-001687-MR, 2000-CA-001688-MR, 2000-CA-001690-MR, 2000-CA-001862-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


95 S.W.3d 875; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 770



April 19, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM MCCRACKEN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. SHADOAN, SPECIAL JUDGE. CIVIL ACTIONS NO. 98-CI-01154 and 99-CI-00352.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a student stole a gun and fired into a group at his high school, killing three students, appellants, decedents' parents, sued appellees, shooter's parents, classmates, gun owner, and school personnel, alleging, inter alia, negligence. The McCracken Circuit Court, Kentucky, dismissed the complaints against the classmates and the school employees and granted summary judgment to the other appellees. The decedents' parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedents' parents argued on appeal, inter alia, that the school personnel were not immune from suit and that genuine issues of material fact existed as to the negligence of (1) the gun owner in the way he stored his gun, (2) the shooter's parents in failing to control their son, and (3) the classmates in not warning someone that the shooter had previously brought guns to school. The appellate court held that qualified official immunity protected the school employees because their allegedly negligent omissions, such as failing to enact safety rules to protect students, involved discretionary functions, and there was no evidence of bad faith. The gun owner was not negligent, as he stored his gun in unloaded condition in a hard plastic case and had no duty to anticipate that the shooter would steal it to shoot students. The shooter's parents were not negligent, as the shooter was not under their control at the time of his illegal acts and there was no evidence that the shooter had previously exhibited violent tendencies toward anyone. The classmates were not liable, as there was no special relationship between the parties, and the incident in question was not foreseeable.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgments.

 

568 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Neal


NO. 2000-CA-002744-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


84 S.W.3d 920; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 586



March 29, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 29, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 97-CR-000030. HONORABLE TOM MCDONALD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for possession of a handgun by a convicted felon, and the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted defendant's motion to suppress. The State filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allowed an officer to enter his residence. After entering the residence, the officer stated he had an arrest warrant for another individual. Defendant allowed the officer to search a jacket, which defendant stated was his, wherein the officer found a firearm. The trial court found defendant's consent to search the jacket was not voluntary because of the officer's statement that he had a warrant. The appellate court found it was error for the trial court to rely, as a matter of law, on a finding in another case that a consent to search given after an officer stated he had a search warrant was too subject to coercion to be voluntary. The trial court's factual findings failed to address the voluntariness of defendant's consent to search, and additional findings of fact based on a preponderance of the evidence from the totality of all the circumstances as to whether the consent to search was freely and voluntarily given were required.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was vacated, and the matter was remanded for additional findings of fact.

Lewis v. Ky. Ret. Sys.


NO. 2000-CA-002859-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


104 S.W.3d 762; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 454



March 15, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion to Reconsider Denied May 24, 2002. Released for Publication July 11, 2003.
Review granted by Ky. Ret. Sys. v. Lewis, 2003 Ky. LEXIS 222 (Ky., Sept. 10, 2003)
Opinion withdrawn by Lewis v. Ky. Ret. Sys., 2003 Ky. App. LEXIS 316 (Ky. Ct. App., Sept. 12, 2003)
Review granted by Lewis v. Ky. Ret. Sys., 2004 Ky. LEXIS 30 (Ky., Feb. 11, 2004)
Reversed by Ky. Ret. Sys. v. Lewis, 163 S.W.3d 1, 2005 Ky. LEXIS 85 (Ky., 2005)
Withdrawn by publisher


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CI-01212.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied. Order of dismissal is reversed, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee's application for disability retirement benefits was denied by defendant state employees retirement systems. The employee filed a declaratory judgment action to compel the retirement system to follow statutory guidelines in processing the application. The Franklin Circuit Court, Kentucky, dismissed for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court agreed with the retirement system that that 105 Ky. Admin. Regs. 1:210, §§ 6, 7, allowed applications to be submitted to a single medical examiner with an appeal to a hearing officer under 105 Ky. Admin. Regs. 1:210, §§ 9, 10. However, the appellate court also found that as Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 61.665(2)(e) existed when the employee filed her claim, in the case of denials, the retirement system was required to submit the employee's application to two additional medical examiners. Thus, the employee's request that the other medical examiners review the case was the correct procedure. Skipping the procedure and setting the matter for a hearing was premature and ultra vires. Because the retirement system was following the wrong procedure, the trial court should not have dismissed the complaint and should have remanded for a decision under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 61.665(2)(e) by a second, and possibly a third medical examiner.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgement was reversed and remanded; the retirement system's motion to dismiss was denied.

Commonwealth v. Bryant


NO. 2001-CA-000264-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 138



January 25, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, February 11, 2004. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered not to be Published. [*1] 
Review denied and ordered not published by Bryant v. Commonwealth, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 27 (Ky., Feb. 11, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM TODD CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE TYLER L. GILL, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 00-CR-00079.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed the order of the Todd Circuit Court (Kentucky) which found Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1432(1)(b) unconstitutionally vague and overbroad and dismissed the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for possession of chemicals or equipment for manufacturing methamphetamine with the intent to manufacture methamphetamine. Defendant filed a motion to declare Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1432(1)(b) unconstitutional and dismiss the indictment. On appeal, the appellate court noted that under the statute, possession of certain household substances was only illegal if the actor possessed them with the intent to use them to manufacture methamphetamine. Hence, the appellate court concluded the statute was not overbroad as seeking to regulate legally protected conduct. Likewise, the appellate court did not believe the statute was void for vagueness. The appellate court advised that criminal statutes must be sufficiently specific that an individual had fair notice of what conduct was forbidden. As to the statute at issue, although it did not precisely state what conduct would indicate an intent to manufacture methamphetamine, the appellate court believed enough of a standard of conduct was defined that an ordinary person would know what conduct was prohibited and that arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement would not result.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order and remanded the matter with directions to reinstate the indictment.

Sherfey v. Sherfey


NO. 2001-CA-000519-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


74 S.W.3d 777; 2002 Ky. App. LEXIS 36



January 18, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 7, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Sherfey v. Sherfey, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 664 (U.S. Jan. 13, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 00-CI-00093. HONORABLE JAMES G. WEDDLE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged the judgment of the Monroe Circuit Court (Kentucky) which awarded custody of their son to appellee grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued on appeal: (1) whether the grandparents met the "de facto custodian" time requirement; (2) whether Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.270(1) unconstitutionally infringed on their fundamental rights; and (3) whether the trial court's findings were clearly erroneous or whether its custody decision was an abuse of discretion. The appellate court determined the son spent roughly two years under the care and custody of the grandparents prior to the filing of the action. Accordingly, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's finding of de facto custodianship by the grandparents. In addition, as applied to the parents, the appellate court did not believe the passage of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.270(1) significantly altered the preexisting law of custody determination in Kentucky. Further, the appellate court found that a finding of unfitness would have been warranted in the case; thus, it could not be held that the parents' constitutional rights were violated. Finally, the appellate court held the trial court's factual findings were clearly supported by substantial evidence and its custody ruling based on those factual findings was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

W. Ky. Coca-Cola Bottling Co. v. Revenue Cabinet


NO. 2000-CA-002883-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


80 S.W.3d 787; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 1262



December 21, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER L. CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. CIVIL ACTION NO. 00-CI-00580.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Franklin Circuit Court, Kentucky, reversed a decision of the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals, affirming the assessment of sales tax against appellant bottling company in favor of appellee Kentucky Revenue Cabinet and board. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company argued that assessing sales tax against them was in error, because a post exchange was a federal instrumentality and sales to it were immune from the imposition of state sales tax under 4 U.S.C.S. § 107 of the Buck Act, 4 U.S.C.S. §§ 105-110. Post exchanges and similar facilities were arms of the government which were essential for the performance of government functions and partook of whatever immunities were provided under the Constitution and federal statutes. The exchange was an instrumentality within the purview of the Buck Act exception. There were no third parties involved in the transaction between the company and the exchange. The state was therefore without authority to tax the sale of canned soft drinks by the company to the exchange for resale to authorized persons. No credible argument could be made that the exchange was not an instrumentality of the federal government.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

573 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Consalvi v. Cawood


NO. 2000-CA-001963-MR, NO. 2001-CA-000010-MR, NO. 2001-CA-000037-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


63 S.W.3d 195; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 1258



December 14, 2001, Rendered  
December 14, 2001, Entered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEALS FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SHEILA R. ISAAC, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CI-01694. CROSS-APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SHEILA R. ISAAC, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CI-01694.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED ON DIRECT APPEALS. DISMISSED CROSS-APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) entered a final judgment finding appellee former husband was a de facto custodian with regard to appellant former wife's two minor children under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.270, and thus, that he had the same standing in a marital separation proceeding as a natural parent. The former wife appealed, and the former husband cross-appealed the award of joint custody to the parties instead of sole custody to him.


OVERVIEW: The former wife and the former husband married after the former wife gave birth to a child. The parties had a difficult relationship. During one of their separations, the former wife began a relationship with another man. The parties then reconciled, but by then the former wife was already pregnant again. The parties then made a final separation. A temporary joint custody order was entered. Shortly thereafter, a paternity test revealed the former husband was not either child's natural father. The trial court then held a hearing, and after finding the children had an established relationship with the former husband and it would be in their best interests to continue it, ordered joint custody. The trial court made the order after concluding the former husband was a de facto guardian under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 403.270. After judgment was entered accordingly, the appellate court found the husband was not a de facto guardian under the statute, as he was not the primary caregiver for the children. The statute required the caregiver stand in place of the natural parent to be a de facto custodian, and the evidence only showed he had provided some care to them.


OUTCOME: The judgment that the former husband was a de facto custodian of the two minor children under the statute was reversed. As the effect of that ruling was that the former husband did not have the same standing as a natural parent would have in the parties' marital separation proceeding, the cross-appeal denying the former husband sole custody of the children was dismissed.

Fields v. Lexington-Fayette Urban County Gov't


NO. 2000-CA-000062-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


91 S.W.3d 110; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 1253



December 7, 2001, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. ACTION NO. 94-CI-01121. HONORABLE GARY D. PAYNE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pedestrian sued defendants, county government and abutting landowner, for injuries suffered when she fell on a sidewalk. The Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) granted both defendants' motions for summary judgment. The pedestrian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the pedestrian's claim against the county government based on the doctrine of sovereign immunity. It dismissed the claim against the abutting landowner because it held that the abutting landowner owed no duty to the pedestrian. The court of appeals agreed with the trial court. The pedestrian argued that because when the county government was created and the prior city government was abolished, the county retained a former city ordinance that required an abutting landowner to maintain a sidewalk, liability could be imposed on the landowner and on the county government. The court of appeals disagreed because even though liability could have been imposed on the city, the city no longer existed and the county was immune from suit on the ground of sovereign immunity. The court of appeals also agreed that under the law of the commonwealth, an abutting land owner had no liability to a pedestrian who was injured on a sidewalk. The pedestrian argued that under the jural rights doctrine, her claim could be maintained against the county government. The court of appeals disagreed because the jural rights doctrine did not trump sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Franklin Roofing, Inc. v. Eagle Roofing & Sheet Metal, Inc.


NO. 2000-CA-000241-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


61 S.W.3d 239; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 1163



November 16, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 3, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM MADISON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JULIA H. ADAMS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 96-CI-00279.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Kentucky roofing company sued appellant Ohio roofing company in the Madison Circuit Court (Kentucky), seeking a judgment that no contract existed between the parties. The trial court denied the Ohio company's motion to dismiss, and judgment was entered for the Kentucky company. The Ohio company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Ohio company inquired of a supplier about other roofing companies that could complete a project in its home state. The supplier informed the Kentucky company, and it contacted the Ohio company. The companies negotiated a contract which the Kentucky company declined to execute shortly before the job was to begin, and the Ohio company was provided restitution under the Kentucky company's performance bond. The Ohio company had no office or agent in Kentucky. This was the only contractual relationship the parties had ever had. The Ohio company did not purposefully avail itself of the privilege of acting within Kentucky, as it never traveled or solicited business there. The evidence did not show the Ohio company reached beyond its home state to create continuing relationships and obligations with the Kentucky company. The contract price in the parties' agreement did not qualify as a "substantial connection" with the forum state because jurisdiction was not reasonably imposed on a non-resident defendant based on a contract price which might never reach the forum state. The Ohio company was not an "active buyer," nor could it foresee being sued in the forum state.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded for an order of dismissal.

Commonwealth v. Arndell


NO. 2000-CA-002426-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 1164



November 16, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Vacated by, Remanded by Arndell v. Commonwealth, 2003 Ky. LEXIS 239 (Ky., Oct. 15, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CALDWELL CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE BILL CUNNINGHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CR-00064.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Caldwell Circuit Court, Kentucky, granted judgment in favor of defendant by adjudging that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1432(1)(b) was unconstitutional. The Commonwealth of Kentucky appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth contended that the trial court erred in finding Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1432(1)(b), which criminalized the possession of chemicals or equipment for the manufacture of methamphetamine with the intent to manufacture methamphetamine, unconstitutional. Because there was no constitutional right to possess chemicals or equipment with the intent of using such to manufacture methamphetamine, the statute could not be attacked on the ground that it was overbroad as attempting to regulate constitutionally permissible conduct. The statute was not overbroad as seeking to regulate legally protected conduct associated with the possession and utilization of over-the-counter drugs for their intended purposes. There was no basis for finding that the statute was unconstitutional as being void for vagueness. The classification of methamphetamine as an illegal substance or dangerous drug was not improper. There was nothing in the statute's language which would prevent an ordinary person of reasonable intelligence from understanding what conduct it prohibited. The statute clearly applied to defendant's conduct on the date he was arrested.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Howard Baer. Inc. v. Schave


NO. 1999-CA-001969-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 590



August 17, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Reported in Table Case Format at: 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 597.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CLARK CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM T. JENNINGS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 97-CI-00342.
Howard Baer, Inc. v. Schave, 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 597 (Ky. Ct. App., Aug. 17, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee brought an action against his company and two individuals also employed at the company, defendants, alleging that the company had discriminated against him on the basis of disability and that it had retaliated against him for filing a workers' compensation claim. The Clark Circuit Court, Kentucky, awarded the employee compensatory damages for emotional distress and punitive damages. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court found that the trial court did not err by refusing to grant the company's motion for directed verdict because the jury's determination that the employee was either disabled or regarded as disabled by the company was supported by substantial evidence. Even if he was not in fact disabled, the evidence showed that he was regarded as being unable to work for the company, and hence, was discriminated against on that basis; the company had no legitimate reason for its action, and its action had no rational relationship to whether the employee could perform his duties. The appellate court also found that the jury acted properly in awarding punitive damages since employment discrimination qualified as an intentional tort. Furthermore, the employee met his burden in proving that the company's conduct warranted punitive damages. However, the trial court should have granted the individual defendants' motion to dismiss because their status as fellow employees did not constitute an "employer" within the meaning of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 344.030(2); thus, they could not have been held personally liable under the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in regard to the individual defendants' liability, but was otherwise affirmed.

Codell v. D.F.


NO. 1998-CA-002895-MR, NO. 1998-CA-002897-MR, NO. 1998-CA-003069-MR, NO. 1998-CA-003176-MR, NO. 1998-CA-003177-MR, NO. 1998-CA-003178-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 71



June 22, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Review or Rehearing granted: D.F. v. Codell, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 205 (Ky. Oct. 9, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CALLOWAY CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DENNIS FOUST, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 95-CI-00056.

CROSS-APPEAL FROM CALLOWAY CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DENNIS FAUST, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 95-CI-00056.
Codell v. D.F., 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 493 (Ky. Ct. App., June 22, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee parent's action on behalf of a minor, to determine the "No Pass-No Drive" law's, Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 159.051, constitutionality was certified as a class action. The Calloway Circuit Court (Kentucky) determined it to be unconstitutional and violative of the Family Education Rights and Privacy Act of 1974 (FERPA). Appellants, Kentucky officials, sought review. Parent cross-appealed in regard to two rulings for officials.


OVERVIEW: The "No Pass-No Drive" law operated to suspend the driver's license of any 16 or 17-year-old student who dropped out of school or was deemed academically deficient. Parent sued and for the most part won. The appellate court held that judicial review under the law was properly limited to clerical errors, not teacher assessments. Procedural due process was not violated because the interest here was a legitimately regulated privilege, not a fundamental right. The Transportation Cabinet's Form TC94-30 regarding parental consent was made to further enforcement of the law; thus it was not impermissible legislating in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13A.130. The circuit court correctly relied on the Family Policy Compliance Office's letter opining that § 159.051 violated FERPA's privacy provisions. But that violation did not operate to strike § 159.051, rather it only related to loss of federal funding. The threat of losing driving privileges was an incentive to stay in school, thus the statute was rationally related to its objective and did not violate substantive due process. Equal protection was not violated because the statute provided for students' different academic abilities.


OUTCOME: The judgments that the statute neither denied meaningful judicial review nor violated procedural due process, but that it did violate federal law, were affirmed. The judgments that the statute violated substantive due process and equal protection, and that the Transportation Cabinet illegally legislated via memorandum, were reversed. The case was remanded.

Louisville Water Co. v. Phelps


NO. 1999-CA-000214-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 61



May 18, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Review or Rehearing granted: Phelps v. Louisville Water Co., 2001 Ky. LEXIS 228 (Ky. Dec. 12, 2001).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ANN SHAKE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 97-CI-001627.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, estates of the decedents, filed suit against the appellant water company and the company which provided signs and barricades to appellant water company, seeking compensatory and punitive damages. The jury in the Jefferson Circuit Court, Kentucky, returned a verdict in favor of appellees. Appellant water company challenged the award.


OVERVIEW: The decedents were riding in a car that crashed into a barricaded construction site where appellant water company was working. Appellant contended that it was a municipal corporation and, as such, could not be liable for punitive damages. Appellees asserted that appellant water company was not in any way, shape or form a municipality or a municipal agent. The general rule was that no punitive damages against a municipality were allowed unless expressly authorized by statute. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 65.2002 did not expressly authorize punitive damages. Appellant also contended that the trial court erred in its rulings on subsequent remedial measures. The appellate court, however, found no abuse of discretion. Finally, there was no manifest error in the trial court's denial of appellant water company's motion for a mistrial after an employee was asked about placement of a flashing arrow board at the accident scene.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in regard to the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for mistrial, as well as the denial of appellant's motion to exclude evidence of subsequent remedial measures. The judgment was reversed with respect to the punitive damage award against appellant.

Bobbie Preece Facility v. Commonwealth


NO. 2000-CA-001393-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


71 S.W.3d 99; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 54

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CI-00893.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought administrative review by appellee state regulatory agency of a denial by appellee of a gaming facility license renewal to appellant. Appellee affirmed the denial of the license. Appellant sought review of the decision in the Franklin County Circuit Court (Kentucky). The trial court affirmed the decision. Appellant challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned a building and operated charitable gaming activities in that building. She also operated a business that distributed gaming equipment. Appellee notified appellant that because of the change to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 238.530(3), as amended effective April 1, 1998, she would no longer be able to operate both businesses. DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the order of the Bullitt Circuit Court, Kentucky, granting summary judgment to appellee, declaring a license tax ordinance unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The City of Lebanon, Kentucky appealed an order granting summary judgment to a cellular business doing business within the city, and in the process declaring unconstitutional an ordinance imposing a license tax upon persons, firms, or corporations engaged in commercial transmission of voice, picture, or data by non-land line means within the city limits using structures 30 feet or more in height. The tax paid by appellee under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. 136.120 was both a franchise assessment and an ad valorem tax. City was thus prohibited from additionally the taxing business under its ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

State Dock, Inc. v. Revenue Cabinet


NO. 1999-CA-001798-MR, NO. 1999-CA-001800-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 19



February 23, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Application for Rehearing Denied May 4, 2001.
Review or Rehearing granted: State Dock, Inc. v. Revenue Cabinet, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 84 (Ky. Apr. 26, 2002).
Review granted by State Dock, Inc. v. Revenue Cabinet, 2002 Ky. LEXIS 84 (Ky., Apr. 26, 2002)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Popplewell's Alligator Dock No. 1, Inc. v. Revenue Cabinet, 2004 Ky. LEXIS 92 (Ky., Apr. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER L. CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 97-CI-01543. APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE ROGER L. CRITTENDEN, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 98-CI-01578.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO NO. 1999-CA-001800-MR AND REMANDED AS TO NO. 1999-CA-001798-MR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the first of two consolidated cases, the Kentucky Board of Tax Appeals upheld an assessment of sales and use tax against appellant marina operator. The Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) affirmed, and appellant marina operator sought review. In the second case, appellant taxpayer's complaint and petition for declaration of rights were dismissed for failure to exhaust administrative remedies, and appellant taxpayer sought review.


OVERVIEW: In the first case, appellant marina operator leased luxury houseboats to the public. Appellant marina operator collected and remitted sales tax on the rental of the houseboats but did not collect or remit sales and use tax on its sale of gasoline used to power the leased vessels. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 139.483 exempted from excise taxes fuel consumed in operation of ships and vessels used in transportation of property or conveyance of persons for hire, but the trial court found the exemption did not apply to appellant marina operator's sale of gasoline. The appellate court agreed that the exemption did not apply because a lessee's principal use of a leased houseboat was not the transportation of property or the conveyance of persons for hire. Section 139.483 was not unconstitutional as applied. In the second case, in which appellant taxpayer claimed its houseboat leases were exempt from sales and use tax, the trial court erred in dismissing the action for failure to pursue administrative remedies because the only issue was the applicability of the § 139.483 exemption.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in the first case because appellant marina operator's sale of gasoline for use in the leased houseboats was not tax exempt. The dismissal of the second action was reversed and remanded because the trial court improperly declined jurisdiction.

 

584 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Donovan v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-002440-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


60 S.W.3d 581; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 13



February 9, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 13, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS B. WINE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 96-CR-001668.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) requiring him to pay a recoupment fee for his court appointed counsel after he was acquitted of all charges.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was acquitted on rape charges, and after trial, the court ordered him to pay his court-appointed attorney fees. Under Ky. Rev. Stat. § 31.120(4), the court assessed a recoupment fee against a defendant who was represented by the Department of Public Advocacy where the defendant had the ability to make such a payment. Appellant contended that he could not pay the amount ordered, and that the statute was unconstitutional; thus the court abused its discretion. The appeals court affirmed assessment. A recoupment fee was only assessed after the representation was complete, and only where the defendant could afford to pay a percentage of the defense costs on reasonable terms. All defendants were treated equally, and those who were capable of paying the recoupment fee could have it assessed against them. The fee was not a penalty, but was merely a partial recoupment of the costs expended by the state to protect those in need.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed. The court was statutorily mandated to impose the recoupment fee against all indigent defendants, based upon their ability to pay. The statute made no exception for persons who are charged and subsequently acquitted or whose charges are dismissed, and was not unconstitutional.

 

585 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Cocke


NO. 1999-CA-002135-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


58 S.W.3d 891; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 1166



January 19, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Denied and Ordered Published By Kentucky Supreme Court: November 14, 2001; 2001-SC-000133-D. Released for Publication November 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE THOMAS J. KNOPF, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 98-CR-002555.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court, Kentucky, dismissed several counts of an indictment against defendant and declared Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 434.845(1)(c) to be void for vagueness. The Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth contended that the trial court erred by finding that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 434.845(1)(c) was unconstitutional. The Commonwealth argued that the trial court erred by agreeing with defendant's contention that the statute, as enacted, lacked an essential requirement mandating that the offense of unlawful access to a computer cannot occur unless the alteration, damage or destruction at issue was committed without authorization. Upholding the Commonwealth's argument would result in a situation where both authorized and unauthorized persons could be prosecuted for first-degree unlawful access as a result of the alteration, damage, or destruction of a computer and/or related components and systems, even though the alteration, damage, or destruction could have been caused by an authorized person with the permission or at the request of the computer's owner. The statute was void for vagueness as an authorized user could not ascertain specifically what alteration, damage or destruction was prohibited. Nothing in Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 434.845(2) prevented an authorized user from being prosecuted under § 434.845(1)(c) for innocent alterations made in good faith.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

586 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Restaurant Ventures v. Lexington-Fayette Urban County Gov't


NO. 1999-CA-000834-MR, NO. 1999-CA-001093-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


60 S.W.3d 572; 2001 Ky. App. LEXIS 2



January 5, 2001, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Denied December 12, 2001. Released for Publication December 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JOHN ADAMS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 97-CI-02330.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART and REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs and defendants sought review of the Fayette County (Kentucky) Circuit Court decision ruling certain ordinances regulating adult entertainment constitutional and other portions unconstitutional pursuant to the U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, adult entertainment establishments and their employees, sued defendants, challenging the constitutionality of ordinances enacted by defendant county. The ordinances regulated activities within the establishments, personnel qualifications, licensing requirements, and hours of operation. The trial court upheld certain parts of the ordinances and struck down others as unconstitutional. Both parties appealed. The court affirmed in part, upholding the ordinances in their entirety. The provisions of the ordinances were content neutral. Defendant county's interest was in combating the secondary effects of adult entertainment establishments. It was not the message of eroticism that was censored but the act that conveyed the message. The line between prohibited conduct and permitted conduct was clearly drawn by the ordinance. No equal protection violation existed concerning advertisement merely because plaintiffs were placed in a different classification than other businesses which sold alcoholic beverages. The classification was rationally related to the unique problems involved in advertising adult entertainment. Stage requirements were not unduly burdensome.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part because stage requirements were not unduly burdensome and affirmed in part because other provisions were rationally related to defendant county's legitimate interests in combating the secondary effects of adult entertainment.

 

587 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Peak v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-001949-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


34 S.W.3d 80; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 149



November 22, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 5, 2001.
Post-conviction relief denied at Peak v. Commonwealth, 2005 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 857 (Ky. Ct. App., May 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM BUTLER CIRCUIT COURT HONORABLE RONNIE DORTCH, JUDGE ACTION NO. 97-CR-00059.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the Butler Circuit Court (Kentucky) for marijuana cultivation of five or more plants, arguing the trial court erred when it refused to allow him to present a medical necessity or lesser evil defense and by refusing to instruct the jury on those defenses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of marijuana cultivation, second offense, in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 218A.1423 and was sentenced to seven years in prison. He appealed, arguing the trial court erred when it refused to allow him to present a medical necessity or lesser evil defense based on chronic problems of depression and headaches, and when it refused to instruct the jury on those defenses. The court held in order for the choice of evils defense to be available, appellant was required to show his conduct was necessitated by an imminent threat of injury to his person under circumstances which left him no reasonable and viable alternative, other than violating the law for which he was charged. The court noted appellant did not present evidence that he did not have reasonable alternatives to cultivating marijuana as a means of medical treatment for his physical ailments. Therefore the court affirmed, holding because he did not meet his burden of proof the trial court was not required to instruct the jury on the choice of evils defense.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because appellant failed to meet his burden of proving his conduct was necessitated by a specific, imminent threat of injury under circumstances which left him no reasonable alternative, other than violating the law for which he was charged; therefore, he was not entitled to the instruction.

Sizemore v. Madison County Fiscal Court


NO. 1999-CA-000962-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


58 S.W.3d 887; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 158



November 22, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Denied and Ordered Published By Kentucky Supreme Court; November 14, 2001 (2000-Sc-001120-d). Released for Publication November 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MADISON CIRCUIT COURT HONORABLE JULIA H. ADAMS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 98-CI-00516.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Madison Circuit Court, Kentucky, granted judgment in favor of appellee county by holding that a proposed mobile home park was subject to state and county subdivision requirements. Appellant owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that the trial court erred in concluding that subdivision regulations applied to the development of a mobile home park. He argued that the proposed development did not constitute a subdivision within the meaning of the statutes and regulations because he had no intention of selling the divided lots. Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 100.111(22) was unequivocal. Nothing in the definitions required that divided lots be offered or developed solely for sale in order to constitute a subdivision of property. The statute's intent was to give local government the power to control the subdivision of land in order to protect its citizens in matters of public safety, health, and welfare. The owner had partitioned the property as part of his intent to develop it. The owner had not sought approval for a development, and did not establish a sufficient basis for review that regulations would be unconstitutional. The owner failed formally to apply to the county for approval of his proposed development. The county did not wrongfully induce the owner to act to his detriment. He had access to the statutes and regulations at issue and was chargeable with notice of the proper procedure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

United Sign, Ltd. v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-002740-MR, NO. 1999-CA-002757-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


44 S.W.3d 794; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 126



October 27, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied December 1, 200. Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, June 7, 2001. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered to be Published. Released for Publication June 8, 2001.
Subsequent appeal at United Sign, Ltd. v. Commonwealth, 2003 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 37 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM ROCKCASTLE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DANIEL J. VENTERS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 97-CI-00162. APPEAL FROM ROCKCASTLE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE DANIEL J. VENTERS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 97-CI-00159.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Rockcastle Circuit Court (Kentucky) granting summary judgment in favor of appellee in appellee's action seeking to compel removal of appellants' billboards erected without a permit within 660 feet of the right-of-way of an interstate highway.


OVERVIEW: Appellants erected six billboards within 660 feet of a right-of-way of an interstate highway without obtaining a permit from appellee in violation of the Billboard Act (Act), Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 177.841(1). Appellee filed suit to compel appellants to remove the billboards. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee having determined that appellants' billboards were illegal per se. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that appellee's administrative regulations requiring permits did not exceed the authority delegated to appellee because Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 177.860 showed the legislature's intent for appellee to adopt regulations to promote highway safety and preserve the scenic beauty of the area surrounding the highways. The permit requirements were rationally related to the Act's objectives because without them, anyone could erect a billboard that could impair drivers' visibility and destroy the scenic beauty. The court held appellee was permitted to conduct administrative hearings for the benefit of persons aggrieved by its actions under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13B.010-170.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Because appellee had the authority to issue permit regulations and those regulations were valid, and because appellants erected their billboards without receiving permits from appellee, the trial court properly determined that appellants' billboards were illegal per se and granted appellee's motion for summary judgment.

Commonwealth v. Hager


NO. 1999-CA-001543-DG


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


35 S.W.3d 377; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 121



October 20, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 9, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SHEILA ISAAC, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 98-XX-112.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed the Fayette Circuit Court's (Kentucky) reversal of the district court's decision that the term "habitual truant" did not need to be defined in jury instructions in appellee's trial for unlawful transaction with a minor pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 530.070(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with unlawful transaction with a minor pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 530.070(1)(c), as a result of her children's habitual truancy. It was asserted that appellee's children had been absent from school an excessive number of times during their educational years. Defense counsel requested that the trial court dismiss the charges on the ground that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 600.020(25) was unconstitutionally vague, in that the term "habitual truant" was not defined. The trial court denied the motion. "Truant" was a term of common usage, and one which the jury could have been expected to understand without a formal definition. The jury did not evidence any lack of understanding of the term "habitual truant." Under such circumstances, the lack of a formal definition constituted harmless error.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. The failure to define "habitual truant" for the jury was harmless error since the term was of common usage, and the jury did not show any lack of understanding of the term.
