Barker v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-000500-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


32 S.W.3d 515; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 111



September 29, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 21, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CLARK CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM T. JENNINGS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 98-CR-00064.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Clark County Circuit Court (Kentucky), denying his motion to moving to suppress the blood alcohol results or to amend the operating a motor vehicle under the influence of alcohol charge to a misdemeanor because the consent statute was void-for-vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for suspected operating a motor vehicle under the influence of alcohol (DUI). He was administered a blood alcohol test which indicated a blood alcohol concentration of 0.26. Thereafter, appellant was indicted for DUI III, a felony. Appellant argued that when Ky. Rev. Stat. § 189A.010 was construed with Ky. Rev. Stat. § 189A.105, the implied consent statute, an irreconcilable conflict resulted rendering the statutory scheme void-for-vagueness. Appellant insisted that the warning that refusal to submit to the blood alcohol test would have resulted in revocation of his driving privilege was insufficient to inform him, a third time offender, that he could have been subject to a felony conviction and that additional warnings should have been supplemented. The statute addressed strictly the notion of implied consent and the penalty for noncompliance therewith. The statute was not vague as it provided the minimal guidance necessary to avoid arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement. Thus, appellant's conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant insisted that warning that refusal to submit to blood alcohol test would have resulted in revocation of his driving privilege was insufficient to inform him, third time offender, that he could have been subject to felony operating a motor vehicle under influence of alcohol conviction. Court held that statute addressing issue of implied consent was not vague. Thus, appellant's conviction affirmed.

Bluegrass Boarding and Training Kennels v. Jefferson County Fiscal Court


NO. 1999-CA-001407-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


26 S.W.3d 801; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 93



August 25, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 6, 2000. Released for Publication October 13, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM JEFFERSON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE JAMES M. SHAKE, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 98-CI-003853.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant kennels challenged the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Kentucky) upholding the constitutionality of Jefferson County, Ky., Ordinance No. 46, § 91.075 (1996) requiring that kennel and cattery owners divulge the names and addresses of pet owners to the Department of Animal Control upon request.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were boarding kennels located in Jefferson County, which boarded domesticated dogs and cats. Appellants alleged that Jefferson County, Ky., Ordinance No. 46, § 91.075 (1996) requiring appellants to provide pet owner's name and home address to appellee Department of Animal Control was unconstitutional because it invaded the privacy of the kennel owners and its clients, violated equal protection, and was vague. The public interest in rabies prevention outweighed the privacy interest an individual pet owner boarding his pet in a kennel or cattery had in his home address being furnished to the department. The county fiscal court had the right to enact more stringent rabies prevention measures than those of other counties; thus, the ordinance did not violate the equal protection clause. Also, the ordinance was not impermissibly vague, as a pet owner could readily determine that his pet was required to have a license to be boarded and was on notice that he would receive a warning citation should his unlicensed pet be discovered during a department inspection. Thus, the ordinance was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the ordinance requiring appellant kennels to provide the name and address of animals being boarded to prevent rabies was upheld as constitutional because rabies prevention outweighed the privacy interest in owner's home address, the ordinance did not violate equal protection rights, and the ordinance was not impermissibly vague.

Stogner v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-001064-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


35 S.W.3d 831; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 89



August 18, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 23, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MUHLENBERG CIRCUIT COURT, HONORABLE DAVID H. JERNIGAN, JUDGE, ACTION NO. 99-CR-00019.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from Muhlenberg Circuit Court (Kentucky), which convicted appellant of criminal facilitation to the manufacture of methamphetamine and the status offense of being a persistent felony offender in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: While police officers were at appellant's house arresting her and another person for shoplifting, the officers noticed a smell of ether coming from the house and saw items that could be used in the manufacture of methamphetamine. A relative of appellant's allowed police to enter the house, and after discovering other items that could be used in methamphetamine manufacture officers obtained a search warrant. The trial court denied appellant's motion to suppress, and appellant entered a conditional guilty plea to charges of criminal facilitation to the manufacture of methamphetamine and being a persistent felony offender in the second degree. The court affirmed. The court rejected appellant's argument that the search and seizure of the drug evidence was unconstitutional because it was tainted by an illegal arrest. Appellant's arrest for theft was supported by probable cause and authorized under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 433.236(3). Furthermore, even if the arrest had been illegal, the seizure of the evidence was not unconstitutional because it was not a product of the arrest, but was otherwise based on items seen in plain view.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion to suppress. Probable cause supported appellant's arrest for theft and the seizure of evidence was constitutional as evidence was in plain view.

Stout v. Commonwealth


NO. 1998-CA-002456-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


44 S.W.3d 781; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 86



August 11, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Denied by the Supreme Court of Kentucky, June 7, 2001. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Ordered to be Published. Released for Publication June 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE SHEILA R. ISAAC, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 97-CR-00847.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a minor, challenged an order of the Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky) in a criminal action where appellant was transferred from juvenile to circuit court for disposition of felony and misdemeanor charges including, receiving stolen property, possession of a handgun by a minor, and resisting arrest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a minor, made a conditional plea of guilty to two felony and three misdemeanor charges, including receiving stolen property, possession of a handgun by a minor, and resisting arrest. Pursuant to his plea agreement he appealed his transfer from juvenile to circuit court and argued that the waiver was invalid because, the waiver statute was constitutionally infirm; he could not be waived on anything less than a clear and convincing standard of proof; the circuit court abused its discretion in finding that the transfer was appropriate; and the refusal to consider a psychological evaluation constituted reversible error. The court held that, while it was axiomatic that a juvenile offender had no constitutional right to be tried in juvenile court, the circuit court had the discretion to order the transfer of appellant as a youthful offender. Appellant's arguments that the circuit court had not articulated the standard of proof in making its transfer decision were unconvincing because the decision comported with traditional notions of due process. Meeting the standard of clear and convincing proof was not required. Any error related to the report was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment, which transferred appellant, a minor, from juvenile to circuit court as a youthful offender because the transfer statute was constitutionally sound, and the action was not an abuse of the court's discretion where the court's decision was based upon sufficient evidence.

Gray v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-002319-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


28 S.W.3d 316; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 81



July 28, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LAURENCE B. VAN METER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CR-000504.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from to Fayette Circuit Court (Kentucky), which after refusing to suppress evidence seized from defendant's automobile in a search conducted at an impoundment lot the day after her arrest, accepted defendant's conditional guilty plea to trafficking in a controlled substance first degree, with a firearm, possession of marijuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, and operating a motor vehicle under the influence.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals upheld a judgment accepting defendant's conditional guilty plea to trafficking in a controlled substance first degree, with a firearm, possession of marijuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, and operating a motor vehicle under the influence after refusing to suppress evidence seized from defendant's car in a search conducted at an impoundment lot the day after her arrest. The court held that it was not error to deny her motion to suppress. The court found there was substantial evidence supporting the determination that there was probable cause for a second search of her car. The court did not accept the characterization of the second search as an inventory search rather than as a second automobile probable cause search. The court held that the same probable cause that supported the first search of the car on the highway continued to exist and to support the second search at the impoundment lot. The court noted that when officers had probable cause to believe there was contraband inside an automobile that had been stopped on the road, the officers could conduct a warrantless search of the vehicle, even after it had been impounded and was in police custody.


OUTCOME: A judgment, which accepted defendant's conditional guilty plea various after refusing to suppress evidence seized from defendant's car in a search conducted at an impoundment lot the day after her arrest, was affirmed because the same probable cause that supported the first search of the car on the highway continued to exist and to support the second search, which was an automobile probable cause search at the impoundment lot.

PSC v. Jackson County Rural Elec. Coop., Inc.


NO. 1998-CA-002609-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


50 S.W.3d 764; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 78



July 14, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified July 21, 2000. Petition for Rehearing Denied September 9, 2000. Discretionary Review Denied August 15, 2001. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM FRANKLIN CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM L. GRAHAM, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 96-CI-01130.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Franklin Circuit Court (Kentucky) reversing and setting aside appellant's orders assessing penalties pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 278.990(1) against appellees for safety violations by their independent contractors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Public Service Commission challenged a judgment of the trial court reversing and setting aside appellant's orders assessing penalties against appellee utilities for safety violations by their independent contractors. The court reversed. The court held that Ky. Rev. Stat. On the basis of the above, the court concluded that appellant acted within its authority under § 278.990(1) in assessing the subject penalties.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment was reversed. Court concluded that statutory provision allowed appellant Public Service Commission to assess penalties against appellee utilities for safety violations committed by appellees' independent contractors.

Cornelison v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-001825-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 73



July 7, 2000, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM MADISON CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE WILLIAM JENNINGS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 99-CR-00053.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged judgment from the Madison Circuit Court (Kentucky) convicting and sentencing him of driving under the influence, in violation of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 189A.010.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the judgment of conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence (DUI), third offense, a Class D felony. Since the court agreed with the trial court's determination that the statute was constitutional, the court affirmed. Appellant argued that the DUI statute violated equal protection laws. There was nothing essentially unjust or unequal in establishing different classifications of multiple offenders based on their level of intoxication. Appellant also argued that the application of the amended statute to his third offense violated the ex post facto clause of the United States Constitution. Under the facts of this case, there clearly were no ex post facto implications. Lastly, appellant argued that the statute subjected him to cruel and unusual punishment. Applying a Solem analysis, the court soundly rejected any argument that the punishment he received was grossly disproportionate to the seriousness of his crime, or that the statute, violated the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment as to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Statute under which appellant was convicted of driving under the influence, and sentenced, did not violate equal protection, ex post facto, or cruel and unusual punishment clauses.

Marshall v. Commonwealth


NO. 1998-CA-003192-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


20 S.W.3d 478; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 62



June 2, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 7, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM GREENUP CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LEWIS D. NICHOLLS, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 1997-CI-00589.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff sought review of a declaratory judgment by the Greenup Circuit Court (Kentucky) that he had to pay account interest from deposits of school taxes he had collected to the school boards pursuant to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.140.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sheriff served as tax collector for school taxes within the county under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 134.140, 160.500, and was required monthly to pay the amount of school taxes collected to the depository of the district boards of education within the county under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 160.510. Section 134.140 permitted appellant to invest any tax revenues held in his possession, subject to Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 66.480. However, appellant had to pay to the board of education investment earnings attributable to school taxes. Appellant was permitted to withhold up to four percent of the investment earnings as a fee under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 134.140(3)(b). Prior to distributing the tax monies appellant deposited some funds into a NOW account and retained the NOW account interest for operating expenses. The public auditor complained. Appellant sought a declaration of rights. The trial court held the NOW account interest income had to be paid. The court affirmed because Ky. Const. § 184 required all income generated by school taxes go to the schools, even though NOW accounts were not considered investments by the banking industry nor listed as such under § 66.480.


OUTCOME: Declaratory judgment was affirmed because the state's constitutional requirement that all school tax income go to the schools included NOW account interest, even though the banking industry did not consider nor did the statutory scheme list NOW accounts as investments.

 

599 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Ky. Dep't of Corr. v. McCullough


NO. 1998-CA-001403-MR (Direct), NO. 1998-CA-001422-MR (Cross)


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 57



May 26, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
Petition for Rehearing Denied July 21, 2000.
Review granted by Kentucky Dep't of Corrections v. McCullough, 2001 Ky. LEXIS 37 (Ky., Feb. 14, 2001)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Ky. Dep't of Corr. v. McCullough, 2003 Ky. LEXIS 180 (Ky., Aug. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM BOYLE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE STEPHEN M. SHEWMAKER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 95-CI-00341.

CROSS-APPEAL FROM BOYLE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE STEPHEN M. SHEWMAKER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 95-CI-00341.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATEDNG IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed action in the Boyle Circuit Court (Kentucky) against defendants, the state department of corrections and warden, for gender discrimination and retaliation. The jury returned a verdict in favor of defendants on the claim of gender discrimination but in favor of plaintiff on the claim of retaliation. Defendants appealed from the judgment of the circuit court and its post-trial orders, and plaintiff cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a correctional officer, filed an action against defendants alleging gender discrimination and retaliation in contravention of Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. ch. 344. Plaintiff claimed she was denied promotion based upon her gender and in retaliation for an Equal Employment Opportunity complaint she had filed previously. On appeal and cross-appeals from a decision of the lower court in favor of defendants on the claim of gender discrimination and in favor of plaintiff on claim of retaliation, the court held that plaintiff's suit against defendant, the state department of corrections, was not barred by doctrine of sovereign immunity. Further, the court found that plaintiff established a prima facie case of retaliation, as there was sufficient evidence from which the jury could have reasonably inferred that defendants failed to promote plaintiff for retaliatory reasons. However, the court stated that it was wholly unclear as to how the lower court arrived at a figure for attorneys' fees; thus, the court vacated lower court's order awarding attorney's fees to plaintiff. Finally, the court held that plaintiff was permitted to seek punitive damages under ch. 344.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the order of the lower court as to attorneys' fees for more specific findings of fact, vacated the order of the lower court setting aside the jury's award of punitive damages against the state department of corrections, and held that plaintiff was entitled to an instruction on punitive damages against warden.

 

600 of 1068 DOCUMENTS


Lozier v. Commonwealth


NO. 1999-CA-001117-MR


COURT OF APPEALS OF KENTUCKY


32 S.W.3d 511; 2000 Ky. App. LEXIS 33



April 7, 2000, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 27, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM WOLFE CIRCUIT COURT. HONORABLE LARRY MILLER, JUDGE. ACTION NO. 1997-CR-00030.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction for sodomy in the Wolfe Circuit Court (Kentucky), alleging that Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 197.045(4), 532.043, which became effective after defendant committed her criminal act, constituted the improper application of ex post facto laws by increasing defendant's punishment and limiting defendant's ability to earn good time credit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sodomy and alleged that the prohibition against ex post facto laws was violated by the imposition of a term of conditional discharge under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 532.043 and by the conditioning of good time credit upon completion of the sexual offender treatment program under Ky. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 197.045(4). The court held that, although both statutes became effective after defendant committed her crime, only the conditional discharge statute constituted an ex post facto law. The term of conditional discharge potentially subjected defendant to a term of imprisonment greater than the maximum sentence applicable at the time of the offense and thus retroactively disadvantaged defendant. However, defendant was sentenced after the effective date of the statute deferring good time credit until after completion of the sex offender program, and thus defendant was not deprived of any previously earned credits, the opportunity to earn good time credits, or the opportunity to qualify for early parole.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed in part because defendant's ability to earn good time credit was only deferred by the retroactively applied statute, but reversed in part because the disadvantage to defendant from the application of the statute requiring a term of conditional discharge, thus potentially increasing defendant's punishment, constituted an ex post facto violation.
